Validity of Sa'i in the Current Mas'a
discussing whether the current sa'i area is valid after renovations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of sa'i in the current mas'a and explain the historical evidence supporting its validity.

Core Idea
Sa'i remains valid after renovations because the current area lies within the original wide mas'a.

This lesson examines a practical concern: after historical changes to the area between Safa and Marwa, is the sa'i still valid? The Hanafi school assures us that it is, as the current mas'a falls within the original boundaries. We will explore the reasoning behind this ruling and understand why later renovations do not invalidate the act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its requirement
Sa'i is an act of devotion that must be performed in the specific area between Safa and Marwa. The location is integral to its validity.
2
Recognize the historical changes
The original mas'a was wide. Over time, houses were built within its width. Later, al-Mahdi demolished some houses and incorporated part of the area into the Haram, but the remaining area includes the current mas'a.
3
Analyze the key argument for validity
The commentator argues that because the current mas'a is still within the original width, it is valid. The relocation was not complete; hence, the location remains legitimate.
4
Understand the implicit counter-argument
Some may think that any change invalidates sa'i, but the passage shows that only a complete relocation would be problematic, which did not occur.
5
Conclude the Hanafi ruling
Based on historical reports and the principle that scholars would have objected if it were invalid, the Hanafi ruling is that sa'i in the current mas'a is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو السعي بين الصفا والمروة من الأمور التعبدية في ذلك المكان المخصوص، وعلى ما ذكر الثقات أدخل ذلك المسعى في الحرم الشريف وحول ذلك المسعى إلى دار ابن عباد كما تقدم. والمكان الذي يسعى فيه الآن لا يتحقق أنه من عرض المسعى الذي سعى فيه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أو غيره، فكيف يصح السعي فيه وقد حول عن محله؟ ولعل الجواب أن المسعى كان عريضاً وبنيت تلك الدور بعد في عرض المسعى القديم فهدمها المهدي وأدخل بعضها في المسجد الحرام وترك البعض ولم يحول تحويلاً كلياً وإلا لأنكره علماء الدين من الأئمة المجتهدين ا.هـ. ملخصاً من المدني
And it is the sa'i between Safa and Marwa, which is an act of devotion in that specific place. According to reliable sources, that mas'a was included in the noble Haram and that mas'a was moved to Dar Ibn Abbad as previously mentioned. The place where sa'i is performed now cannot be verified to be within the width of the mas'a in which the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم performed sa'i or others. So how can sa'i be valid in it when it has been relocated from its original place? Perhaps the answer is that the mas'a was wide, and those houses were later built within the width of the old mas'a. Then al-Mahdi demolished them and included some in the Sacred Mosque and left some, and it was not completely relocated; otherwise, the scholars of religion from the mujtahid imams would have rejected it. End of summary from al-Madani.
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage addresses a concern about the validity of sa'i in the current location due to historical changes. The original sa'i area was between Safa and Marwa, a wide space. Over time, houses were built within that width, and later al-Mahdi (an Abbasid caliph) removed some of them and incorporated part into the Haram. The current sa'i area is within the original width, so it is still valid. The commentator reassures that the relocation was not total, and scholars would have objected if it were invalid.

Key Terms
مسعى (mas'a): The area between Safa and Marwa where sa'i is performed.
سعي (sa'i): Walking seven times between Safa and Marwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is sa'i in the current mas'a considered valid despite renovations?
A) The entire mas'a was rebuilt exactly as it was.
B) The current area falls within the original wide mas'a.
C) Scholars unanimously agreed it is valid.
D) The Prophet's sa'i was in a different location.

Key Takeaway
Sa'i in the current mas'a is valid because the area remains within the original boundaries, and no complete relocation occurred.

Ruling on Mutamatti' Performing Additional Umrah
Ruling on mutamatti' performing extra Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mutamatti' performing an extra Umrah and identify the penalty.

Core Idea
A mutamatti' must not perform an additional Umrah in Makkah; doing so incurs sin and a dam.

In the context of tamattu' Hajj, the pilgrim performs Umrah first and then Hajj. While staying in Makkah between these rites, a question arises whether he may perform another Umrah. The classical Hanafi texts address this, emphasizing the special status of the mutamatti' and the penalty for violating the prescribed order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What action is being ruled upon? It is the mutamatti' performing an Umrah during his stay in Makkah. The ruling is that he should not do so; if he does, he sins and must offer a dam.
The act is considered makruh tahrimi.
2
Understand the consequence
The consequence of performing an extra Umrah is that a dam (penalty sacrifice) becomes obligatory. This indicates the severity of the prohibition.
Dam is a sheep or goat, to be slaughtered in Makkah.
3
Scope of the ruling
Does the time matter? The text states that the sin and dam apply whether the extra Umrah is done in the months of Hajj or before them. So the ruling is general.
Months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah.
4
Intra-Hanafi difference
Some later Hanafis, as noted by the commentator, consider it permissible. However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position from the main texts like al-Lubab is that it is prohibited and requires a dam.
The difference stems from whether the mutamatti' is considered like a Makkan or not.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi position is that it is makruh tahrimi and a dam is due. This is based on the statement in al-Lubab and the comment of the commentator.
The commentator's apparent permissibility is not acted upon due to the explicit ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فأفاد أن فسخ الحج إلى العمرة لا يجوز أي بأن يفسخ نية الحج بعد ما أحرم به ويقطع إحرامه وأفعاله للعمرة، وكذا لا يجوز فسخ العمرة ليجعلها حجاً. كذا في اللباب قبيل الجنايات، وفيه : لا يعتمر أي المتمتع حال إقامته بمكة فإن فعل أساء ولزمه دم سواء كان في أشهر الحج أو قبلها، وإن كان لم يسق الهدي وأحل بعد الحلق يفعل كما يفعل الحلال . قال شارحه : والظاهر أنه يجوز له الإتيان بالعمرة حينئذ لأنه غير ممنوع منها لكراهتها في الأزمنة المخصوصة، وإنما كرهت العمرة للمكي في أشهر الحج لأن الغالب أنه يجح فيبقى متمتعاً مسيئاً
He said: (So it indicates that faskh of Hajj to Umrah is not allowed, i.e., that he changes the intention of Hajj after having entered ihram for it and cuts his ihram and its actions for Umrah. Similarly, it is not allowed to change Umrah to make it Hajj. As is in al-Lubab before the chapter on jinayat. And in it: The mutamatti' should not perform Umrah while he is staying in Makkah; if he does, he sins and a dam is due upon him, whether it is in the months of Hajj or before them. And if he did not bring the Hadi and exited ihram after shaving, he does as the halal does. The commentator said: Apparently, it is permissible for him to perform Umrah then because he is not prohibited from it due to its dislike in specific times. Rather, Umrah is disliked for the Makkan in the months of Hajj because usually he performs Hajj and remains as a mutamatti' sinning.)
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage returns to the topic of faskh, clarifying that changing Hajj to Umrah or vice versa is not allowed. Then it addresses the case of a mutamatti' (one who performs Umrah first and then Hajj) who is staying in Makkah: he should not perform another Umrah. If he does, he commits a sin and must offer a dam (penalty sacrifice) regardless of whether he does it in the months of Hajj or earlier. The commentator adds that it is permissible for him to perform Umrah then because he is not prohibited, but it is disliked for a Makkan to perform Umrah in the months of Hajj because it might lead to being a mutamatti' and sinning.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): A pilgrim who performs Umrah first and then Hajj in the same journey.
دم (dam): A penalty sacrifice (one sheep or goat) for omitting or doing a prohibited act in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mutamatti' performs an additional Umrah while staying in Makkah, what is the consequence?
A) No penalty, it is recommended.
B) He sins and must offer a dam.
C) His Hajj becomes invalid.
D) He must repeat the Umrah.

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' staying in Makkah must not perform an additional Umrah; doing so incurs sin and a dam penalty.

Khutbah before Yawm al-Tarwiyah and Definition of the Day
defining the days of Hajj and the khutbah before Yawm al-Tarwiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the pre-Hajj khutbah and explain the meaning and significance of Yawm al-Tarwiyah according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
The khutbah teaching Hajj rituals is delivered on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah after Zuhr, a day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah.

This lesson clarifies the recommended khutbah that precedes the Hajj rituals. It explains on which day and at what time this sermon is given, and also explores the meaning of Yawm al-Tarwiyah, the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. Understanding these details helps ensure that the sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ is followed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being described? The matn instructs to deliver a khutbah. In Hanafi fiqh, this khutbah is sunnah, not wajib. The commentary specifies it is a single khutbah after Zuhr on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah.
The phrase 'ثم اخطب' is an imperative, but Hanafi usul classifies such amr for recommended acts when there is evidence supporting sunnah.
2
Understand the timing and manner
The khutbah is delivered on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah (the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah) after Zuhr prayer. It is one khutbah with no sitting (i.e., no break between two parts). Its content should teach the rituals (manasik) of Hajj.
This differs from the Friday khutbah which has two parts with sitting in between.
3
Define Yawm al-Tarwiyah
Yawm al-Tarwiyah is the 8th day of Dhul Hijjah. The name comes either from people watering their camels (tarvīyah) for the journey to Arafah, or from the Prophet Ibrahim reflecting (tarvīyah) on his dream to sacrifice his son.
Both explanations are mentioned in the commentary; they are not mutually exclusive.
4
Recognize the significance for Hajj
This khutbah serves to educate pilgrims about the rites they will perform. It is part of the sunnah practices of the Hajj season.
Missing this khutbah does not invalidate Hajj, but following the sunnah is meritorious.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم اخطب قبل يوم التروية بيوم وعلم فيها المناسك) يعني في اليوم السابع من الحجة بعد صلاة الظهر خطبة واحدة لا جلوس فيها، ويوم التروية هو يوم الثامن سمي به لأن الناس يرون إبلهم فيه لأجل يوم عرفة، وقيل لأن إبراهيم عليه السلام رأى في تلك الليلة في منامه أن يذبح ولده بأمر ربه فلما أصبح روّى في النهار كله أي تفكر أن ما رآه
He said: (Then deliver a khutbah a day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah and teach therein the rituals.) Meaning on the seventh day of Dhul Hijjah after Zuhr prayer, one khutbah without sitting. Yawm al-Tarwiyah is the eighth day; it is named thus because people water their camels for the day of Arafah, or because Ibrahim عليه السلام saw in his dream that night that he would slaughter his son by his Lord's command, and when he morning came, he reflected (ruwwa) the entire day, i.e., thought about what he saw.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage explains the matn instructing the imam to deliver a khutbah on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, before Yawm al-Tarwiyah. The khutbah teaches the rituals of Hajj. It is a single khutbah after Zuhr with no sitting in between. The passage then defines Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah), giving two reasons for its name: either because people water their camels for the journey to Arafah, or because of the story of Ibrahim's dream where he reflected on the command to sacrifice his son. The definition of subsequent days (9th, 10th, etc.) is also implied but not fully stated in this extract.

Key Terms
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th day of Dhul Hijjah, named for watering camels or Ibrahim's reflection.
خطبة (khutbah): Sermon delivered on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah to teach Hajj rituals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which day and time is the khutbah teaching the rituals delivered?
A) On the 8th of Dhul Hijjah at Zuhr.
B) On the 7th of Dhul Hijjah after Zuhr.
C) On the 9th of Dhul Hijjah at Fajr.
D) On the 10th of Dhul Hijjah after Maghrib.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah khutbah teaching Hajj rites is delivered on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah after Zuhr, and Yawm al-Tarwiyah is the 8th day named after watering camels or Ibrahim's reflection.

The Shadhirwan and Woman's Tawaf: A Madhhab Dispute
Explains Hanafi and Shafi'i views on shadhirwan and woman's tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the shadhirwan and derive the recommended tawaf procedure for a woman, identifying the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The shadhirwan is not part of the Kaaba in the Hanafi school; a woman must tawaf behind it to ensure validity.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two intertwined issues: the recommended position for a woman performing tawaf, and the legal status of the shadhirwan, the sloping base around the Kaaba. The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools disagree on whether the shadhirwan is part of the Kaaba, leading to different rulings on the validity of tawaf upon it. Understanding this dispute is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi view in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
First, note the recommended position for a woman's tawaf: she should keep behind the shadhirwan. Second, note the underlying legal dispute: is the shadhirwan part of the Kaaba?
The passage links these two rulings.
2
State the Hanafi position on the shadhirwan
According to al-Kirmani, the Hanafi school holds that the shadhirwan is not part of the Kaaba. It was a later addition by Quraysh when they rebuilt and narrowed the structure.
This is based on historical evidence (athar).
3
State the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school considers the shadhirwan part of the original foundation of the Kaaba. Therefore, tawaf upon it would be valid, but they still recommend avoiding it.
The dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf in fiqh.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The Hanafi ruling: tawaf performed on the shadhirwan is invalid because it would be outside the Kaaba. The Shafi'i ruling: tawaf on the shadhirwan is valid but makruh (disliked) as a precaution.
This directly affects the validity of a woman's tawaf if she steps onto the shadhirwan.
5
Apply to the woman's tawaf recommendation
To avoid any part of her tawaf being on the shadhirwan, the Hanafi school recommends the woman keeps at the edge of the tawaf area, ensuring her entire circumambulation is behind the shadhirwan.
This is an act of caution (ihtiyat) even though the shadhirwan is not part of the Kaaba according to us.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأفضل للمرأة أن تكون في حاشية المطاف ويكون طوافه وراء الشاذروان كي لا يكون بعض طوافه بالبيت بناء على أنه منه وقال الكرماني : الشاذروان ليس عندنا من البيت، وعند الشافعي منه حتى لا يجوز الطواف عليه وهو تلك الزيادة الملصقة بالبيت من الحجر الأسود إلى فرجة الحجر، قيل بقي منه حين عمرته قريش وضيقته.
And the best for a woman is that she be at the edge of the circumambulation area and her circumambulation be behind the shadhirwan so that part of her tawaf is not upon the House based on it being from it. And al-Kirmani said: The shadhirwan is not from the House according to us, but according to al-Shafi'i it is from it, so tawaf upon it is not permissible. And it is that addition attached to the House from the Black Stone to the gap of the Hijr; it is said it remained from when Quraysh rebuilt it and narrowed it.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage addresses two related rulings: the recommended position for a woman performing tawaf, and the legal status of the shadhirwan (the sloping base around the Kaaba). The Hanafi school holds that the shadhirwan is not part of the Kaaba, based on the understanding that it was a later addition when Quraysh rebuilt the Kaaba. Therefore, tawaf performed on the shadhirwan is invalid as it would be outside the actual House. The Shafi'i school considers it part of the Kaaba, so tawaf on it is valid but not upon the wall itself. The woman is advised to keep her tawaf behind the shadhirwan to avoid any part of her tawaf being upon the shadhirwan, which according to the Shafi'i view would be upon the House but is avoided for caution. The commentator al-Kirmani clarifies the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الشاذروان (al-shadhirwan): The sloping base around the Kaaba, a built-up area attached to the wall

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it recommended for a woman to perform tawaf behind the shadhirwan?
A) Because the shadhirwan is part of the Kaaba and tawaf must be inside it
B) To avoid any part of her tawaf being on the shadhirwan, which would be invalid
C) Because the shadhirwan is too narrow for women
D) To follow the Shafi'i school's precaution

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds the shadhirwan is not part of the Kaaba, so tawaf must be performed behind it; the Shafi'i school differs, and the woman's recommended tawaf position reflects this caution.

Dhikr Preferred over Quran Recitation in Tawaf
Rules on the preference of dhikr over Quran in tawaf and the prohibition of loud recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that dhikr is superior to Quran recitation during tawaf and explain the ruling on raising one's voice with Quran in tawaf.

Core Idea
In tawaf, dhikr is better than Quran recitation; raising the voice with Quran is makruh.

Tawaf is an act of worship with specific etiquettes and preferences. The Hanafi school teaches that while both dhikr (remembrance of Allah) and Quran recitation are virtuous, dhikr takes precedence during tawaf. Additionally, raising one's voice with Quran recitation is disliked (makruh), though silent recitation is permissible. This lesson unpacks these rulings and their rationale, drawing from classical Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary act and its ruling
The passage discusses two supererogatory acts during tawaf: dhikr and Quran recitation. Determine which is preferred according to the Hanafi school. The first source cited is al-Tanjis, which states that dhikr is better.
Dhikr includes phrases like Subhanallah, Alhamdulillah, Allahu Akbar.
2
Identify the secondary ruling on voice
The passage also rules on the manner of Quran recitation during tawaf: raising voice vs. silent. Identify the hukm (makruh) and its basis. Fath al-Qadir, quoting Kafi al-Hakim, states it is makruh to raise one's voice but no harm in silent recitation.
This ruling applies to Quran recitation; dhikr may be recited aloud softly.
3
Understand the rationale
Consider why dhikr is preferred and loud Quran is disliked. Tawaf resembles prayer (salah) in its requirement of focus and humility; loud recitation can disturb oneself and others. The commentary hints that tawaf is akin to salah in this regard.
Other schools may differ; this is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التنجيس : الذكر أفضل من القراءة في الطواف وفي فتح القدير معزياً لكافي الحاكم : يكره أن يرفع صوته بالقراءة فيه ولا بأس بقراءته في نفسه.
And in al-Tanjis: Dhikr is better than recitation in tawaf. And in Fath al-Qadir, attributed to Kafi al-Hakim: It is disliked to raise one's voice with recitation in it, and there is no harm in reciting it to oneself.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding the recommended supererogatory acts during tawaf. The author cites two sources: al-Tanjis states that dhikr (remembrance of Allah) is superior to reciting the Quran during tawaf. Fath al-Qadir, quoting Kafi al-Hakim, adds that raising one's voice in Quran recitation during tawaf is makruh (disliked), but reciting silently to oneself is permissible. This is based on the principle that tawaf is akin to prayer in its focus, and loud recitation may disturb others.

Key Terms
ذكر (dhikr): Remembrance of Allah, typically by repeating phrases like Subhanallah, Alhamdulillah, Allahu Akbar.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba seven times, an essential ritual of Hajj and Umrah.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an act whose avoidance is rewarded but committing it is not sinful (makruh tanzihi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on raising one's voice with Quran recitation during tawaf?
A) Recommended
B) Permissible
C) Disliked (makruh)
D) Forbidden

Key Takeaway
During tawaf, dhikr is better than Quran recitation, and raising the voice with Quran is makruh.

Entering the Kaaba: Ruling and Etiquettes
Ruling on entering the Kaaba and etiquettes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on entering the Kaaba, identify its condition, and list the recommended actions and etiquettes as derived from the Hanafi text.

Core Idea
Entering the Kaaba is recommended only when it causes no harm; the Prophet's practice includes prayer, adab, and dhikr at the corners.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that entering the Kaaba is a recommend act (mustahabb) but conditional on not harming anyone, a condition often unmet due to crowding. The commentator then details the prophetic practice and the example of Ibn 'Umar, emphasizing outward and inward etiquette.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Read the first part of the passage to determine the hukm (mustahabb) and the condition that restricts it (no harm to oneself or others). Note the commentator's observation about the rarity of fulfilling this condition.
The ruling is conditional, not absolute.
2
List the recommended actions
Extract the specific actions mentioned: praying in the Prophet's spot, positioning like Ibn 'Umar (door behind back, three cubits from wall), maintaining adab (not raising gaze), placing cheek on wall, seeking forgiveness, praising, and doing dhikr at the corners.
These are sunan (recommended practices).
3
Understand the concept of adab
The passage says 'yalzim al-adab' – adhering to etiquette outwardly and inwardly. Identify the specific examples: not raising sight to ceiling, placing cheek, and humble supplication.
Adab combines physical actions with inner state.
4
Recognize the practical limitation
The commentator notes that the condition 'no harm' is rarely met in his time. Consider why this would be the case (overcrowding) and how it applies today.
This reflects the Hanafi sensitivity to actual conditions.
5
Apply to modern context
Think about how a pilgrim should decide whether to enter the Kaaba today, balancing the desire for reward with the condition of no harm.
If entry causes discomfort or risk, it is not recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف دخول البيت وهو مستحب إذا لم يؤذ أحداً كذا قالوا يعني لا نفسه ولا غيره وقليل أن يوجد هذا الشرط في زمن كما شاهدناه. ويستحب أن يصلي فيه اقتداء به عليه السلام وينبغي أن يقصد مصلاه عليه السلام وكان ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما إذا دخل مشى قبل وجهه ويجعل الباب قبل ظهره حتى يكون بينه وبين الجدار الذي قبل وجهه قريب من ثلاثة أذرع . ثم يصلي ويلزم الأدب ما استطاع بظاهره وباطنه ولا يرفع بصره إلى السقف، فإذا صلى إلى الجدار يضع خده عليه ويستغفر ويحمد ثم يأتي الأركان فيحمد ويهلل ويسبح ويكبر ويسأل الله تعالى ما شاء.
And the author did not mention entering the House, and it is recommended if one does not harm anyone, thus they said: meaning neither himself nor others, and it is rare to find this condition in our time as we have witnessed. And it is recommended to pray in it following him (peace be upon him), and one should intend his prayer place (peace be upon him). And Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) when he entered, he walked forward and placed the door behind his back until between him and the wall in front of him was about three cubits. Then he prayed, and he adhered to etiquette as much as possible outwardly and inwardly, and he did not raise his sight to the ceiling. When he prayed facing the wall, he placed his cheek on it, sought forgiveness, praised, then came to the corners, praised, said la ilaha illa Allah, glorified, said takbir, and asked Allah Almighty for whatever he wished.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage explains that entering the Kaaba is a recommended (mustahabb) act, but conditional on not causing harm to oneself or others. The commentator observes that this condition is rarely met in their time due to crowding. The recommended actions upon entry include: praying two rak'ahs emulating the Prophet ﷺ, specifically in the place where he prayed; following the method of Ibn 'Umar who would position himself with the door behind his back and three cubits away from the front wall; maintaining full adab (etiquette) outwardly and inwardly; avoiding raising the gaze to the ceiling; after prayer, placing the cheek on the wall, seeking forgiveness, praising, and then doing dhikr at the corners.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an act whose performance is rewarded and omission is not sinful
الأدب (al-adab): Etiquette and proper conduct, encompassing outward actions and inner state

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Hajj Sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah
Describes the khutbah on 7th Dhul Hijjah and defines Hajj days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the timing and form of the Hajj sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, define Yawm al-Tarwiyah, and distinguish the opening of Hajj sermons from other sermons.

Core Idea
The 7th sermon is one after Dhuhr, beginning with takbir, talbiyah, then tahmid.

This lesson unpacks the matn's instruction to deliver a sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that it is a single sermon after Dhuhr, teaches the Hajj rituals, and explains the meaning of Yawm al-Tarwiyah. Understanding these details ensures correct performance of this sunnah act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delivering a sermon (khutbah) on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah. According to the Hanafi school, it is a sunnah (recommended) act, not obligatory.
The matn says 'then deliver a sermon' indicating it is part of the Hajj practices.
2
Analyze the timing and form
The sermon is delivered after Dhuhr on the 7th. It is one sermon without a sitting between its parts, unlike Friday sermons which are two with a sitting.
The commentary emphasizes 'one sermon' and 'no sitting'.
3
Define Yawm al-Tarwiyah
Yawm al-Tarwiyah is the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. The name has two origins: from watering camels (ri) for Arafah, or from Ibrahim's reflection (tawriyah) on the dream of sacrifice.
The text mentions both explanations; both are accepted.
4
List the rituals taught
The sermon teaches the manasik: going out to Mina, to Arafah, prayer therein, standing (wuquf), and ifadah (returning from Arafah).
These are core Hajj rituals.
5
Contrast the sermon's opening with other sermons
Hajj sermons (three total) begin with takbir, then talbiyah, then tahmid. In contrast, Friday, rain prayer, and marriage sermons begin with tahmid directly.
This distinction is important for proper performance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم اخطب قبل يوم التروية بيوم وعلم فيها المناسك) يعني في اليوم السابع من الحجة بعد صلاة الظهر خطبة واحدة لا جلوس فيها، ويوم التروية هو يوم الثامن سمي به لأن الناس يرون إبلهم فيه لأجل يوم عرفة، وقيل لأن إبراهيم عليه السلام رأى في تلك الليلة في منامه أن يذبح ولده بأمر ربه فلما أصبح روّى في النهار كله أي تفكر أن ما رآه من الله تعالى فيأتمره أو لا .فلا وظاهر كلام المغرب تعينه فإنه قال : والأصل الهمزة وأخذها ومن الري منظور فيه وأراد بالمناسك الخروج إلى منى وإلى عرفة والصلاة فيها والوقوف والإفاضة وهذه أول الخطب الثلاث التي في الحج ويبدأ في الكل بالتكبير ثم بالتلبية ثم بالتحميد كابتدائه في خطبة العيدين ويبدأ بالتحميد في ثلاث خطب وهي خطبة الجمع والاستسقاء والنكاح. كذا في المبتغى
His saying: (Then deliver a sermon one day before the day of tarwiyah and teach therein the rituals) means on the seventh of Dhul Hijjah after the Dhuhr prayer, one sermon without sitting in it. And the day of tarwiyah is the eighth; it is named because people water their camels therein for the day of Arafah. And it is said because Ibrahim (peace be upon him) saw in that night in his dream that he was to sacrifice his son by the command of his Lord; when morning came, he reflected (rawwa) the whole day, i.e., pondered whether what he saw was from Allah and he would follow it or not. And the apparent meaning of al-Mughrib is that it is determined; for he said: The root is the hamza and its derivation, and from 'ray' it is considered. And he meant by the rituals: going out to Mina and to Arafah, prayer therein, standing, and ifadah. And this is the first of the three sermons of Hajj, and he begins all with takbir, then talbiyah, then tahmid, as in the beginning of the Eid sermons. And he begins with tahmid in three sermons: the Friday sermon, the rain prayer sermon, and the marriage sermon. Thus in al-Mubtagha.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage explains the matn's instruction to deliver a sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, one day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah (the 8th). The sermon is one (not two), delivered after Dhuhr, and there is no sitting between parts. The speaker teaches the Hajj rituals (manasik). The names of the days are defined: Yawm al-Tarwiyah is the 8th, deriving from irrigation (ri) as people water their camels for Arafah, or from Ibrahim's reflection (tawriyah). This is the first of three Hajj sermons; they begin with takbir, talbiyah, then tahmid, except Friday, rain, and marriage sermons which begin with tahmid.

Key Terms
التروية (al-tarwiyah): The eighth day of Dhul Hijjah; named from watering camels or from reflection
المناسك (al-manasik): The rituals of Hajj, including going to Mina, Arafah, prayer, standing, and ifadah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 7th Dhul Hijjah
B) 8th Dhul Hijjah
C) 9th Dhul Hijjah
D) 10th Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
The Hajj sermon on the 7th is one sermon after Dhuhr, teaching rituals, and begins with takbir, talbiyah, then tahmid.

Departure to Mina on Yawm al-Tarwiyah
Ruling on going to Mina on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and recommended time for leaving Mecca to Mina on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah and identify the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Departure to Mina on Yawm al-Tarwiyah is sunnah; the best time is after sunrise, but any time is valid.

The pilgrimage to Mecca involves specific rites on specific days. One of these is the departure from Mecca to Mina on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah). This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling and recommended timing of this departure, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under discussion
The act is departure from Mecca to Mina on Yawm al-Tarwiyah, the 8th of Dhul Hijjah.
2
Determine the general ruling
The ruling is that it is permissible to go to Mina at any time on that day.
The text says 'Aṭlaqah' meaning absolute permission.
3
Find the recommended (mustahabb/sunnah) time
The strongest opinion is that the recommended time is after sunrise, based on the Prophet's practice.
There are three opinions; the soundest is after sunrise.
4
Understand the consequences of delay
If one does not leave until the day of Arafah, the hajj is valid but one has abandoned the sunnah and is blameworthy.
5
Note special Friday rule
If Yawm al-Tarwiyah falls on Friday, one may leave before zawal; after zawal, one must pray Jumu'ah first.
Compare with the rule for traveling on Friday from one's town.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم رح يوم التروية إلى منى) وهي قرية فيها ثلاث سكك بينها وبين مكة فرسخ وهي من الحرم والغالب عليه التذكير والصرف وقد يكتب بالألف كذا في المغرب. أطلقه فأفاد أنه يجوز التوجه إليها في أي وقت شاء من اليوم. واختلف في المستحب على ثلاثة أقوال أصحها أنه يخرج إليها بعد ما طلعت الشمس لما ثبت من فعله عليه السلام كذلك في حديث جابر الطويل وابن عمر مع اتفاق الرواة أنه صلى الظهر بمنى، والبيتوتة بها سنة والإقامة بها مندوبة كذا في المحيط. ولو لم يخرج من يوم عرفة أجزأه أيضاً ولكنه أساء لترك السنة، وأفاد أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون يوم التروية يوم الجمعة أو لا فله الخروج إليها يوم الجمعة قبل الزوال وأما بعده فلا يخرج ما لم يصلها كما إذا أراد أن يسافر يوم الجمعة من مصره. وينبغي أن يترك التلبية في الأحوال كلها حال الإقامة بمكة داخل المسجد الحرام وخارجه إلى حال كونه في الطواف ويلبي عند الخروج إلى منى ويدعو بما شاء، ويستحب أن ينزل بالقرب من مسجد الخيف
His saying: (Then depart on the day of tarwiyah to Mina) and it is a village with three streets; between it and Mecca is one farsakh; it is part of the Haram; it is predominantly masculine and diptote, and it may be written with an alif. Thus in al-Mughrib. He made it absolute, so it indicates that it is permissible to go to it at any time of the day. And there is disagreement on the recommended (mustahabb) with three opinions, the soundest of which is that one leaves after sunrise due to the confirmed action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as in the long hadith of Jabir and Ibn 'Umar, with the agreement of narrators that he prayed Dhuhr at Mina. And spending the night there is sunnah, and staying there is mandub, as in al-Muhit. Even if one does not leave until the day of Arafah, it is still sufficient, but he is at fault for abandoning the sunnah. And it indicates there is no difference whether the day of tarwiyah is Friday or not; one may leave on Friday before zawal (declination), but after it he should not leave without having prayed it, just as if he intended to travel on Friday from his town. And he should leave the talbiyah in all states while residing in Mecca, inside and outside the Sacred Mosque, until he is in tawaf; he should recite talbiyah when leaving for Mina, and supplicate as he wishes. And it is recommended to stay near the Masjid al-Khayf.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of going to Mina on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah). It describes Mina as a village within the Haram one farsakh from Mecca. The matn uses an absolute command, so it is permissible to go at any time. The recommended (mustahabb) time is after sunrise, based on the Prophet's practice as recorded in authentic hadith. Spending the night at Mina is sunnah, and staying there is mandub. Delaying departure until the day of Arafah is valid but entails leaving a sunnah. If the 8th falls on Friday, one may leave before zawal; after zawal, one must pray Jumu'ah first, like other travel restrictions. Talbiyah should be left off while residing in Mecca, even in the mosque, until tawaf; talbiyah is resumed when leaving for Mina. It is recommended to stay near Masjid al-Khayf.

Key Terms
البيتوتة (al-baytutah): Spending the night; here at Mina

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on leaving for Mina on Yawm al-Tarwiyah?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Mubah
D) Mandub

Key Takeaway
Departure to Mina on the 8th is a sunnah, best done after sunrise, but any time on that day is permissible.

Timing for Going to Arafat
Preferred time to go to Arafat and permission to go before sunrise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred time for going to Arafat and identify whether going earlier is permissible.

Core Idea
Going to Arafat after sunrise is best; before sunrise is permissible.

In this lesson, we examine the recommended timing for heading to Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. The classical Hanafi texts clarify that while it is best to go after sunrise, going earlier—even before Fajr—is entirely valid. This distinction between afdal (best) and ja'iz (permissible) is crucial for understanding the flexibility in hajj rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is going to Arafat on the day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah). The ruling is sunnah (preferred) but not obligatory at a specific time.
The act is part of the hajj rituals, but the timing is flexible.
2
Determine the best time (afdal)
According to the commentators, the best time is after sunrise (or after Fajr prayer, depending on interpretation).
Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir and others prefer after sunrise.
3
Note the permissibility of going earlier
Going before Fajr is permissible (ja'iz) and valid. There is no sin or requirement to repeat.
The matn of al-Hidayah states: 'if he goes before it, it is permissible because no ruling is attached to this place.'
4
Understand the difference between afdal and ja'iz
Afdal indicates the superior action; ja'iz indicates that the action is allowed and valid even if not optimal.
This distinction is important for fatwa: the mufta bihi is that after sunrise is better, but earlier is fine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم إلى عرفات بعد وهي علم للموقف وهي منونة لا غير ويقال لها عرفة أيضاً، ويوم عرفة التاسع من ذي الحجة وسمي به لأن إبراهيم عليه السلام عرف أن الحكم من الله فيه أو لأن جبريل عرفه المناسك فيه أو لأن آدم وحواء تعارفا فيه بعد الهبوط إلى الأرض وهذا بيان الأفضل حتى لو ذهب قبل طلوع الفجر إليها جاز كما يفعله الحجاج في زماننا فإن أكثرهم لا صلاة الفجر يوم عرفة) قوله: (وهذا بيان (الأفضل) عبارة :الهداية : ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات فيقيم بها، وهذا بيان الأولوية، أما لو دفع قبله جاز لأنه لا يتعلق بهذا المكان حكم. قال في غاية البيان: قوله «وهذا بيان الأولوية قال الإمام حميد الدين الضرير وغيره في شروحهم : أي الذهاب إلى عرفة بعد طلوع الشمس هو الأولى، ولو دفع قبله جاز . قلت : هذا حسن ولكن بقي في كلام صاحب الهداية شيء لأنه كان من الواجب أن يقيد بطلوع الشمس عند قوله «ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات» بأن يقول : ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات بعد طلوع الشمس حتى يصح بناء قوله وهذا بيان «الأولوية وكان هذا القيد ترك لسهو الكاتب، ولهذا صرح به في شرح الطحاوي وشرح الكرخي والإيضاح وغيرها ا هـ. ومثله في العناية. وأجاب في الحواشي السعدية بما في الغاية من إرجاع الإشارة إلى التوجه بعرفات بعد صلاة الفجر، أما لو توجه إليها قبلها جاز لكن لا يخفى أنها حينئذ توهم أن التوجه قبل الشمس كعبارة المتن هنا تأمل. هذا وفي مناسك الإمام النووي : وأما ما يفعله الناس في هذه الأزمان من دخولهم
His saying: (Then to Arafat afterwards) and it is a sign for the standing place, and it is diptote only, and it is also called 'Arafah. And the day of Arafah is the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; it is named because Ibrahim (peace be upon him) came to know (arafa) that the command was from Allah therein, or because Jibril taught him the rituals therein, or because Adam and Hawwa' recognized each other (ta'arafa) therein after descending to earth. And this is a statement of the best (afdal), even if he went before dawn it would be permissible, as the pilgrims do in our time, for most of them do not pray Fajr on the day of Arafah. His saying: (And this is a statement of the best) the expression of al-Hidayah: Then he goes to Arafat and stays there, and this is a statement of priority (awlawiyyah). But if he goes before it, it is permissible because no ruling is attached to this place. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: The wording 'and this is a statement of priority' – Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir and others in their commentaries said: meaning going to Arafah after sunrise is better, and if he goes before it, it is permissible. I said: This is good, but there remains something in the statement of the author of al-Hidayah because he should have qualified with sunrise at his words 'then goes to Arafat' by saying: then goes to Arafat after sunrise so that his statement 'and this is a statement of priority' would be correct, and this qualification was omitted due to oversight of the scribe. For this reason, it is explicitly stated in Sharh al-Tahawi, Sharh al-Karkhi, al-Idah, and others. The same is in al-Inayah. And al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyah responded by referring back to Ghayah that the indication is to going to Arafat after Fajr prayer; but if one goes before it, it is permissible. However, it is not hidden that then it suggests that going before sunrise is like the expression of the matn here – ponder. This, and in Manasik of Imam al-Nawawi: As for what people do in these times of entering...
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage discusses the timing for going to Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. The matn says 'then to Arafat after', and the commentator explains that 'afdal' refers to the best time. The best (afdal) is to go after sunrise, but it is permissible to go before dawn (Fajr), as many pilgrims do. Al-Hidayah's wording 'then goes to Arafat' is interpreted as priority (awlawiyyah), not obligation. A critical note points out that al-Hidayah omitted the qualification 'after sunrise', which was added in other commentaries. The preferred view is that going after Fajr prayer is better, but before Fajr is also valid. The text concludes with a reference to people's practice in later times, though the sentence is incomplete.

Key Terms
الأفضل (al-afdal): The best or preferred time; here for heading to Arafat
الأولوية (al-awlawiyyah): Priority; the recommended action that is superior but not obligatory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a pilgrim goes to Arafat before Fajr on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah?
A) Invalid, must repeat
B) Permissible but not the best
C) Forbidden
D) Only for those who cannot walk

Key Takeaway
Going to Arafat before Fajr is permissible, but the preferred time is after sunrise.

The Day of Tarwiyah: Departure to Mina and the First Khutbah
Explains the day of Tarwiyah rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for departing to Mina on the day of Tarwiyah, explain the structure of the first Hajj khutbah, and identify the sunnah acts for that day.

Core Idea
Departure to Mina on the 8th is sunnah, not fard; the best time is after sunrise, based on the Prophet’s practice.

The day of Tarwiyah marks the formal start of Hajj rites. On this day, the first of three special khutbahs is delivered, teaching the pilgrims the manasik. The matn then addresses the departure to Mina, a small village within the Haram boundaries. This lesson unpacks the ruling on when to leave, the recommended actions, and the structure of the khutbah, all grounded in the Hanafi school’s reliance on the sunnah of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
What is the ruling on departing to Mina on the day of Tarwiyah? The matn says it is permissible anytime, but the recommended time is after sunrise. This is a sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard or wajib.
The unrestricted wording allows flexibility; the sunnah is derived from hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites the long hadith of Jabir and the action of Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) departed after sunrise and prayed Zuhr at Mina. This serves as the proof for recommending after sunrise.
The dalil is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling is at the level of sunnah, not obligation.
3
Understand the khutbah structure
The first Hajj khutbah begins with takbir, then talbiyah, then tahmid – distinct from Eid khutbah (only takbir) and other khutbahs (Friday, rain, marriage) which begin with tahmid directly.
This is a unique formula for the three Hajj khutbahs (Tarwiyah, Arafah, and the day after Nahr?).
4
Apply the Friday rule
If the day of Tarwiyah falls on Friday, one may depart before zawal. After zawal, he must pray Jumuah first before leaving, analogous to the rule for travel on Friday from one's city.
This is because Jumuah becomes obligatory once zawal passes.
5
Note the sunnah acts and consequences
Staying overnight at Mina (baytutah) is sunnah. If one delays departure until the day of Arafah, the Hajj is valid but he is blameworthy for abandoning a sunnah. Also, talbiyah is stopped during tawaf in Makkah and resumed when leaving for Mina.
The commentator stresses that baytutah at Mina is a sunnah for the night of Tarwiyah, not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الإحرام التروية بيوم وعلم فيها المناسك ثم رح يوم التروية إلى منى ثم إلى عرفات بعد. وأراد بالمناسك الخروج إلى منى وإلى عرفة والصلاة فيها والوقوف والإفاضة وهذه أول الخطب الثلاث التي في الحج ويبدأ في الكل بالتكبير ثم بالتلبية ثم بالتحميد كابتدائه في خطبة العيدين ويبدأ بالتحميد في ثلاث خطب وهي خطبة الجمع والاستسقاء والنكاح. كذا في المبتغى. قوله: (ثم رح يوم التروية إلى منى) وهي قرية فيها ثلاث سكك بينها وبين مكة فرسخ وهي من الحرم والغالب عليه التذكير والصرف وقد يكتب بالألف. أطلقه فأفاد أنه يجوز التوجه إليها في أي وقت شاء من اليوم. واختلف في المستحب على ثلاثة أقوال أصحها أنه يخرج إليها بعد ما طلعت الشمس لما ثبت من فعله عليه السلام كذلك في حديث جابر الطويل وابن عمر مع اتفاق الرواة أنه صلى الظهر بمنى، والبيتوتة بها سنة والإقامة بها مندوبة. ولو لم يخرج من يوم عرفة أجزأه أيضاً ولكنه أساء لترك السنة. وأفاد أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون يوم التروية يوم الجمعة أو لا فله الخروج إليها يوم الجمعة قبل الزوال وأما بعده فلا يخرج ما لم يصلها كما إذا أراد أن يسافر يوم الجمعة من مصره. وينبغي أن يترك التلبية في الأحوال كلها حال الإقامة بمكة داخل المسجد الحرام وخارجه إلى حال كونه في الطواف ويلبي عند الخروج إلى منى ويدعو بما شاء، ويستحب أن ينزل بالقرب من مسجد الخيف.
The Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: The day of Tarwiyah, and he taught the rites therein, then he departed on the day of Tarwiyah to Mina, then to Arafat afterwards. He intended by 'rites' the departure to Mina and to Arafah, prayer there, standing, and ifadah. This is the first of the three khutbahs of Hajj, and he begins all with takbir, then talbiyah, then tahmid, like his beginning in the Eid khutbah. He begins with tahmid in three khutbahs: the Friday, rain prayer, and marriage khutbah. So in al-Mubtagha. His statement: 'Then depart on the day of Tarwiyah to Mina' — it is a village with three streets between it and Makkah, one farsakh away, and it is part of the Haram. The predominant is masculine and declinable, and it is sometimes written with alif. He left it unrestricted, indicating that it is permissible to go there at any time of the day. There is a difference of opinion on what is recommended, with three views, the most sound being that he goes there after sunrise, as established by his action, similarly in the long hadith of Jabir and Ibn Umar, with the narrators agreeing that he prayed Zuhr at Mina. Spending the night there is a sunnah, and staying there is recommended, as in al-Muhit. If he did not go until the day of Arafah, it is also acceptable, but he is blameworthy for abandoning the sunnah. He indicated that there is no difference whether the day of Tarwiyah is Friday or not, so he may go on Friday before zawal, but after zawal he should not go until he has prayed, just as if he wanted to travel on Friday from his city. He should refrain from talbiyah in all situations while staying in Makkah, inside the Masjid al-Haram and outside, until he is in tawaf, and he recites talbiyah when leaving for Mina and makes any du'a he wishes. It is recommended to stay near the Masjid al-Khayf.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul Hijjah). The author first explains the matn: on the day of Tarwiyah, the pilgrim should be taught the rites (manasik). This teaching occurs in the first of three khutbahs of Hajj. Unlike the Eid khutbah which begins with takbir, the Hajj khutbahs begin with takbir, then talbiyah, then tahmid. Other khutbahs (Friday, rain, marriage) begin with tahmid directly. The matn then says 'then depart on the day of Tarwiyah to Mina'. The commentator explains that Mina is a village one farsakh from Makkah and part of the Haram. The matn is unrestricted, so it is permissible to go anytime. However, the preferred time is after sunrise, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported in the long hadith of Jabir and the action of Ibn Umar. Staying overnight (baytutah) at Mina is a sunnah, and staying there longer is mandub. If someone does not go until the day of Arafah, it is still valid but he is blameworthy for abandoning a sunnah. The rule about Friday is clarified: if the day of Tarwiyah is Friday, one may go before zawal; after zawal, one must not go until after praying Jumuah, similar to traveling on Friday. The author also mentions that during stay in Makkah, one should stop talbiyah when in tawaf, and resume when leaving for Mina. It is recommended to stay near Masjid al-Khayf.

Key Terms
التروية (al-tarwiyah): The day before the day of Arafah (8th of Dhul Hijjah); traditionally the day when pilgrims water their animals and prepare for Hajj.
المناسك (al-manasik): The rites of Hajj, specifically the acts from ihram to completion, including going to Mina, Arafah, Muzdalifah, etc.
البيتوتة (al-baytutah): Spending the night (at Mina during the nights of Hajj).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the most recommended time to depart for Mina on the day of Tarwiyah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Before dawn
B) After sunrise
C) After Zuhr
D) Anytime is equally recommended

Key Takeaway
Departure to Mina on the 8th is a sunnah mu'akkadah, best performed after sunrise; missing it does not invalidate Hajj but is blameworthy.

Timing of Departure to Arafat and the Error of Entering on the 8th
Discusses the preferred time for going to Arafat and rebuts the practice of going on the 8th

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the best time to go to Arafat on the day of Arafah and identify why entering on the 8th is a blameworthy practice that misses sunnan.

Core Idea
The sunnah is to go to Arafat after Fajr on the 9th; entering on the 8th forfeits many sunan.

This passage clarifies the preferred timing for proceeding to Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet, holds that going after Fajr (or after sunrise) is best, while going earlier is merely permissible. The commentator strongly criticizes the common practice of entering Arafat on the 8th, citing Imam al-Nawawi's condemnation of this innovation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the best time to go to Arafat
Identify that the relied-upon view is to go after Fajr on the 9th, though some say after sunrise. The key is that departing before Fajr is permissible but not optimal.
2
Identify the opposing practice being criticized
The text describes people entering Arafat on the 8th (day of Tarwiyah), claiming convenience or fear of thieves.
3
Explain why this practice is rejected
Al-Nawawi lists missing many sunan: the prayers and stay at Mina, proceeding from Mina to Namirah, the khutbah at Namirah, and entering Arafat after zawal.
4
Note the Hanafi response to the justification
The Hanafi response is that the sunnah is clearly established; fear of thieves does not override it, and the practice of the Prophet is the model.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Those who go on the 8th abandon multiple recommended acts (sunan) and engage in a practice contrary to the sunnah, which is blameworthy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم إلى عرفات بعد) وهي علم للموقف وهي منونة لا غير ويقال لها عرفة أيضاً، ويوم عرفة التاسع من ذي الحجة وسمي به لأن إبراهيم عليه السلام عرف أن الحكم من الله فيه أو لأن جبريل عرفه المناسك فيه أو لأن آدم وحواء تعارفا فيه بعد الهبوط إلى الأرض وهذا بيان الأفضل حتى لو ذهب قبل طلوع الفجر إليها جاز كما يفعله الحجاج في زماننا فإن أكثرهم لا يبيت بمنى لتوهم الضرر من السراق. ويستحب أن يسير على طريق ضب ويعود على طريق المأزمين اقتداء بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كما في العيدين وينزل مع الناس حيث شاء وبقرب الجبل أفضل والبعد عن الناس في هذا المكان تجبر والحال حال تضرع ومسكنة أو اضرار بنفسه أو متاعه أو تضيق على المارة إن كان بالطريق والسنة أن ينزل الإمام بنمرة وتزول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بها لا نزاع فيه. كذا في فتح القدير. قوله: (وهذا بيان الأفضل) عبارة الهداية: ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات فيقيم بها، وهذا بيان الأولوية، أما لو دفع قبله جاز لأنه لا يتعلق بهذا المكان حكم. قال في غاية البيان: قوله «وهذا بيان الأولوية قال الإمام حميد الدين الضرير وغيره في شروحهم : أي الذهاب إلى عرفة بعد طلوع الشمس هو الأولى، ولو دفع قبله جاز . قلت : هذا حسن ولكن بقي في كلام صاحب الهداية شيء لأنه كان من الواجب أن يقيد بطلوع الشمس عند قوله «ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات» بأن يقول : ثم يتوجه إلى عرفات بعد طلوع الشمس حتى يصح بناء قوله وهذا بيان «الأولوية وكان هذا القيد ترك لسهو الكاتب، ولهذا صرح به في شرح الطحاوي وشرح الكرخي والإيضاح وغيرها ا هـ. ومثله في العناية. وأجاب في الحواشي السعدية بما في الغاية من إرجاع الإشارة إلى التوجه بعرفات بعد صلاة الفجر، أما لو توجه إليها قبلها جاز لكن لا يخفى أنها حينئذ توهم أن التوجه قبل الشمس كعبارة المتن هنا تأمل. هذا وفي مناسك الإمام النووي : وأما ما يفعله الناس في هذه الأزمان من دخولهم أرض عرفات في اليوم الثامن فخطأ مخالف للسنة ويفوتهم بسببه سنن كثيرة، ومنها الصلوات بمنى والمبيت بها والتوجه منها إلى نمرة والنزول بها والخطبة والصلاة قبل دخول عرفات وغير ذلك، فالسنة أن يمكثوا بنمرة حتى تزول الشمس ويغتسلوا بها للوقوف فإذا زالت الشمس ذهب الإمام والناس إلى المسجد المسمى مسجد إبراهيم ويخطب الإمام قبل صلاة الظهر خطبتين الخ
His statement: 'Then to Arafat after' — it is a sign for the standing place, and it is nunated only, and it is also called Arafah. The day of Arafah is the ninth of Dhul Hijjah. It is named so because Ibrahim (peace be upon him) knew that the command was from Allah on it, or because Jibril taught him the rites on it, or because Adam and Hawwa recognized each other on it after the descent to earth. This is a statement of the best practice, for if he went before dawn it is permissible, as the pilgrims do in our time, for most of them do not spend the night at Mina due to fear of thieves. It is recommended to travel via the road of Dhab and return via the road of Muzdalifah, following the Prophet, as in the Eid, and to camp with the people wherever he wishes, and near the mountain is better. Being away from the people in this place is blameworthy, and the state is one of supplication and humility, or harming himself or his goods, or causing hardship to passersby if on the road. The sunnah is that the imam camps at Namirah, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) zawaal there, without dispute. So in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: 'This is a statement of the best practice' — the wording of al-Hidayah: 'Then he proceeds to Arafat and stays there, and this is a statement of priority; however, if he left before it, it is permissible because no ruling is attached to this place.' He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: 'His statement: "This is a statement of priority" — Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir and others in their commentaries said: i.e., going to Arafah after sunrise is best, and if he left before it, it is permissible.' I said: 'This is good, but there remains something in the wording of the author of al-Hidayah, because it was necessary to restrict it to sunrise in his statement "then he proceeds to Arafat" so that his statement "This is a statement of priority" would be correct, but this restriction was omitted due to the scribe's oversight. Hence it is explicitly stated in Sharh al-Tahawi, Sharh al-Karkhi, al-Idah, etc.' Similarly in al-Inayah. He responded in al-Hawashi al-Sadiyyah with what is in al-Ghayah, referring the indication to proceeding to Arafat after Fajr prayer; but if he proceeds before it, it is permissible, yet it implies that proceeding before sunrise is like the wording of the text here—reflect. This is in Manasik of Imam al-Nawawi: 'As for what the people do in these times, entering the land of Arafat on the eighth day, it is an error contrary to the sunnah, and they miss many sunnahs because of it, including the prayers at Mina, spending the night there, proceeding from there to Namirah, staying there, the khutbah, prayer before entering Arafat, etc. The sunnah is that they stay at Namirah until the sun passes its zenith and perform ghusl there for standing; when the sun passes its zenith, the imam and people go to the mosque called Masjid Ibrahim, and the imam delivers two khutbahs before Zuhr prayer...'
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and expansion on the ruling for going to Arafat on the 9th. The commentator first explains the matn 'then to Arafat after' — noting that Arafah is the name of the standing place, and the 9th is the day of Arafah. The best practice is to go after Fajr (or after sunrise, as per al-Hidayah) but earlier is permissible. The commentator cites al-Hidayah's statement that going after sunrise is 'priority' (awlawiyyah). A critique follows: the author of al-Hidayah omitted the restriction of sunrise, leading some to think going before sunrise is also priority, but the correct view is that it's merely permissible. The text then cites al-Nawawi condemning the practice of entering Arafat on the 8th as a bid'ah that misses many sunan. The recommended route (via Dhab and Muzdalifah) and staying at Namirah are also explained. The Hanafi position is that going after Fajr is best, but going before is valid; other schools may differ on the timing.

Key Terms
عرفة (Arafah): The plain near Makkah where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; also the day itself.
نمرة (Namirah): A place near Arafat where the Prophet stayed before entering Arafat; it is sunnah for the imam to camp there.
الأفضل / الأولوية (al-afdal / al-awlawiyyah): The best or priority practice; a ruling that is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the best time to proceed to Arafat on the day of Arafah?
A) Before Fajr
B) After Fajr (or after sunrise)
C) Any time after midday
D) After Maghrib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the best time to go to Arafat is after Fajr on the 9th; entering on the 8th is an innovation that forfeits many sunan.

The Khutbah and Combined Prayer on the Day of Arafah
Explains the two khutbahs and the combined Zuhr and Asr prayer at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the khutbah and combined prayer at Arafah, identify the proof from the hadith of Jabir, and explain why no voluntary prayer is offered between them.

Core Idea
Two khutbahs after zawal; Zuhr and Asr with one adhan, two iqamahs, no nafl between.

In this passage, the commentator explains the sunnah practice of the Prophet ﷺ on the day of Arafah regarding the khutbah and the combined Zuhr and Asr prayer. You will learn the established procedure and the evidence from the hadith of Jabir, which also settles the intra-madhhab dispute about praying voluntary prayers between them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The khutbah and combined prayer at Arafah are both sunnah muakkadah. The khutbah is two, after zawal, with adhan before and sitting between. The prayer is Zuhr and Asr, each in its own time but connected with one adhan and two iqamahs.
The ruling is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Jabir, which describes the Prophet's actions at Arafah. This hadith is ahad but accepted in practice.
Hadith reference: long hadith of Jabir on Hajj.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly states that the Prophet gave adhan, then iqamah for Zuhr, then iqamah for Asr, with no prayer in between. This proves the procedure and the prohibition of any nafl between.
The phrase 'no prayer between' is key.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi works (e.g., al-Dhakhirah, al-Muhit) allow praying the sunnah of Zuhr between, but the correct view, based on the hadith and the mashayikh, is that it is not allowed.
The commentator refutes this, citing al-Fath and the hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is that no voluntary prayer, including the sunnah of Zuhr, is prayed between the two fard prayers at Arafah. This is established by the clear hadith and is the predominant position in the madhhab.
Tarjih authority: Hadith of Jabir and mashayikh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم اخطب) يعني خطبتين بعد الزوال والآذان قبل الصلاة يجلس بينهما كما في الجمعة للإتباع وإنما أطلقه لإفادة أنها جائزة قبل الزوال واكتفى بما ذكره في الأولى من تعليم المناسك عن أن يقول ويعلم الناس فيها المناسك التي هي إلى الخطبة الثالثة الوقوف بعرفة والمزدلفة والإفاضة منهما ورمى جمرة العقبة يوم النحر والذبح والحلق وطواف الزيارة. ولما كان الإطلاق مصروفاً إلى المعهود دل أنه إذا صعد الإمام المنبر وجلس أذن المؤذن وهو ظاهر المذهب وهو الصحيح للإتباع الثابت عنه عليه السلام . قوله : (ثم صل بعد الزوال الظهر والعصر بأذان وإقامتين بشرط الإمام والإحرام) لما ثبت من حديث جابر من الجمع بينهما كذلك فيؤذن للظهر ثم يقيم له ثم يقيم للعصر لأنها تؤدى قبل وقتها المعتاد فتفرد بالإقامة للإعلام. وأشار بذكر العصر بعد الظهر إلى أنه لا يصلي سنة الظهر البعديه وهو الصحيح كما في التصحيح فبالأولى أن لا يتنقل بينهما، فلو فعل كره وأعاد الأذان للعصر لانقطاع فوره فصار كالاشتغال بينهما بفعل آخر. وفي اقتصاره في بيان ... قوله : (فلو فعل كره) وأما ما ذكره في الذخيرة والمحيط والكافي من أنه لا يشتغل بين الصلاتين بالنافلة غير سنة الظهر فغير لما قال في الفتح : هذا ينافي حديث جابر فصلى الظهر ثم أقام فصلى العصر ولم يصل بينهما شيئاً وكذا ينافي إطلاق المشايخ في قولهم ولا يتطوع بينهما بشيء فإن التطوع يقال على السنة.
His statement: 'Then he delivers the khutbah' — i.e., two khutbahs after zawal, with the adhan before the prayer, and he sits between them as in Jumuah, following the sunnah. He only left it unrestricted to indicate that it is permissible before zawal, and he sufficed with what he mentioned in the first regarding teaching the rites, instead of saying that he teaches the people the rites which are up to the third khutbah: the standing at Arafah, Muzdalifah, the ifadah from them, stoning the Jamarat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr, slaughtering, shaving, and the tawaf al-ziyarah. Since the unrestricted statement is directed to the customary, it indicates that when the imam ascends the minbar and sits, the muezzin gives the adhan, and this is the apparent madhhab and is correct because of the established sunnah. His statement: 'Then pray after zawal Zuhr and Asr with one adhan and two iqamahs, on condition of imam and ihram' — because it is established from the hadith of Jabir that he combined them similarly. So he gives adhan for Zuhr, then iqamah for it, then iqamah for Asr, because it is performed before its usual time, so it is singled out with iqamah as notification. By mentioning Asr after Zuhr, he indicates that he does not pray the sunnah of Zuhr after it, and this is correct as in al-Tashih, so a fortiori he should not perform voluntary prayers between them. If he does, it is disliked, and he must repeat the adhan for Asr because its immediacy is broken, making it like occupying oneself with another act between them. And regarding his conciseness in explaining... His statement: 'If he did, it is disliked' — as for what is mentioned in al-Dhakhirah, al-Muhit, and al-Kafi, that he does not occupy himself between the two prayers with a nafl other than the sunnah of Zuhr, it is not accepted, because al-Fath said: This contradicts the hadith of Jabir that he prayed Zuhr, then gave iqamah and prayed Asr, and did not pray anything between them. Similarly, it contradicts the unrestricted statements of the mashayikh: 'He does not perform voluntary prayers between them' for tatawwu' is said of the sunnah.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the khutbah and combined prayer on the day of Arafah. The matn states: 'then deliver the khutbah' and then 'pray Zuhr and Asr after zawal with one adhan and two iqamahs'. The commentator explains that the khutbah is two, after zawal, with an adhan before prayer and a sitting between them, just like Jumuah. The matn's unrestricted wording implies that it is also valid before zawal, but the customary practice is after. The khutbah includes teaching the rites of Hajj. Regarding the prayer, the combination is proven by the hadith of Jabir. The procedure is: adhan for Zuhr, iqamah for Zuhr, then iqamah for Asr — no separate adhan for Asr because it is performed out of its normal time. Importantly, the sunnah of Zuhr after the fard is not prayed, nor any other voluntary prayer between them, as this would break the connection. If one does pray a nafl, the adhan for Asr must be repeated. The commentator refutes a contrary view from some books that allow praying the sunnah of Zuhr, citing the clear hadith.

Key Terms
الخطبتان (al-khutbatan): The two sermons delivered on the day of Arafah after zawal, teaching the rites of Hajj.
الجمع بين الصلاتين (al-jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining Zuhr and Asr on the day of Arafah in terms of time, performed with one adhan and two iqamahs.
فوت التطوع (fawt al-tatawwu'): The loss of the opportunity to pray voluntary prayers between the two fard prayers at Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying the sunnah of Zuhr after the fard Zuhr on the day of Arafah?
A) It is recommended
B) It is permissible
C) It is disliked and should be omitted
D) It is obligatory

Key Takeaway
On the day of Arafah, the Prophet's practice was two khutbahs after zawal and combining Zuhr and Asr with one adhan and two iqamahs, with no voluntary prayers between.

beginner
6 min
Recommended Route on 'Arafah Day
Ruling with proof: recommended Hajj route.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended route for the Imam and pilgrims on the Day of 'Arafah and explain its legal status as sunnah muakkadah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice sets the sunnah route: go via Dhabb, return via al-Ma'ziman.

The Day of 'Arafah is the pinnacle of Hajj. The Prophet ﷺ took a specific route from Mina to 'Arafah, and the Hanafi school recommends following it. This lesson unpacks that recommended path and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act and its ruling
Read the passage to find what act is recommended (route from Dhabb to al-Ma'ziman) and its legal classification (sunnah muakkadah).
The text uses 'yustahabbu' (it is recommended), indicating sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's practice: 'iqitida'an bi al-nabi' (following the Prophet). Identify the type of evidence (Sunnah).
The Prophet's own action establishes the sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the Prophet's action prove the ruling? In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's fi'l (action) is a proof of istihbab (recommendation) unless it indicates wujub. Here, it shows the route is sunnah.
4
Note any ikhtilaf
The text states there is no dispute about the Prophet setting out from Namirah, indicating consensus on that part.
The route recommendation is based on established practice, not a wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب أن يسير على طريق ضب ويعود على طريق المأزمين اقتداء بالنبي ﷺ كما في العيدين وينزل مع الناس حيث شاء وبقرب الجبل أفضل والبعد عن الناس في هذا المكان تجبر والحال حال تضرع ومسكنة أو اضرار بنفسه أو متاعه أو تضيق على المارة إن كان بالطريق والسنة أن ينزل الإمام بنمرة وتزول النبي ﷺ بها لا نزاع فيه. كذا في فتح القدير قوله : (ثم اخطب) يعني خطبتين بعد الزوال والآذان قبل الصلاة يجلس بينهما كما في الجمعة للإتباع وإنما أطلقه لإفادة أنها جائزة قبل الزوال واكتفى بما ذكره في الأولى من تعليم المناسك عن أن يقول ويعلم الناس فيها المناسك التي هي إلى الخطبة الثالثة الوقوف بعرفة والمزدلفة والإفاضة منهما ورمى جمرة العقبة يوم النحر والذبح والحلق وطواف الزيارة. ولما كان الإطلاق مصروفاً إلى المعهود دل أنه إذا صعد الإمام المنبر وجلس أذن المؤذن وهو ظاهر المذهب وهو الصحيح للإتباع الثابت عنه عليه السلام .
It is recommended to travel on the path of [mountain] Dhabb and return on the path of al-Ma'ziman, following the Prophet ﷺ as in the two 'Eids. He descends with the people wherever he wishes, and near the mountain is better. Distance from the people in this place is disliked if it causes hardship or harm to oneself or one's belongings or obstructs passersby if it is on the road. The Sunnah is that the Imam descends at Namirah, and the Prophet ﷺ set out from there; there is no dispute about that. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: (then deliver the sermon) means two sermons after zawal, and the adhan is before the prayer. He sits between them as in Jumu'ah, following the Sunnah. He expressed it absolutely to indicate that it is permissible before zawal, and he sufficed with what he mentioned in the first sermon about teaching the rituals, instead of saying that he teaches the people the rituals which are (included) up to the third sermon: the standing at 'Arafah, Muzdalifah, the departure from them, the stoning of Jamrat al-'Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, the slaughter, shaving, and the visitation Tawaf. Since the absolute expression is understood according to the customary practice, it indicates that when the Imam ascends the pulpit and sits, the mu'adhdhin gives the adhan. This is the apparent madhhab and it is the correct view due to the established following of the Prophet ﷺ.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the recommended acts for the Day of 'Arafah. It first mentions the recommended route: going via the mountain called Dhabb and returning via al-Ma'ziman, following the Prophet's practice as in the 'Eid prayers. The Imam and people should descend wherever convenient, but near the mountain is better. Staying far from people is disliked if it causes hardship. The Sunnah is for the Imam to camp at Namirah. Then it comments on the matn 'then deliver the sermon' (thumma akhtub). The author clarifies that this means two sermons after zawal (midday) with an adhan before the prayer, and sitting between them like Jumu'ah. The absolute expression indicates it can be done before zawal, though the custom is after. The first sermon includes teaching the rituals needed for Hajj. The fact that the absolute expression is understood according to the customary practice shows that when the Imam ascends the pulpit and sits, the mu'adhdhin gives the adhan; this is the apparent position of the madhhab and is correct due to the established practice of the Prophet ﷺ.

Key Terms
طريق ضب (Tariq Dhabb): A mountain road near 'Arafah; Dhabb is a specific mountain.
المأزمين (al-Ma'ziman): The narrow pass between Muzdalifah and 'Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal ruling of taking the route via Dhabb and returning via al-Ma'ziman on the Day of 'Arafah?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Makruh tanzih

Key Takeaway
The recommended route for 'Arafah is sunnah based on the Prophet's practice: entering via Dhabb and returning via al-Ma'ziman.

The Khutbah of 'Arafah
Ruling with proof: sunnah of the 'Arafah khutbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah of the 'Arafah khutbah, including its timing, number, content, and the accompanying adhan.

Core Idea
The 'Arafah khutbah mirrors Jumu'ah: two sermons after zawal, with adhan and sitting.

The sermon on 'Arafah is a pivotal moment. The Hanafi school details its structure: two sermons, adhan before, sitting between, and permissible content including teaching Hajj rituals. This lesson unpacks these details from the source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage comments on the matn 'thumma akhtub' (then deliver the sermon). Identify that it refers to two sermons (khutbatayn) and its ruling: sunnah.
The context is the Day of 'Arafah, not Jumu'ah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's practice: 'lil-ittiba' (following) and 'thabata anhu alayhi al-salam' (established from him).
The details of timing and structure are based on what the Prophet did.
3
Analyze the timing
The text says the sermons are after zawal (midday) and that the absolute wording indicates permissibility before zawal. Understand the flexibility.
The customary practice is after zawal, but not required.
4
Identify the components
List the parts: adhan before, two sermons with sitting between, content of first sermon (teaching rituals).
The adhan is given when the Imam ascends the pulpit.
5
Note the authority
The passage states that this is the apparent madhhab and correct view because of the established following.
This strengthens the position.

Combining Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah with One Adhan and Two Iqamahs
Ruling on combining Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah with conditions and consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for combining Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling if a sunnah is prayed between them.

Core Idea
Combining Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah is a confirmed sunnah: one adhan, two iqamahs, no voluntary prayers between.

The Day of 'Arafah is the most important day of Hajj. The Prophet ﷺ combined Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah in a specific way, which the Hanafi school meticulously preserves. Understanding this ruling ensures that pilgrims follow the Sunnah correctly and avoid common errors that break the prescribed sequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Combining Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah). It is not wajib, but it is highly recommended and must be performed exactly as the Prophet did.
The ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, which establishes a recommended act, not an obligation.
2
State the two conditions
The combination requires two conditions: (1) The presence of an Imam (the leader of the Hajj pilgrimage or his deputy), and (2) being in the state of ihram.
If either condition is missing, the combination is not recognized, and each prayer must be prayed in its own time.
3
Explain the procedure
The procedure is: one adhan for Zuhr, then iqamah for Zuhr, then two rak'ahs of Zuhr; then immediately iqamah for 'Asr, then two rak'ahs of 'Asr. No adhan is repeated for 'Asr because it is prayed before its usual time.
This is based on the hadith of Jabir (Sahih Muslim).
4
Note the prohibition of sunnan between
No sunnah or voluntary prayers are to be offered between the two fard prayers. The text specifically mentions that the post-sunnah of Zuhr is not prayed. If one prays any sunnah, it is disliked and breaks the immediate sequence (wusul).
If the sequence is broken, the adhan for 'Asr becomes invalid and must be repeated.
5
Understand the broader Sunnah
The passage also criticizes those who restrict the explanation to the eighth day, emphasizing that many other sunan (e.g., staying at Namira, bathing, two sermons) are part of the complete practice.
The full Sunnah includes staying at Namira until zawal, bathing, then proceeding to Masjid Ibrahim for the two sermons before the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم صل بعد الزوال الظهر والعصر بأذان وإقامتين بشرط الإمام والإحرام) لما ثبت من حديث جابر من الجمع بينهما كذلك فيؤذن للظهر ثم يقيم له ثم يقيم للعصر لأنها تؤدى قبل وقتها المعتاد فتفرد بالإقامة للإعلام. وأشار بذكر العصر بعد الظهر إلى أنه لا يصلي سنة الظهر البعديه وهو الصحيح كما في التصحيح فبالأولى أن لا يتنقل بينهما، فلو فعل كره وأعاد الأذان للعصر لانقطاع فوره فصار كالاشتغال بينهما بفعل آخر. وفي اقتصاره في بيان أرض عرفات في اليوم الثامن فخطأ مخالف للسنة ويفوتهم بسببه سنن كثيرة، ومنهم الصلوات بمعنى والمبيت بها والتوجه منها إلى نمرة والنزول بها والخطبة والصلاة قبل دخول عرفات وغير ذلك، فالسنة أني يمكثوا بنمرة حتى تزول الشمس ويغتسلوا بها للوقوف فإذا زالت الشمس ذهب الإمام والناس إلى المسجد المسمى مسجد إبراهيم ويخطب الإمام قبل صلاة الظهر خطبتين الخ
His statement: (then pray after zawal Zuhr and 'Asr with one adhan and two iqamahs, with the condition of the imam and ihram). This is established from the hadith of Jabir about combining them in this manner: he gives adhan for Zuhr, then iqamah for it, then iqamah for 'Asr, because it is performed before its usual time, so it is singled out with iqamah for notification. By mentioning 'Asr after Zuhr, he indicates that the post-sunna of Zuhr is not prayed; this is the correct view as in al-Tashih. A fortiori, no voluntary prayer is offered between them. If one does so, it is disliked, and the adhan for 'Asr must be repeated because its immediate sequence is broken, thus it becomes like engaging in another act between them. His restriction in explaining the land of 'Arafah on the eighth day is an error contrary to the Sunnah, causing them to miss many sunan: the prayers in meaning, staying overnight, proceeding to Namira, descending there, the khutbah, the prayer before entering 'Arafah, and others. The Sunnah is that they stay at Namira until the sun passes its zenith, and they bathe there for the standing. When the sun passes its zenith, the Imam and the people go to the mosque called Masjid Ibrahim, and the Imam delivers two sermons before Zuhr prayer.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn regarding the combination of Zuhr and 'Asr on the Day of 'Arafah. The author explains that the combination is performed with one adhan and two iqamahs, based on the hadith of Jabir. The adhan is for Zuhr, then iqamah for Zuhr, then another iqamah for 'Asr, because 'Asr is being prayed before its usual time. The mention of 'Asr after Zuhr indicates that the post-sunna of Zuhr is not prayed, and no voluntary prayer is offered between them. If one does pray, it is disliked and the adhan for 'Asr must be repeated because the immediate sequence is broken. The author then criticizes those who restrict the explanation of 'Arafah to the eighth day, saying that is an error that causes one to miss many sunan, such as staying at Namira, bathing, and the khutbah.

Key Terms
أذان وإقامتين (adhan wa iqamatayn): One adhan for Zuhr and two iqamahs: one for Zuhr and one for 'Asr.
سنن (sunan): Recommended acts that are highly encouraged; missing them is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
