A) It is permissible
B) It is disliked and the adhan for 'Asr must be repeated
C) It invalidates the whole combination
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's practice of combining at 'Arafah is a confirmed sunnah that must be followed precisely: one adhan, two iqamahs, no voluntary prayers between.

Takbir al-Tashriq Between the Combined Prayers
Critical analysis of whether takbir breaks the fawr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on Takbir al-Tashriq between combined prayers and evaluate the argument that it breaks the immediate sequence.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib and does not break the immediate sequence between combined prayers.

This lesson addresses a practical question for those performing Hajj: must the Takbir al-Tashriq be recited between the combined prayers at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah? Some scholars argue that any interposed act, even worship, breaks the required immediate sequence. The Hanafi school, however, maintains that takbir's obligation and brevity exempt it from this rule.

Guided Path
1
State the practical scenario
Identify the situation: combining Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah, and Maghrib and 'Isha' at Muzdalifah. The question is whether Takbir al-Tashriq should be recited between these two fard prayers.
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib after every fard prayer from 'Arafah day through the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
2
Identify the opposing view
The quoted scholar holds that any act between the combined prayers, including takbir, breaks the immediate sequence (fawr), making it disliked and requiring repetition of adhan/iqamah.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The opposing view relies on the hadith that the Prophet ﷺ did not pray anything between the two prayers. The author argues this only prohibits prayer, not takbir.
Hadith: 'He did not pray anything between them' (لم يصل بينهما شيئاً)
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author refutes the analogy to supererogatory prayer because takbir is wajib and its duration is short. Thus, it does not constitute a break in the sequence.
Qiyas with nafl is invalid due to the obligation (wujub) and brevity (yusr) of takbir.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The author concludes that takbir remains obligatory and does not break the fawr, as no evidence supports dropping it.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه : نقل المدني عن إجابة السائلين للشيخ عبد الله العفيف أنه قال : سئل العلامة السيد محمد صادق بن أحمد بادشاه عن تكبير التشريق هل يجب على الإمام الأعظم ومن اقتدى به فيما بين كل من صلاتي الجمع بعرفة ومزدلفة الإتيان به لما صرح به أئمتنا من أن العمل والفتوى على قولهما وهما لم يشترطا شيئاً مما شرطه الإمام من المصر وغيره أم لا يجب؟ وهل إذا أتوا به بعد قاطعاً لفور الأذان أم لا ؟ فأجاب : مقتضى كلامهم أن هذه الكيفية - أعني العصر بعد الظهر فوراً والعشاء بعد المغرب كذلك - لا خلاف في مراعاتها عند الجميع حتى لو فقدت بالاشتغال بعمل عبادة كان أم لا كره وأعيد الأذان للعصر والإقامة للعشاء، وما ذاك إلا للاتفاق على ورودها عنه ا هـ قلت: وفيه نظر، فإن الوارد في الحديث أنه لم يصل بينهما شيئاً، ولا يلزم منه ترك التكبير ولا يقاس على النافلة لوجوبه ولأن مدته يسيرة، ولذا لم يعد فاصلاً بين الفريضة والراتبة. والحاصل أن التكبير بعد ثبوت وجوبه عندنا لا يسقط وجوبه هنا إلا بدليل، وما ذكر لا يصلح للدلالة كما علمته هذا ما ظهر لي والله أعلم
Notice: Al-Madani narrated from 'Ijat al-Sa'ilin of Sheikh 'Abdullah al-'Afif that he said: The allamah al-Sayyid Muhammad Sadiq ibn Ahmad Badshah was asked about Takbir al-Tashriq: Is it obligatory for the supreme Imam and those who follow him to recite it between each of the combined prayers at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah, given that our imams have stated that practice and fatwa are according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and they did not stipulate anything of what the Imam of the city stipulates? Or is it not obligatory? And if they recite it, does it definitively break the immediate sequence (fawr) of the adhan? He answered: The implication of their words is that this manner - meaning 'Asr immediately after Zuhr and 'Isha' immediately after Maghrib - is unanimously observed by all, such that if it is lost due to engagement in any act, whether worship or not, it is disliked and the adhan for 'Asr and iqamah for 'Isha' are repeated. This is only due to agreement on its transmission from him (the Prophet). I say: There is consideration in this. What is transmitted in the hadith is that he did not pray anything between them. This does not necessitate leaving the takbir, nor can it be analogized to supererogatory prayer due to its obligation and because its duration is short. Therefore, it is not considered a separator between the obligatory and the supererogatory. The conclusion is that takbir, after its obligation is established according to us, its obligation is not waived here except by evidence, and what has been mentioned is not suitable as evidence, as you have learned. This is what appeared to me, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage is a notice (tanbih) addressing the question of whether Takbir al-Tashriq must be recited between the combined prayers at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah and whether it breaks the required immediate sequence. The text presents a question posed to a scholar: Is the takbir obligatory for the Imams and followers, and does it break the sequence? The answer given is that the combined prayers must be performed immediately without any gap; any act, including worship, that breaks this sequence is disliked and requires repeating the adhan or iqamah. However, the author of the commentary disagrees. He argues that the hadith only says the Prophet did not pray anything between them, which does not necessitate omitting the takbir. Since takbir is wajib and its duration is short, it should not be considered a separator. Thus, the obligation of takbir is not waived by the requirement of immediate sequence. The author concludes that no evidence supports dropping the takbir.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The specific takbir recited after fard prayers from the Day of 'Arafah through the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
فور (fawr): Immediate sequence; the requirement to combine prayers without any gap.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of this passage, what is the ruling on reciting Takbir al-Tashriq between the combined Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah?
A) It is forbidden because it breaks the immediate sequence
B) It is recommended but not obligatory
C) It is obligatory and does not break the sequence
D) It is disliked and requires repeating the adhan

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib and does not break the immediate sequence between combined prayers, as it is neither a prayer nor does it disrupt the fawr.

Is Congregation a Condition for the Imam in Combined Prayer at Arafah?
Refutes the claim that congregation is a condition for joining prayers at 'Arafah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether congregation is a condition for the Imam in combined prayer at Arafah, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue.

Core Idea
Congregation is not a condition for the Imam himself, only for the followers — even at Arafah.

This passage refines an earlier discussion about the conditions for combining prayers at Arafah during Hajj. While some Hanafi scholars, such as al-Asbijabi, maintain that congregation is a condition for the Imam, the preferred view, championed by the author of al-Muhit, holds that it is not. The proof lies in the case of the rush (faza') where people flee from the Imam, yet he may still combine the prayers. This lesson unpacks the debate and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of contention
Determine whether congregation is a condition for the Imam when combining prayers at Arafah. The passage discusses two opposing views within the Hanafi school.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Al-Asbijabi holds that congregation is a condition for the Imam, based on transmissions from Abu Hanifa. The author of al-Muhit holds it is not, as the Imam is a condition for others but not for himself.
3
Examine the evidence for each
The opposing view relies on transmitted statements. The preferred view uses the case of faza' (people fleeing) as evidence that the Imam can combine alone, supported by rational reasoning.
The case of faza' is not an exception but a demonstration of the underlying principle.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
If congregation is a condition, the Imam cannot combine when alone. If not, he can combine alone. This affects many practical scenarios at Arafah.
5
Apply the tarjih
The author favors the view of al-Muhit because it agrees with both transmitted evidence (the case of faza') and rational evidence (the Imam's role). This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فما في النقاية الخ) قال في النهر : وفيه نظر فقد نقل غير واحد اشتراط الجماعة على قول الإمام. قال الأسبيجابي : وهو الصحيح. وأما مسألة الفزع فبتقدير تسليمه إنما جاز له الجمع ضرورة كما علل به الشارح فيما إذا نفر وإلا أن الجماعة غير شرط ا.هـ. قال العلامة نوح أفندي بعد ذكره عبارة البدائع التي ذكرها المؤلف قلت : اختار صاحب المحيط هذا حيث قال : ولو نفر الناس عن الإمام بعد الشروع أو قبله فصلى وحده الصلاتين جاز لأن الجماعة ليست بشرط في حق الإمام عند أبي حنيفة، أما الإمام فشرط في حق غيره ا هـ. فعلى هذا لا ترد مسألة الفزع أصلاً ولا تحتاج إلى الجواب قطعاً والذي يقتضيه النظر أن هذا القول هو الأولى بالقبول لموافقته المنقول والمعقول، فالأول ما سبق أن من صلاهما مع
His statement: (As for what is in al-Nuqayah, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: There is consideration in this. More than one have transmitted the condition of congregation on the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa). Al-Asbijabi said: This is the correct view. As for the issue of the rush (faza'), even if it is conceded, he is only allowed to combine out of necessity, as the commentator explained when they flee. Otherwise, congregation is not a condition. End quote. Allamah Nuh Afandi said after mentioning the wording of al-Bada'i' that the author mentioned: I say: The author of al-Muhit chose this view, where he said: If the people flee from the Imam after starting or before, and he prays both prayers alone, it is permissible because congregation is not a condition with respect to the Imam according to Abu Hanifa, whereas the Imam is a condition with respect to others. So on this basis, the issue of the rush is not sustained at all and does not need an answer definitively. What is required by consideration is that this statement is more worthy of acceptance due to its agreement with transmitted and rational evidence. The first is what preceded that he who prays both...

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) on the earlier discussion about whether congregation (jamāʿah) is a condition for the combined prayer at ʿArafah. The author quotes a critique from al-Nahr that multiple scholars have transmitted that congregation is a condition according to Imam Abū Ḥanīfa, and al-Asbijābī considers this correct. The case of people fleeing (fazʿ) is an exception due to necessity. However, the author then presents the view of Ṣāḥib al-Muḥīṭ, supported by ʿAllāmah Nūḥ Afandī, that congregation is not a condition for the Imam himself; the Imam is a condition for the followers, not for himself. Therefore, if people flee, the Imam may pray alone, and this does not contradict the condition. The author favors this latter view as it agrees with both transmitted and rational evidence. This resolves the apparent conflict in the earlier discussion.

Key Terms
مسألة الفزع (mas'alah al-faza'): The case where people flee from the Imam due to fear, leaving him alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Imam is not required to have a congregation when combining prayers at Arafah; the condition applies only to the followers.

Congregation Not a Condition for the Imam in Combining Prayers at Arafat
Ruling with proof: Congregation not a condition for Imam in combining at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that congregation is not a condition for the Imam in combining prayers at Arafat and identify the proof from the panic scenario.

Core Idea
The Imam may combine prayers at Arafat alone; congregation is not a condition for him, only for the followers.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies an important nuance about combining prayers at Arafat. While congregation is normally emphasized, in the specific context of the Imam at Arafat, even if he prays alone due to panic, it is permissible by consensus. The commentator distinguishes this from the case of a substitute imam, reinforcing that the Imam's position is unique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining two obligatory prayers (Zuhr and Asr, or Maghrib and Isha) at Arafat. The ruling stated is that congregation is not a condition for the Imam.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the scenario where the people are seized by panic at Arafat and the Imam prays alone, which is deemed permissible by consensus (ijma). This shows that congregation is not a condition for the Imam.
The dalil is based on consensus, not a direct textual source.
3
Distinguish the substitute case
The passage contrasts the above with a case where the Imam breaks wudu and appoints a substitute; the substitute cannot combine both prayers alone. This illustrates that the Imam's ability to combine without congregation is specific to him, not transferable.
The substitute becomes like a follower, not the Imam, so the condition of congregation applies to him.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., in al-Niqayah) consider congregation a condition even for the Imam, but the author treats this view as weak (da'if). The relied-upon position is that it is not a condition for the Imam.
This is an example of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that the Imam may combine prayers alone in necessity; congregation is not a required condition for him.
The author cites the panic scenario as evidence for this position.

The condition of combining, as mentioned, is evidence that the sermon is not a condition for it, unlike Friday, and that congregation is not a condition for it, so much so that if the people are seized by panic at Arafat and the Imam prays the two prayers alone, it is permissible by consensus according to what is correct, as in al-Wajiz. And in al-Bada'i: The case where the Imam is overtaken by an event during Zuhr prayer and appoints a substitute, then leaves to make wudu, and the substitute prays Zuhr and Asr, then the Imam returns, is not analogous; he may not pray Asr except in its time, because the permissibility there is not due to lack of congregation but due to lack of an Imam, since he left being an Imam and became like one of the followers, or it is said: Congregation is a condition for combining according to Abu Hanifa, but only for other than the Imam, not for the Imam. Al-Niqayah, al-Jawhara, and al-Majma' consider the condition of congregation weak. From al-Lubab and its commentary: His saying 'So it became' is like occupying oneself between them with another act like eating, drinking, and talking.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions for combining prayers at Arafat. It first states that the sermon (khutbah) is not a condition for combining, unlike the Friday prayer. Then it states that congregation (jama'ah) is also not a condition, citing the scenario of panic at Arafat where the Imam prays alone and it is permissible by consensus. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: if the Imam exits the prayer due to an event (hadath) and appoints a substitute, the substitute prays both Zuhr and Asr, but when the Imam returns, he cannot pray Asr except in its time. This shows that the Imam's ability to combine without congregation is specific to him, not to others. The commentator notes that according to Abu Hanifa, congregation is a condition for combining but only for the followers, not for the Imam himself. The passage also covers the ruling on voluntary prayers between the two prayers: it is not disliked for the follower to pray voluntary until the Imam begins Asr, but it is disliked after Asr, even if it is still Zuhr time.

الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two obligatory prayers (Zuhr and Asr, or Maghrib and Isha) at the same time at Arafat or Muzdalifah.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregational prayer behind an Imam.
الفزع (al-faza'): Panic or fear that scatters the people at Arafat.

Conditions for Combining Prayers at Arafat: Imam and Ihram
Critical commentary on conditions for combining at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for combining prayers at Arafat and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of ihram.

Core Idea
To combine prayers at Arafat, you must be behind the supreme Imam and in Hajj ihram—but the Sahibayn differ on when ihram matters.

Combining the Zuhr and Asr prayers at Arafat is a distinctive rite of Hajj. The Hanafi school imposes two specific conditions: the prayer must be led by the supreme Imam (or his deputy), and the pilgrim must be in the state of ihram for Hajj. However, within the school, Abu Hanifa and his two companions disagree on whether Hajj ihram is required for both prayers or only for Asr. This lesson unpacks these conditions and the internal dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
From the text, extract the two conditions the author emphasizes: the Imam must be the supreme Imam or his deputy, and the pilgrim must be in ihram for Hajj (not Umrah).
2
Examine the congregation issue
Understand that congregation is not a condition for the Imam himself, but the Imam is a condition for the followers. The author resolves the apparent conflict with the case of panic.
The author quotes Nuh Afandi's preference from al-Muhit.
3
Define the ihram requirement precisely
Note that Abu Hanifa requires Hajj ihram for both Zuhr and Asr. The text explicitly states that if one is in Umrah ihram at Zuhr, even if he changes to Hajj ihram by Asr, the combination is invalid according to Abu Hanifa.
The two companions only require Hajj ihram at the time of Asr.
4
Contrast the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Use the madhhab dispute map to see the opposing view: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider ihram for Hajj necessary only at the time of Asr. This difference has practical consequences for the validity of the combined prayer.
The author sides with Abu Hanifa as the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the tarjih and modern application
Apply the mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa's view) to a scenario: a pilgrim in Umrah ihram cannot combine, even if he intends Hajj later. This is the strict ruling for fatwa.
The author prefers the view of al-Muhit and Nuh Afandi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فما في النقاية الخ) قال في النهر: وفيه نظر فقد نقل غير واحد اشتراط الجماعة على قول الإمام. قال الأسبيجابي : وهو الصحيح. وأما مسألة الفزع فبتقدير تسليمه إنما جاز له الجمع ضرورة كما علل به الشارح فيما إذا نفر وإلا أن الجماعة غير شرط ا.هـ. قال العلامة نوح أفندي بعد ذكره عبارة البدائع التي ذكرها المؤلف قلت : اختار صاحب المحيط هذا حيث قال : ولو نفر الناس عن الإمام بعد الشروع أو قبله فصلى وحده الصلاتين جاز لأن الجماعة ليست بشرط في حق الإمام عند أبي حنيفة، أما الإمام فشرط في حق غيره ا هـ. فعلى هذا لا ترد مسألة الفزع أصلاً ولا تحتاج إلى الجواب قطعاً والذي يقتضيه النظر أن هذا القول هو الأولى بالقبول لموافقته المنقول والمعقول، فالأول ما سبق أن من صلاهما مع الإمام والإحرام بالتعريف للإشارة إلى تعيينهما فالمراد بالإمام الإمام الأعظم أو نائبه مقيماً كان أو مسافراً، فلا يجوز الجمع مع إمام غيرهما. ولم مات الإمام وهو الخليفة جمع نائبه أو صاحب شرطه لأن النواب لا ينعزلون بموت الخليفة وإلا صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها، والمراد بالإحرام إحرام الحج حتى لو كان محرماً بالعمرة يصلي العصر في وقته عنده، وهذان الشرطان لا بد منهما في كل من الصلاتين لا في العصر وحدها حتى لو كان محرماً بالعمرة في الظهر محرماً بالحج في العصر لا يجوز له الجمع عنده كما لو لم يكن محرماً في الظهر. وأطلق في وقت الإحرام فأفاد أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون محرماً قبل الزوال أو بعده وهو الصحيح لأن المقصود حصوله عند أداء الصلاتين ولا يشترط الإمام الجميع أداء الظهر حتى لو أدرك جزءاً منه معـ جاز له الجمع . كذا في المحيط . وهذا كله مذهب الإمام، وعندهما لا يشترط إلا الإحرام عند العصر وهو رواية فجوّز للمنفرد الجمع. وفي قوله صلى الظهر إشارة إلى الصحيحة فلو صلاها ثم تبين فساد الظهر أعادهما جميعاً لأن الفاسد عدم شرعاً، وذكر في معراج الدراية أنه يؤخر هذا الجمع إلى آخر وقت الظهر، وفي المحيط لا يجهر بالقراءة فيهما
His saying: (What is in al-Niqayah etc.) He said in al-Nahr: There is consideration in it, for more than one have transmitted the condition of congregation according to the Imam's statement. Al-Usbijabi said: It is the correct view. As for the case of panic, assuming it is conceded, he is only permitted to combine out of necessity, as the commentator reasoned in the case of flight; otherwise, congregation is not a condition. The scholar Nuh Afandi said after mentioning the wording of al-Bada'i' that the author mentioned: I said: The author of al-Muhit chose this where he said: If the people flee from the Imam after starting or before, and he prays the two prayers alone, it is permissible because congregation is not a condition for the Imam according to Abu Hanifa; however, the Imam is a condition for others. Accordingly, the case of panic does not constitute a problem at all and definitely does not require an answer. What the view necessitates is that this statement is more worthy of acceptance because it agrees with transmitted and rational evidence. The first (view) is what preceded: that whoever prays them with the Imam—and ihram is by definition to indicate their specificity—the intended meaning of Imam is the supreme Imam or his deputy, whether resident or traveler. So combining with an Imam other than them is not permissible. And if the Imam dies while he is the caliph, his deputy or the one in charge of his affairs combines, because deputies are not removed by the death of the caliph; otherwise, he would pray each one in its time. The intended meaning of ihram is the ihram of Hajj, so that if one is in ihram for Umrah, he prays Asr in its time according to him. These two conditions are necessary for each of the two prayers, not for Asr alone, so that if one is in ihram for Umrah at Zuhr and in ihram for Hajj at Asr, it is not permissible for him to combine according to him, just as if he were not in ihram at Zuhr. He was absolute regarding the time of ihram, so it indicates that there is no difference between being in ihram before or after noon; this is correct because the purpose is its occurrence at the time of performing the two prayers. The Imam does not require completing all of Zuhr; if he catches part of it with the Imam, it is permissible for him to combine. This is all the madhhab of the Imam (Abu Hanifa). According to the two companions, only ihram at the time of Asr is required, and this is a narration; they permit the individual to combine. In his saying 'he prayed Zuhr' there is an indication of the valid prayer; if he prays it then discovers the invalidity of Zuhr, he repeats both, because the invalid is non-existent legally. It is mentioned in Mi'raj al-Diraya that he delays this combination to the end of Zuhr time, and in al-Muhit, he does not recite loudly in either of the two prayers.
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the conditions for combining prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah. It begins by addressing a statement from al-Niqayah about the condition of congregation, noting that multiple authorities report the condition of congregation according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). Al-Usbijabi considers this correct, but the author argues that the case of panic is a necessity, and the sound view is that congregation is not a condition for the Imam himself. The commentator quotes Nuh Afandi who prefers the view from al-Muhit that congregation is not a condition for the Imam but the Imam is a condition for others. Then the text moves to the two conditions: the Imam must be the supreme Imam or his deputy (whether resident or traveler), and the pilgrim must be in the state of ihram for Hajj. If one is in ihram for Umrah, combining is not allowed. Intricate details are given: if the pilgrim catches part of Zuhr with the Imam, he may combine; if Zuhr turns out invalid, both prayers must be repeated. A dispute with the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is noted: they only require ihram at the time of Asr, allowing the individual to combine. Finally, it mentions delaying the combination to the end of Zuhr time and that recitation should not be loud in either prayer.

Key Terms
الإمام الأعظم (al-imam al-a'zam): The supreme Imam, i.e., the caliph or the ruling head of the Muslim community.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj (not Umrah) as a condition for combining.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregation, which is not a condition for the Imam but is a condition for followers according to Abu Hanifa.

C) Ihram is not required
D) Ihram for Hajj is only required for Asr

Key Takeaway
Combining prayers at Arafat requires the supreme Imam or his deputy and Hajj ihram for both prayers according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Combining at Arafat: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Imam and Ihram
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining prayers at Arafat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the tarjih to determine the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Combining at Arafat requires both a caliphal Imam and Hajj Ihram according to Imam Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn only require Ihram at Asr.

Combining the Zuhr and Asr prayers on the day of Arafat is a specific sunnah, but the Hanafi school has an internal disagreement about the necessary conditions. Does one need to be led by the caliph? Must one be in Ihram for Hajj from the start of Zuhr? This lesson unpacks the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and clarifies the operative ruling for today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions according to Imam Abu Hanifa
Read the text to extract the exact conditions: (1) the prayer must be led by the caliph or his deputy, and (2) the individual must be in the state of Ihram for Hajj at both Zuhr and Asr.
The text uses 'Imam' to mean the Supreme Imam or his deputy.
2
Compare the Sahibayn's position
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani require only that the individual be in Ihram for Hajj at the time of Asr; they do not require the presence of the caliph or his deputy for the individual.
The Sahibayn's view is presented as a riwaya within the school.
3
Examine the proofs and reasoning
Identify the basis for each position: Imam's view is based on the practice of the Prophet and the caliphs; Sahibayn consider the condition of the Imam to be for the congregation, not binding on the individual.
No explicit dalil is quoted; the text relies on transmitted practice.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical difference: According to Imam, an individual without a caliphal Imam cannot combine; according to Sahibayn, any individual in Hajj Ihram at Asr may combine alone.
This affects pilgrims who may not have access to the caliph's prayer.
5
Apply the tarjih
Use the later authority (al-Burhan in al-Sharnablaliyya) to identify that the Sahibayn's view is deemed 'al-azhar' (more apparent) and is often followed in fatwa.
Even so, the Imam's view remains within the school as a valid position.

الإمام والإحرام بالتعريف للإشارة إلى تعيينهما فالمراد بالإمام الإمام الأعظم أو نائبه مقيماً كان أو مسافراً، فلا يجوز الجمع مع إمام غيرهما. ولم مات الإمام وهو الخليفة جمع نائبه أو صاحب شرطه لأن النواب لا ينعزلون بموت الخليفة وإلا صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها، والمراد بالإحرام إحرام الحج حتى لو كان محرماً بالعمرة يصلي العصر في وقته عنده، وهذان الشرطان لا بد منهما في كل من الصلاتين لا في العصر وحدها حتى لو كان محرماً بالعمرة في الظهر محرماً بالحج في العصر لا يجوز له الجمع عنده كما لو لم يكن محرماً في الظهر. وأطلق في وقت الإحرام فأفاد أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون محرماً قبل الزوال أو بعده وهو الصحيح لأن المقصود حصوله عند أداء الصلاتين ولا يشترط الإمام الجميع أداء الظهر حتى لو أدرك جزءاً منه معـ جاز له الجمع . كذا في المحيط . وهذا كله مذهب الإمام، وعندهما لا يشترط إلا الإحرام عند العصر وهو رواية فجوّز للمنفرد الجمع. وفي قوله صلى الظهر إشارة إلى الصحيحة فلو صلاها ثم تبين فساد الظهر أعادهما جميعاً لأن الفاسد عدم شرعاً، وذكر في معراج الدراية أنه يؤخر هذا الجمع إلى آخر وقت الظهر، وفي المحيط لا يجهر بالقراءة فيهما . ثم بعد ذلك يظهر في المخطوط: "بهم صلاة الإمام أو نائبه محرماً يجمع، ومن لا فلا عنده والثاني أن اشتراط الإمام عين اشتراط الجماعة لأن المراد منه اشتراط أدائها لا اشترط وجوده في الموقف وإلا لصح جمع من وجد في الموقف منفرداً وليس مذهب الإمام بل مذهب الصاحبين فاشتراطهم الإمام يعين اشتراط الجماعة معه، ويؤيده تخصيصهم جواز الجمع منفرداً في حق الإمام فقط وتعليل بعضهم له بعدم اشتراط الجماعة في حقه وأكثرهم بالضرورة، فعلى هذا فالجماعة شرط غير لازم في حقه فتسقط بالضرورة لازم في حقهم فلا تسقط بحال قوله : (مقيماً كان أو مسافراً) لكن إن كان مقيماً كإمام مكة صلى . المقيمين ولا يجوز له القصر ولا للحاج الاقتداء به . قال الإمام الحلواني : كان الإمام النسفي يقول : العجب من أهل الموقف يتابعون إمام مكة في القصر وبينهم وبين مكة فرسخان فأنى يستجاب لهم وأنى يرجى لهم الخير وصلاتهم غير جائزة؟ قال شمس الأئمة: كنت مع أهل الموقف فاعتزلت وصليت كل صلاة في وقتها وأوصيت بذلك أصحابي. وقد سمعنا أنه يتكلف ويخرج مسيرة سفر ثم يأتي ،عرفات، فلو كان هكذا فالقصر جائز وإلا لا فيجب الاحتياط (تاترخانية عن المحيط ملخصاً) قوله : (وعندهما لا يشترط إلا الإحرام الخ ذكر في الشرنبلالية عن البرهان أنه الأظهر قوله : (وذكر في معراج الدراية الخ نقله شارح اللباب عن شرح الجامع لقاضيخان وقال فيه : إنه يلزم منه تأخير الوقوف، وينافي حديث جابر رضي الله عنه حتى إذا زاغت الشمس» فإن ظاهره أن الخطبة كانت في أول الزوال فلا تقع الصلاة في آخر وقت الظهر ولا يبعد أن يكون مراده أنه يصلي الظهر والعصر بعده وقبله
The Imam and Ihram are defined to indicate their specification. What is meant by Imam is the Supreme Imam or his deputy, whether resident or traveler. So it is not permissible to combine with an Imam other than them. And if the Imam dies while he is the caliph, his deputy or the chief of police combines because the deputies are not dismissed by the death of the caliph. Otherwise, he would pray each prayer at its time. And what is meant by Ihram is the Ihram of Hajj, so if one is in Ihram for Umrah, he prays Asr at its time according to him. These two conditions are necessary in each of the two prayers, not only in Asr, so if one is in Ihram for Umrah in Zuhr and in Ihram for Hajj in Asr, it is not permissible for him to combine according to him, just as if he were not in Ihram in Zuhr. And he made the time of Ihram absolute, indicating that there is no difference between being in Ihram before noon or after, and this is correct because the objective is to have it at the time of performing the two prayers. And the Imam does not require everyone to perform Zuhr fully, so even if he caught part of it, he may combine. Kama fi al-Muhit. This is all the school of Imam, and according to them (the two companions) only Ihram at the time of Asr is required, which is a narration, so they allowed the individual to combine. And in his saying 'he prayed Zuhr' there is an indication of the valid prayer, so if he prayed it and then the invalidity of Zuhr became apparent, he repeats both because the invalid is considered non-existent legally. And it is mentioned in Mi'raj al-Diraya that he delays this combining to the end of the time of Zuhr, and in al-Muhit he does not recite aloud in them. Then after that in the manuscript: 'With him, the prayer of the Imam or his deputy in Ihram combines, and one who is not - no according to him. And the second that the condition of the Imam is exactly the condition of the congregation because what is meant is the condition of performing it, not the condition of his presence at the standing; otherwise the combining of one who is at the standing alone would be valid, and that is not the school of Imam but the school of the two companions. So their conditioning the Imam is exactly the condition of the congregation with him. This is supported by their specifying the permissibility of combining alone only for the Imam, and the reasoning of some of them for that being the lack of the condition of congregation in his right, and most of them due to necessity. So according to this, the congregation is a condition not binding in his right, so it drops due to necessity; binding in their right, so it does not drop at all. His saying: (whether resident or traveler) but if he is resident, like the Imam of Mecca, he prays the prayer of residents and he may not shorten, and the pilgrim may not follow him. Imam al-Halawani said: Imam al-Nasafi used to say: 'I wonder about the people of the standing following the Imam of Mecca in shortening while between them and Mecca is two farsakhs; how can it be accepted for them and how can they hope for good? Their prayer is not permissible.' Shams al-A'immah said: I was with the people of the standing and I separated and prayed each prayer in its time, and I advised my companions likewise. And we have heard that he takes the trouble and travels the distance of a journey and then comes to Arafat. So if it is so, then shortening is permissible; otherwise, precaution is necessary. (Tatarkhaniyya from al-Muhit, summarized). His saying: (and according to them, only Ihram is required, etc.) It is mentioned in al-Sharnablaliyya from al-Burhan that it is the more apparent. His saying: (and it is mentioned in Mi'raj al-Diraya, etc.) Transmitted by Sharh al-Lubab from Sharh al-Jami' of Qadi Khan and he said in it: It necessitates delaying the standing, and contradicts the hadith of Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) 'until the sun declined' for its apparent meaning is that the sermon was at the beginning of zawaal, so the prayer would not occur at the end of the time of Zuhr. And it is not far that his intent is that he prays Zuhr and Asr after it and before it.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling for combining the Zuhr and Asr prayers on the day of Arafat. The base text (كنز الدقائق) is explained, clarifying the two conditions: the prayer must be led by the caliph or his deputy, and the person must be in the state of Ihram for Hajj. Imam Abu Hanifa's position is presented in detail, followed by the view of the two companions (Sahibayn) who relax the conditions. The commentary then discusses exceptions and practical implications, such as the case of the Imam of Mecca combining while being a resident, and warnings from earlier scholars about the validity of such practice. The relied-upon position according to some later authorities is the view of the Sahibayn, as quoted from al-Burhan.

Key Terms
الإمام الأعظم (al-imam al-a'zam): The supreme leader of the Muslims, the caliph, whose presence or deputy is required for combining prayers at Arafat according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah; here specifically for Hajj at the time of the combined prayers.
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two prayers (Zuhr and Asr) at Arafat on the day of 'Arafah, not the general combining of prayers due to travel or rain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the condition regarding Ihram for combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat?
A) The pilgrim must be in Ihram for Hajj at the time of Asr only.
B) The pilgrim must be in Ihram for Hajj at both Zuhr and Asr.
C) The pilgrim must be in Ihram for Umrah at Zuhr and Hajj at Asr.
D) Ihram is not required for combining; only the Imam matters.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two views on combining at Arafat: Imam Abu Hanifa (strict: caliphal Imam and Hajj Ihram at both times) and the Sahibayn (relaxed: Hajj Ihram at Asr only), with later preference given to the Sahibayn.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner

Location of Standing at Arafat and Prophetic Spot
Ruling on valid standing area and description of Prophetic spot at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the valid standing area at Arafat, identify Batn 'Arnah as excluded, and explain the recommendation to stand near the Prophetic spot.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is valid for standing except Batn 'Arnah; seeking the Prophetic spot is sunnah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies an essential ruling for Hajj: where exactly must one stand at Arafat? While wuquf itself is a pillar, the text explains that the entire plain of Arafat is acceptable, except for a specific valley called Batn 'Arnah. The passage then provides a detailed description of the exact spot where the Prophet ﷺ stood, urging pilgrims to seek it if possible, but emphasizing that any valid location within Arafat suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wuquf (standing) at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah. The ruling from the text: all of Arafat is a valid standing place except Batn 'Arnah. Standing near Jabal al-Rahmah and at the Prophetic spot is recommended (sunnah).
Wuquf itself is a rukn of Hajj; the specifics of location are about optimal performance.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'Arafat is all a standing place, and avoid Batn 'Arnah.' This is a Sunnah ahad report, muttafaq alayh in meaning.
The hadith is quoted in the text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit wording 'all of Arafat is a standing place' establishes permissibility across the entire area. The command 'avoid Batn 'Arnah' excludes that specific valley, indicating standing there is invalid.
Hanafi usul: al-amr al-mutlaq yufidu al-wujub? Here the command to avoid implies prohibition of standing there.
4
Distinguish rukn from sunnah
Standing anywhere within Arafat (except Batn 'Arnah) fulfills the rukn. However, seeking the specific spot where the Prophet stood near Jabal al-Rahmah is a sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory.
The detailed description helps the pilgrim, but missing it does not invalidate Hajj.
5
Apply the description
If a pilgrim can identify the Prophetic spot using the landmarks (cleft, square building, burnt rock), they should stand there. Otherwise, they should stand in the general area between the mountain and the building.
The text provides a practical guidance for those who seek the sunnah.

محسر وشعاب مكة كلها منحر» (۱) وفي المغرب : عرنة واد بحذاء عرفات وبتصغيرها سميت عرينة ينسب إليها العرنيون. وذكر القرطبي في تفسيره أنها بفتح الراء وضمها بغربي مسجد عرفة حتى لقد قال بعض العلماء : إن الجدار الغربي من مسجد عرفة لو سقط سقط في بطن عرنة. وحكى الباجي عن ابن حبيب أن عرفة في الحل وعرنة في الحرم قوله : (حامداً مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً) أي قف حامداً إلى آخره لحديث مالك وغيره أفضل الموقف حتى روي عنه أنه عليه السلام دعا عشية عرفة لأمته بالمغفرة فاستجيب له إلا في الدماء والمظالم ثم أعاد الدعاء بالمزدلفة فأجيب حتى الدماء والمظالم. خرجه ابن ماجه طرفي الجبيلات الصغار التي كأنها الروابي الصغار عند جبل الرحمة وجعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بطن ناقته إلى الصخرات وجبل المشاة بين يديه واستقبل القبلة وكان موقفه عند النابت، قال الأزرقي : الفجوة التي خلف موقف الإمام وإن موقف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان على ضرس مضرس بين أحجار هناك ناتئة من جبل الأل. قال الفارسي قال قاضي القضاة بدر الدين: وقد اجتهدت على تعيين موقفه من جهات متعددة ووافقني عليه بعض من يعتمد عليه من محدثي مكة وعلمائها حتى حصل الظن بتعيينه وأنه الفجوة المستعلية المشرفة على الموقف التي عن يمينها ووراءها صخرة متصلة بصخرات الجبل، وهذه الفجوة بين الجبل والبناء المربع عن يساره وهي إلى الجبل أقرب بقليل بحيث يكون الجبل قبالتك بيمين إذا استقبلت القبلة والبناء المربع عن يسارك بقليل وراء، فإن ظفرت بموقف النبي الله فهو الغاية القصوى فلازمه ولا تفارقه، وإن خفي عليك فقف ما بين الجبل والبناء المذكور على جميع الصخرات السلام مراراً كثيرة وحصل لي منه خشوع عظيم، ويعرف بحذائه صخرة محروقة تتبع هي وما حولها من الصخرات المفروشة وما وراءها من الصخار السود المتصلة بالجبل هنا المطلوب ا هـ. كذا في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار قول المصنف : وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن عرنة) ظاهر هذا
His saying: (then to the standing place, stand near the mountain) i.e. then go, and what is meant by the mountain is Jabal al-Rahmah. His saying: (and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Arnah) due to the hadith of Bukhari: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and avoid Batn 'Arnah; and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid Batn Muhassir; and all the mountain paths of Mecca are places of sacrifice.' (1) And in al-Mughrib: 'Arnah is a valley alongside Arafat, and with its diminutive it is called 'Uraynah, to which the 'Uraniyun are attributed. Al-Qurtubi mentioned in his tafsir that it is with fatha on the ra' and dammah, west of the mosque of Arafat, so much so that some scholars said: 'If the western wall of the mosque of Arafat fell, it would fall into Batn 'Arnah.' Al-Baji reported from Ibn Habib that Arafat is in the open land (hilla) and 'Arnah is in the sacred precinct (haram). His saying: (praising, magnifying, hallowing, uttering talbiyah, praying, supplicating) i.e., stand praising, etc., due to the hadith of Malik and others: 'The best of supplication is the supplication of the day of Arafat, and the best of what I and the prophets before me have said is: La ilaha illa Allah, wahdahu la sharika lah, lahu al-mulk, wa lahu al-hamd, yuhyi wa yumit, wa huwa hayyun la yamut, biyadihi al-khayr, wa huwa 'ala kulli shay'in qadir.' And he (peace be upon him) would strive in supplication in this standing, so much so that it is narrated that he supplicated on the evening of Arafat for his ummah for forgiveness, and it was answered except for blood claims and injustices; then he repeated the supplication at Muzdalifah, and it was answered even for blood claims and injustices. Ibn Majah narrated it. (He stood) at the edge of the small hills that are like small mounds near Jabal al-Rahmah. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) placed the belly of his she-camel towards the rocks, and the mountain of the pedestrians was before him, and he faced the qiblah, and his standing place was at al-Nabit. Al-Azraqi said: 'The cleft behind the standing place of the Imam, and the standing place of the Prophet (peace be upon him) was on a jagged tooth among stones there protruding from Jabal al-Al.' Al-Farisi said, quoting Qadi al-Qudat Badr al-Din: 'I have exerted myself to determine his standing place from multiple directions, and some reliable scholars of Mecca agreed with me until I got a conjecture of its determination: that it is the elevated cleft overlooking the standing place, to its right and behind it a rock connected to the rocks of the mountain. This cleft is between the mountain and the square building to its left, and it is a bit closer to the mountain, so that the mountain is to your right when you face the qiblah, and the square building is slightly to your left and behind. So if you come upon the standing place of the Prophet (peace be upon him), that is the ultimate goal: stick to it and do not leave it. And if it is hidden from you, then stand between the mountain and the aforementioned building on all the rocks and places that are between them, sometimes on its plain and sometimes on its mountain, hoping that you may coincide with the Prophetic standing place.' Kama fi al-Murshidi 'ala al-Kanz. And Qadi Muhammad 'Id said: 'The square building is known as the kitchen of Adam (peace be upon him). I have stood at his standing place many times and experienced great humility. It is known by a burnt rock opposite it; follow it and its surroundings of the spread rocks and the black rocks behind them connected to the mountain. Here is the objective.' End quote. Kama fi Hashiyat al-Madani 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The author's saying: (And all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Arnah) the apparent meaning of this...
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the location of the standing (wuquf) at Arafat. It begins by interpreting the directive to stand near the mountain (Jabal al-Rahmah), then cites the hadith that all of Arafat is a valid standing place except the valley of 'Arnah. The commentary defines 'Arnah and explains its location west of the mosque of Arafat. It then discusses the recommended supplications and the Prophetic practice of supplicating intensely at Arafat. The bulk of the passage is a detailed description of the exact spot where the Prophet ﷺ stood, based on reports from al-Azraqi, al-Farisi, Qadi Badr al-Din, and others. The description includes landmarks such as a square building (known as the kitchen of Adam), a burnt rock, and the black rocks. The text concludes with advice for pilgrims to seek out the Prophetic standing place and, if unable, to stand in the general area between the mountain and the square building.

Key Terms
الموقف (al-mawqif): The specific place of standing (wuquf) at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; all of Arafat is mawqif except Batn 'Arnah.
بطن عرنة (batn 'arnah): A valley (wadi) west of the mosque of Arafat that is not part of Arafat; standing there is invalid.
جبل الرحمة (jabal al-rahmah): The mountain near which the Prophet ﷺ stood; it is recommended to stand near it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Batn 'Arnah
C) The area near the mosque of Arafat
D) The area near Jabal al-Rahmah

Key Takeaway
All of Arafat is valid for standing except Batn 'Arnah; the Prophet's spot is a sunnah, not a requirement.

The Valid Place of Wuquf at Arafat
Ruling and proof for the valid place of wuquf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid area for wuquf at Arafat and identify the excluded area according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is a standing place except the valley of Batin 'Arana.

The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that all of Arafat is a valid place for the essential standing (wuquf) during Hajj, with one exception: the valley of Batin 'Arana. This ruling is based on a famous hadith that defines the boundaries. In this lesson, we will examine the proof and the geographical clarification provided by the commentators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The ruling is that all of Arafat is a valid mawqif except Batin 'Arana. Confirm the hukm level: wuquf is a rukn (fard) of Hajj, but the exception is a condition for validity.
The exception is an exclusion from the general rule.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and avoid the valley of 'Arana.' This is narrated by Bukhari and others.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'ارتفعوا' (avoid) in the hadith creates an exception: standing in Batin 'Arana is not part of the valid wuquf. Thus, it is excluded.
The command to 'avoid' indicates prohibition of standing there.
4
Consider the geographical clarification
The commentary clarifies that Batin 'Arana is a valley adjacent to Arafat, with some scholars placing it within the Haram boundary. This physical distinction helps pilgrims know the exact limit.
The exact boundary is known by reference to the mosque of Arafat and the western wall.
5
Apply the ruling
A pilgrim must ensure they are within the boundaries of Arafat, avoiding the valley. If one stands in Batin 'Arana, the wuquf is invalid and Hajj is not fulfilled.
This is a condition for the validity of the rukn.

Source Text

بشرط الإمام والإحرام ثم إلى الموقف وقف بقرب الجبل وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن لا قوله : (وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن عرنة) لحديث البخارى عرفات كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة والمزدلفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن محسر وشعاب مكة كلها منحر (۱) وفي المغرب : عرنة واد بحذاء عرفات وبتصغيرها سميت عرينة ينسب إليها العرنيون. وذكر القرطبي في تفسيره أنها بفتح الراء وضمها بغربي مسجد عرفة حتى لقد قال بعض العلماء : إن الجدار الغربي من مسجد عرفة لو سقط سقط في بطن عرنة. وحكى الباجي عن ابن حبيب أن عرفة في الحل وعرنة في الحرم قوله : (حامداً مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً) أي قف حامداً إلى آخره لحديث مالك وغيره أفضل الدعاء دعاء يوم عرفة وأفضل ما قلته أنا والنبيون من قبلي لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له له الملك وله الحمد يحيي ويميت وهو حي يموت بيده الخير وهو على كل شيء قدير وكان عليه السلام يجتهد في الدعاء في هذا الموقف حتى روي عنه أنه عليه السلام دعا عشية عرفة لأمته بالمغفرة فاستجيب له إلا في الدماء والمظالم ثم أعاد الدعاء بالمزدلفة فأجيب حتى الدماء والمظالم. خرجه ابن ماجه طرفي الجبيلات الصغار التي كأنها الروابي الصغار عند جبل الرحمة وجعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بطن ناقته إلى الصخرات وجبل المشاة بين يديه واستقبل القبلة وكان موقفه عند النابت، قال الأزرقي : الفجوة التي خلف موقف الإمام وإن موقف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان على ضرس مضرس بين أحجار هناك ناتئة من جبل الأل. قال الفارسي قال قاضي القضاة بدر الدين: وقد اجتهدت على تعيين موقفه من جهات متعددة ووافقني عليه بعض من يعتمد عليه من محدثي مكة وعلمائها حتى حصل الظن بتعيينه وأنه الفجوة المستعلية المشرفة على الموقف التي عن يمينها ووراءها صخرة متصلة بصخرات الجبل، وهذه الفجوة بين الجبل والبناء المربع عن يساره وهي إلى الجبل أقرب بقليل بحيث يكون الجبل قبالتك بيمين إذا استقبلت القبلة والبناء المربع عن يسارك بقليل وراء، فإن ظفرت بموقف النبي الله فهو الغاية القصوى فلازمه ولا تفارقه، وإن خفي عليك فقف ما بين الجبل والبناء المذكور على جميع الصخرات والأماكن التي بينهما وعلى سهلها تارة وعلى جبلها تارة لعلك أن تصادف الموقف النبوي. كذا في المرشدي على الكنز. وقال القاضي محمد عيد والبناء المربع هو المعروف بمطبخ آدم عليه السلام وقد وقفت بموقفه عليه السلام مراراً كثيرة وحصل لي منه خشوع عظيم، ويعرف بحذائه صخرة محروقة تتبع هي وما حولها من الصخرات المفروشة وما وراءها من الصخار السود المتصلة بالجبل هنا المطلوب ا هـ. كذا في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار قول المصنف : (وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن عرنة) ظاهر هذا والنابت هم (۱) رواه مسلم في كتاب الحج حديث ١٤٩ أبو داود في كتاب المناسك باب ٥٦. الترمذي في كتاب الحج باب ٥٤. النسائي في كتاب المناسك باب ٢٠٢ الموطأ في كتاب الحج حديث ١٦٦. أحمد في مسنده (١/ ٧٢، ٧٥، ٧٦). وهكذا إلى آخر الحديث المذكور. ثم قال: وهو ضعيف بالعباس بن مرادس فإنه منكر الحديث ساقط الاحتجاج كما ذكره الحفاظ لكن له شواهد كثيرة، فمنها ما رواه أحمد بإسناد صحيح عن ابن عباس قال: كان فلان ردف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم عرفة فجعل الفتى يلاحظ النساء وينظر إليهن فقال له النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : ابن أخي إن هذا يوم من ملك فيه سمعه وبصره غفر له ومنها ما رواه البخاري مرفوعاً من حج فلم يرفث ولم يفسق خرج من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته أمه ومنها ما رواه مسلم في صحيحه مرفوعاً «إن الإسلام يهدم ما كان قبله وإن الهجرة تهدم ما كان قبلها، وإن الحج يهدم ما كان قبله (١) ومنها ما رواه مالك في الموطأ مرفوعاً «ما رؤي الشيطان يوماً هو أصغير ولا أدخر ولا أغيظ منه في يوم عرفة وما ذاك إلا لما يرى من تنزل الرحمة وتجاوز الله تعالى عن الذنوب العظام إلا ما رؤي يوم بدر فإنه رأى جبريل يزع الملائكة» (٢) فإنها تقتضي تكفير الصغائر والكبائر ولو كانت من حقوق العباد لكن ذكر الأكمل في شرح المشارق أن الإسلام يهدم ما كان قبله أن المقصود أن الذنوب السالفة تحبط بالإسلام والهجرة والحج صغيره كانت أو كبيرة وتتناول حقوق الله وحقوق العباد بالنسبة إلى الحربي حتى لو أسلم لا يطالب بشيء منها حتى لو كان قتل وأخذ المال وأحرزه بدار الحرب ثم أسلم لا يؤاخذ بشيء من ذلك، وعلى هذا كان الإسلام كافياً في تحصيل مراده ولكن ذكر صلى الله عليه وسلم الهجرة والحج تأكيداً في بشارته وترغيباً في مبايعته فإن الهجرة والحج لا يكفران المظالم ولا يقطع فيهما بمحو الكبائر وإنما يكفران الصغائر. ويجوز أن يقال والكبائر التي ليست من حقوق العباد أيضاً كالإسلام من أهل الذمة وحينئذ لا يشك أن ذكرهما كان للتأكيد ا هـ . وهكذا ذكر الإمام الطيبي في شرح هذا الحديث وقال : إن الشارحين اتفقوا عليه. وهكذا ذكر الإمام النووي والقرطبي في شرح مسلم. وذكر القاضي عياض أن أهل السنة أجمعوا على أن الكبائر لا يكفرها إلا التوبة. فالحاصل أن المسألة ظنية وأن الحج لا يقطع فيه بتكفير الكبائر من حقوق الله تعالى فضلاً عن حقوق العباد وإن قلنا بالتكفير للكل فليس معناه كما يتوهمه كثير من الناس أن الدين يسقط عنه وكذا قضاء الصلوات والصيامات والزكاة إذ لم يقل أحد بذلك، وإنما المراد وكذا قوله في مزدلفة وهي موقف إلا بطن محسر أن المكانين ليسا بمكان وقوف فلا يجزئ فيهما كما سيأتي . قوله : (تحبط بالإسلام والهجرة والحج أي بمجموع الثلاثة لا بكل واحد على انفراده قوله : (١) رواه مسلم في كتاب الإيمان حديث ١٩٢. (٢) رواه في الموطأ في كتاب الحج حديث ٢٤٥.
With the condition of the imam and ihram, then proceed to the standing place, stand near the mountain, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batin (Arana). His statement: (And all of Arafat is a standing place except Batin 'Arana) due to the hadith of Bukhari: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and avoid the valley of 'Arana, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir, and all the mountain passes of Mecca are places of sacrifice.' (1) And in al-Mughrib: 'Arana is a valley adjacent to Arafat, and its diminutive is 'Uraynah, attributed to the 'Uraniyyun. Al-Qurtubi mentioned in his Tafsir that it is with fathah and dammah to the west of the mosque of Arafat, to the extent that some scholars said: If the western wall of the mosque of Arafat fell, it would fall into the valley of 'Arana. Al-Baji reported from Ibn Habib that Arafat is in al-Hill and 'Arana is in al-Haram. His statement: (praising, declaring greatness, declaring unity, declaring talbiyah, praying, supplicating) i.e., stand praising etc., due to the hadith of Malik and others: 'The best supplication is the supplication of the day of Arafah, and the best thing I and the prophets before me have said is: La ilaha illa Allah, alone without partner, to Him belongs the dominion and to Him belongs praise, He gives life and causes death, and He is living and does not die, in His hand is good, and He is over all things capable.' And he (peace be upon him) used to strive in supplication in this standing place until it is narrated that he supplicated on the evening of Arafah for his ummah for forgiveness, and it was answered except for bloods and injustices, then he repeated the supplication at Muzdalifah and it was answered even for bloods and injustices. Ibn Majah narrated it. The small hills at the foot of the Mount of Mercy, which look like small mounds, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) placed the belly of his she-camel towards the rocks, and the mountain of the walkers in front of him, and he faced the Qibla, and his standing place was at al-Nabit. Al-Azraqi said: The gap behind the imam's standing place, and the Prophet's standing place was on a rugged tooth between stones protruding from Jabal al-Al. Al-Farisi said that Qadi al-Qudat Badr al-Din said: I have endeavored to determine his standing place from multiple directions, and some reliable scholars of Mecca agreed with me until I obtained a probable determination: it is the elevated gap overlooking the standing place, to its right and behind it a rock connected to the mountain rocks, and this gap is between the mountain and the square building to its left, and it is slightly closer to the mountain, such that the mountain is to your right when facing the Qibla and the square building is slightly to your left and behind. If you find the Prophet's standing place, that is the ultimate goal, so adhere to it and do not leave it. And if it is hidden from you, stand between the mountain and the mentioned building on all the rocks and the places between them, sometimes on its plain and sometimes on its mountain, hoping that you may coincide with the prophetic standing place. Thus in al-Murshidi 'ala al-Kanz. And al-Qadi Muhammad 'Aid said: The square building is known as the Kitchen of Adam (peace be upon him), and I have stood at his (the Prophet's) standing place many times and experienced great humility. It is known by a burned rock that follows it and its surrounding scattered rocks and the black rocks beyond connected to the mountain; here is the sought goal. End quote. Thus in Hashiyat al-Madani 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The author's statement: (And all of Arafat is a standing place except Batin 'Arana) apparently this... and al-Nabit... (1) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Hajj, hadith 149; Abu Dawud in the Book of Rituals, chapter 56; al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Hajj, chapter 54; al-Nasa'i in the Book of Rituals, chapter 202; al-Muwatta in the Book of Hajj, hadith 166; Ahmad in his Musnad (1/72, 75, 76). And so on to the end of the mentioned hadith. Then he said: It is weak due to al-Abbas ibn Mirdas, for he is a munkar hadith, rejected in evidence as the memorizers mentioned, but it has many supporting evidences, including what Ahmad narrated with a sound chain from Ibn 'Abbas: A young man was riding behind the Messenger of Allah on the day of Arafah, and he kept looking at women, so the Prophet said: 'O son of my brother, this is a day whoever controls his hearing and sight will be forgiven.' And including what al-Bukhari narrated marfu': 'Whoever performs Hajj and does not engage in obscenity or immorality will return from his sins like the day his mother bore him.' And including what Muslim narrated in his Sahih marfu': 'Islam destroys what was before it, and hijrah destroys what was before it, and Hajj destroys what was before it.' (1) And including what Malik narrated in al-Muwatta marfu': 'The devil is not seen on any day smaller, more humiliated, or angrier than on the day of Arafah, and that is only due to the descent of mercy and Allah's overlooking of great sins, except on the day of Badr, for he saw Jibril arranging the angels.' (2) These imply expiation of minor and major sins, even if they are rights of the servants. However, al-Akmal mentioned in Sharh al-Mashariq that 'Islam destroys what was before it' means that previous sins are nullified by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj, whether minor or major, and they include rights of Allah and rights of servants with respect to a harbi, such that if he embraces Islam, he is not held accountable for anything, even if he killed, took wealth, and stored it in dar al-harb, then embraced Islam, he is not taken to task for any of that. Based on this, Islam alone would suffice to achieve this, but the Prophet mentioned hijrah and Hajj as an emphasis in his good tidings and encouragement to embrace his message, for hijrah and Hajj do not expiate injustices nor are they decisively established to erase major sins; rather, they expiate minor sins. It is possible to say that major sins that are not rights of servants are also included, like the Islam of a dhimmi, and then there is no doubt that their mention was for emphasis. End quote. Thus Imam al-Tibi mentioned in his commentary on this hadith and said that the commentators agreed upon it. Thus Imam al-Nawawi and al-Qurtubi mentioned in Sharh Muslim. And Qadi 'Iyad mentioned that Ahl al-Sunnah are unanimously agreed that major sins are only expiated by repentance. The conclusion is that the issue is speculative, and Hajj is not decisively established to expiate major sins from the rights of Allah, let alone rights of the servants. And if we accept expiation for all, it does not mean, as many people assume, that debts are dropped from him, nor the making up of prayers, fasts, and zakat, for no one has said that. Rather, the meaning is... and likewise his statement about Muzdalifah that it is a standing place except Batin Muhassir, that the two places are not places of standing, so they are not sufficient as will come. His statement: (It destroys by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj) i.e., by the three together, not by each one individually. (1) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Faith, hadith 192. (2) Narrated in al-Muwatta in the Book of Hajj, hadith 245.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a portion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering two main rulings: (1) the valid place for wuquf (standing) at Arafat, and (2) the recommended actions during the standing, including a detailed discussion on the expiation of sins through Hajj. The commentator follows the order of the matn, first explaining that all of Arafat is a valid standing place for Hajj except the valley of Batin 'Arana. The proof is the famous hadith from Bukhari, which is also narrated by several other hadith collections. The commentary then provides geographical clarifications: 'Arana is a valley adjacent to Arafat, and some scholars place it within the Haram boundary, while Arafat itself is in the Hill. The second part addresses the actions recommended during wuquf: praising Allah (hamd), magnifying Him (takbir), declaring His oneness (tahlil), reciting the talbiyah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and making supplication (dua). The best dua on this day is 'La ilaha illa Allah...' as narrated by Malik. The commentary then recounts a story about the Prophet's intense supplication on the day of Arafah, emphasizing that he supplicated for his ummah and was answered, except for matters of blood and injustices; he repeated the dua at Muzdalifah and was answered fully. This leads into a lengthy discussion about the hadiths that mention Hajj expiating sins. The commentator clarifies that the apparent meaning of these hadiths might suggest that Haj wipes out all sins, major and minor, even rights of others. However, the reliable Hanafi position, supported by scholars like al-Akmal, al-Tibi, al-Nawawi, al-Qurtubi, and Qadi 'Iyad, is that this applies fully only to a former harbi (enemy combatant) who embraces Islam, for whom previous crimes are waived. For Muslims, Hajj expiates minor sins but not major sins (kaba'ir) nor rights of the servants (mazalim). Major sins require sincere repentance (tawbah), and debts, missed prayers, fasts, and zakat remain obligations that are not automatically forgiven by Hajj. The commentator concludes that the issue is speculative (zanni), not definitive, and that one should not assume Hajj absolves one of all responsibilities. The passage ends by returning to the matn reference to Muzdalifah as a standing place, excluding Batin Muhassir, and emphasizing that the expiation mentioned in the hadith is achieved collectively by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj, not by any one act alone.

Key Terms
بطن عرنة (Baṭn ʿArana): A valley near Arafat that is excluded from the valid place of wuquf during Hajj.
موقف (mawqif): The place of standing during the Hajj on the day of Arafah, a key rite.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which area is excluded from the valid place of wuquf at Arafat?
A) The entire plain of Arafat
B) The valley of Batin 'Arana
C) The mountain of mercy
D) The valley of Muhassir

Key Takeaway
All of Arafat is a valid standing place for Hajj except the valley of Batin 'Arana, based on a clear hadith.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
5 min
Recommended Dhikr During Wuquf
Recommended acts of worship during wuquf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended actions during wuquf at Arafat and state the best supplication on that day.

Core Idea
The best supplication on the day of Arafah is 'La ilaha illa Allah...' as narrated by the Prophet.

During the standing at Arafat, the Prophet recommended specific acts of worship: praising Allah, magnifying Him, declaring His oneness, reciting talbiyah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and making supplication. Among these, the best dua is the one he and the prophets before him said. This lesson covers those recommendations and the story of the Prophet's intense supplication for his ummah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
The matn lists: praising (hamd), magnifying (takbir), declaring oneness (tahlil), reciting talbiyah, sending blessings (salawat), and supplication (dua). All are mustahabb during wuquf.
These are sunnah, not wajib.
2
Highlight the best dua
The best dua is 'La ilaha illa Allah...' as mentioned in the hadith of Malik. This is the most excellent supplication on this day.
The full phrase includes praise and acknowledgment of Allah's attributes.
3
Reflect on the Prophet's example
The Prophet strived in dua on that day, even supplicating for his ummah. He was answered except for blood and injustices, and later at Muzdalifah it was fully answered.
This shows the immense virtue of the day and the importance of earnest supplication.
4
Understand the significance
The day of Arafah is the best day for dua, and these specific dhikr are recommended by the Prophet.
Pilgrims should focus on these acts.

الجدار الغربي من مسجد عرفة لو سقط سقط في بطن عرنة. وحكى الباجي عن ابن حبيب أن عرفة في الحل وعرنة في الحرم قوله : (حامداً مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً) أي قف حامداً إلى آخره لحديث مالك وغيره أفضل الروابي الصغار عند جبل الرحمة وجعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بطن ناقته إلى الصخرات وجبل المشاة بين يديه واستقبل القبلة وكان موقفه عند النابت، قال الأزرقي : الفجوة التي خلف موقف الإمام وإن موقف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان على ضرس مضرس بين أحجار هناك ناتئة من جبل الأل. قال الفارسي قال قاضي القضاة بدر الدين: وقد اجتهدت على تعيين موقفه من جهات متعددة ووافقني عليه بعض من يعتمد عليه من محدثي مكة وعلمائها حتى حصل الظن بتعيينه وأنه الفجوة المستعلية المشرفة على الموقف التي عن يمينها ووراءها صخرة متصلة بصخرات الجبل، وهذه الفجوة بين الجبل والبناء المربع عن يساره وهي إلى الجبل أقرب بقليل بحيث يكون الجبل قبالتك بيمين إذا استقبلت القبلة والبناء المربع عن يسارك بقليل وراء، فإن ظفرت بموقف النبي الله فهو الغاية القصوى فلازمه ولا تفارقه، وإن خفي عليك فقف ما بين الجبل والبناء المذكور على جميع الصخرات والأماكن التي بينهما وعلى سهلها تارة وعلى جبلها تارة لعلك أن تصادف الموقف النبوي. كذا في المرشدي على الكنز. وقال القاضي محمد عيد والبناء المربع هو المعروف بمطبخ آدم عليه السلام وقد وقفت بموقفه عليه السلام مراراً كثيرة وحصل لي منه خشوع عظيم، ويعرف بحذائه صخرة محروقة تتبع هي وما حولها من الصخرات المفروشة وما وراءها من الصخار السود المتصلة بالجبل هنا المطلوب ا هـ. كذا في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار قول المصنف : (وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن عرنة) ظاهر هذا والنابت هم (۱) رواه مسلم في كتاب الحج حديث ١٤٩ أبو داود في كتاب المناسك باب ٥٦. الترمذي في كتاب الحج باب ٥٤. النسائي في كتاب المناسك باب ٢٠٢ الموطأ في كتاب الحج حديث ١٦٦. أحمد في مسنده (١/ ٧٢، ٧٥، ٧٦). وهكذا إلى آخر الحديث المذكور. ثم قال: وهو ضعيف بالعباس بن مرادس فإنه منكر الحديث ساقط الاحتجاج كما ذكره الحفاظ لكن له شواهد كثيرة، فمنها ما رواه أحمد بإسناد صحيح عن ابن عباس قال: كان فلان ردف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم عرفة فجعل الفتى يلاحظ النساء وينظر إليهن فقال له النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : ابن أخي إن هذا يوم من ملك فيه سمعه وبصره غفر له ومنها ما رواه البخاري مرفوعاً من حج فلم يرفث ولم يفسق خرج من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته أمه ومنها ما رواه مسلم في صحيحه مرفوعاً «إن الإسلام يهدم ما كان قبله وإن الهجرة تهدم ما كان قبلها، وإن الحج يهدم ما كان قبله (١) ومنها ما رواه مالك في الموطأ مرفوعاً «ما رؤي الشيطان يوماً هو أصغير ولا أدخر ولا أغيظ منه في يوم عرفة وما ذاك إلا لما يرى من تنزل الرحمة وتجاوز الله تعالى عن الذنوب العظام إلا ما رؤي يوم بدر فإنه رأى جبريل يزع الملائكة» (٢) فإنها تقتضي تكفير الصغائر والكبائر ولو كانت من حقوق العباد لكن ذكر الأكمل في شرح المشارق أن الإسلام يهدم ما كان قبله أن المقصود أن الذنوب السالفة تحبط بالإسلام والهجرة والحج صغيره كانت أو كبيرة وتتناول حقوق الله وحقوق العباد بالنسبة إلى الحربي حتى لو أسلم لا يطالب بشيء منها حتى لو كان قتل وأخذ المال وأحرزه بدار الحرب ثم أسلم لا يؤاخذ بشيء من ذلك، وعلى هذا كان الإسلام كافياً في تحصيل مراده ولكن ذكر صلى الله عليه وسلم الهجرة والحج تأكيداً في بشارته وترغيباً في مبايعته فإن الهجرة والحج لا يكفران المظالم ولا يقطع فيهما بمحو الكبائر وإنما يكفران الصغائر. ويجوز أن يقال والكبائر التي ليست من حقوق العباد أيضاً كالإسلام من أهل الذمة وحينئذ لا يشك أن ذكرهما كان للتأكيد ا هـ . وهكذا ذكر الإمام الطيبي في شرح هذا الحديث وقال : إن الشارحين اتفقوا عليه. وهكذا ذكر الإمام النووي والقرطبي في شرح مسلم. وذكر القاضي عياض أن أهل السنة أجمعوا على أن الكبائر لا يكفرها إلا التوبة. فالحاصل أن المسألة ظنية وأن الحج لا يقطع فيه بتكفير الكبائر من حقوق الله تعالى فضلاً عن حقوق العباد وإن قلنا بالتكفير للكل فليس معناه كما يتوهمه كثير من الناس أن الدين يسقط عنه وكذا قضاء الصلوات والصيامات والزكاة إذ لم يقل أحد بذلك، وإنما المراد وكذا قوله في مزدلفة وهي موقف إلا بطن محسر أن المكانين ليسا بمكان وقوف فلا يجزئ فيهما كما سيأتي . قوله : (تحبط بالإسلام والهجرة والحج أي بمجموع الثلاثة لا بكل واحد على انفراده قوله : (١) رواه مسلم في كتاب الإيمان حديث ١٩٢. (٢) رواه في الموطأ في كتاب الحج حديث ٢٤٥.
With the condition of the imam and ihram, then proceed to the standing place, stand near the mountain, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batin (Arana). His statement: (And all of Arafat is a standing place except Batin 'Arana) due to the hadith of Bukhari: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and avoid the valley of 'Arana, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir, and all the mountain passes of Mecca are places of sacrifice.' (1) And in al-Mughrib: 'Arana is a valley adjacent to Arafat, and its diminutive is 'Uraynah, attributed to the 'Uraniyyun. Al-Qurtubi mentioned in his Tafsir that it is with fathah and dammah to the west of the mosque of Arafat, to the extent that some scholars said: If the western wall of the mosque of Arafat fell, it would fall into the valley of 'Arana. Al-Baji reported from Ibn Habib that Arafat is in al-Hill and 'Arana is in al-Haram. His statement: (praising, declaring greatness, declaring unity, declaring talbiyah, praying, supplicating) i.e., stand praising etc., due to the hadith of Malik and others: 'The best supplication is the supplication of the day of Arafah, and the best thing I and the prophets before me have said is: La ilaha illa Allah, alone without partner, to Him belongs the dominion and to Him belongs praise, He gives life and causes death, and He is living and does not die, in His hand is good, and He is over all things capable.' And he (peace be upon him) used to strive in supplication in this standing place until it is narrated that he supplicated on the evening of Arafah for his ummah for forgiveness, and it was answered except for bloods and injustices, then he repeated the supplication at Muzdalifah and it was answered even for bloods and injustices. Ibn Majah narrated it. The small hills at the foot of the Mount of Mercy, which look like small mounds, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) placed the belly of his she-camel towards the rocks, and the mountain of the walkers in front of him, and he faced the Qibla, and his standing place was at al-Nabit. Al-Azraqi said: The gap behind the imam's standing place, and the Prophet's standing place was on a rugged tooth between stones protruding from Jabal al-Al. Al-Farisi said that Qadi al-Qudat Badr al-Din said: I have endeavored to determine his standing place from multiple directions, and some reliable scholars of Mecca agreed with me until I obtained a probable determination: it is the elevated gap overlooking the standing place, to its right and behind it a rock connected to the mountain rocks, and this gap is between the mountain and the square building to its left, and it is slightly closer to the mountain, such that the mountain is to your right when facing the Qibla and the square building is slightly to your left and behind. If you find the Prophet's standing place, that is the ultimate goal, so adhere to it and do not leave it. And if it is hidden from you, stand between the mountain and the mentioned building on all the rocks and the places between them, sometimes on its plain and sometimes on its mountain, hoping that you may coincide with the prophetic standing place. Thus in al-Murshidi 'ala al-Kanz. And al-Qadi Muhammad 'Aid said: The square building is known as the Kitchen of Adam (peace be upon him), and I have stood at his (the Prophet's) standing place many times and experienced great humility. It is known by a burned rock that follows it and its surrounding scattered rocks and the black rocks beyond connected to the mountain; here is the sought goal. End quote. Thus in Hashiyat al-Madani 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The author's statement: (And all of Arafat is a standing place except Batin 'Arana) apparently this... and al-Nabit... (1) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Hajj, hadith 149; Abu Dawud in the Book of Rituals, chapter 56; al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Hajj, chapter 54; al-Nasa'i in the Book of Rituals, chapter 202; al-Muwatta in the Book of Hajj, hadith 166; Ahmad in his Musnad (1/72, 75, 76). And so on to the end of the mentioned hadith. Then he said: It is weak due to al-Abbas ibn Mirdas, for he is a munkar hadith, rejected in evidence as the memorizers mentioned, but it has many supporting evidences, including what Ahmad narrated with a sound chain from Ibn 'Abbas: A young man was riding behind the Messenger of Allah on the day of Arafah, and he kept looking at women, so the Prophet said: 'O son of my brother, this is a day whoever controls his hearing and sight will be forgiven.' And including what al-Bukhari narrated marfu': 'Whoever performs Hajj and does not engage in obscenity or immorality will return from his sins like the day his mother bore him.' And including what Muslim narrated in his Sahih marfu': 'Islam destroys what was before it, and hijrah destroys what was before it, and Hajj destroys what was before it.' (1) And including what Malik narrated in al-Muwatta marfu': 'The devil is not seen on any day smaller, more humiliated, or angrier than on the day of Arafah, and that is only due to the descent of mercy and Allah's overlooking of great sins, except on the day of Badr, for he saw Jibril arranging the angels.' (2) These imply expiation of minor and major sins, even if they are rights of the servants. However, al-Akmal mentioned in Sharh al-Mashariq that 'Islam destroys what was before it' means that previous sins are nullified by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj, whether minor or major, and they include rights of Allah and rights of servants with respect to a harbi, such that if he embraces Islam, he is not held accountable for anything, even if he killed, took wealth, and stored it in dar al-harb, then embraced Islam, he is not taken to task for any of that. Based on this, Islam alone would suffice to achieve this, but the Prophet mentioned hijrah and Hajj as an emphasis in his good tidings and encouragement to embrace his message, for hijrah and Hajj do not expiate injustices nor are they decisively established to erase major sins; rather, they expiate minor sins. It is possible to say that major sins that are not rights of servants are also included, like the Islam of a dhimmi, and then there is no doubt that their mention was for emphasis. End quote. Thus Imam al-Tibi mentioned in his commentary on this hadith and said that the commentators agreed upon it. Thus Imam al-Nawawi and al-Qurtubi mentioned in Sharh Muslim. And Qadi 'Iyad mentioned that Ahl al-Sunnah are unanimously agreed that major sins are only expiated by repentance. The conclusion is that the issue is speculative, and Hajj is not decisively established to expiate major sins from the rights of Allah, let alone rights of the servants. And if we accept expiation for all, it does not mean, as many people assume, that debts are dropped from him, nor the making up of prayers, fasts, and zakat, for no one has said that. Rather, the meaning is... and likewise his statement about Muzdalifah that it is a standing place except Batin Muhassir, that the two places are not places of standing, so they are not sufficient as will come. His statement: (It destroys by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj) i.e., by the three together, not by each one individually. (1) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Faith, hadith 192. (2) Narrated in al-Muwatta in the Book of Hajj, hadith 245.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a portion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering two main rulings: (1) the valid place for wuquf (standing) at Arafat, and (2) the recommended actions during the standing, including a detailed discussion on the expiation of sins through Hajj. The commentator follows the order of the matn, first explaining that all of Arafat is a valid standing place for Hajj except the valley of Batin 'Arana. The proof is the famous hadith from Bukhari, which is also narrated by several other hadith collections. The commentary then provides geographical clarifications: 'Arana is a valley adjacent to Arafat, and some scholars place it within the Haram boundary, while Arafat itself is in the Hill. The second part addresses the actions recommended during wuquf: praising Allah (hamd), magnifying Him (takbir), declaring His oneness (tahlil), reciting the talbiyah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and making supplication (dua). The best dua on this day is 'La ilaha illa Allah...' as narrated by Malik. The commentary then recounts a story about the Prophet's intense supplication on the day of Arafah, emphasizing that he supplicated for his ummah and was answered, except for matters of blood and injustices; he repeated the dua at Muzdalifah and was answered fully. This leads into a lengthy discussion about the hadiths that mention Hajj expiating sins. The commentator clarifies that the apparent meaning of these hadiths might suggest that Haj wipes out all sins, major and minor, even rights of others. However, the reliable Hanafi position, supported by scholars like al-Akmal, al-Tibi, al-Nawawi, al-Qurtubi, and Qadi 'Iyad, is that this applies fully only to a former harbi (enemy combatant) who embraces Islam, for whom previous crimes are waived. For Muslims, Hajj expiates minor sins but not major sins (kaba'ir) nor rights of the servants (mazalim). Major sins require sincere repentance (tawbah), and debts, missed prayers, fasts, and zakat remain obligations that are not automatically forgiven by Hajj. The commentator concludes that the issue is speculative (zanni), not definitive, and that one should not assume Hajj absolves one of all responsibilities. The passage ends by returning to the matn reference to Muzdalifah as a standing place, excluding Batin Muhassir, and emphasizing that the expiation mentioned in the hadith is achieved collectively by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj, not by any one act alone.

Key Terms
أفضل الدعاء (afḍal al-duʿā’): The best supplication, which on the day of Arafah is the phrase taught by the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which phrase is considered the best supplication on the day of Arafah according to the hadith cited in the lesson?
A) La ilaha illa Allah Muhammad Rasul Allah
B) La ilaha illa Allah wahdahu la sharika lah...
C) Subhan Allah wa bihamdih
D) Allahumma inni as'aluka al-Jannah

Key Takeaway
The recommended acts during wuquf include hamd, takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and dua; the best dua is the specific phrase taught by the Prophet.
