Hajj — Pilgrimage
advanced
8 min
The Expiation of Sins through Hajj: Hanafi Clarification
Clarification on the scope of expiation through Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the extent of expiation of sins through Hajj and distinguish between minor sins, major sins, and rights of others.

Core Idea
Hajj expiates minor sins but not major sins or debts; major sins require sincere repentance.

Many hadiths promise great forgiveness for one who performs Hajj properly, including that it destroys sins. However, the Hanafi scholars clarify that this applies fully only to a former harbi (enemy combatant) who embraces Islam; for Muslims, Hajj expiates minor sins. Major sins and rights of others (mazalim) require separate repentance and fulfillment. This lesson unpacks the commentary from the text and the consensus among major commentators.

Guided Path
1
Examine the hadith on destruction
The hadith states: 'Islam destroys what was before it, hijrah destroys what was before it, and Hajj destroys what was before it.' Understand the apparent generalization.
The word 'yahdim' suggests complete annulment.
2
Identify the Hanafi interpretation
The commentator explains that this complete annulment applies to a former harbi (non-Muslim combatant) who embraces Islam – all past sins and even crimes are waived. For a Muslim, Hajj and hijrah only expiate minor sins, not major sins or debts.
This is based on the distinction in the status of the person.
3
Review the scholarly consensus
The text cites al-Akmal, al-Tibi, al-Nawawi, al-Qurtubi, and Qadi 'Iyad agreeing that major sins are only expiated by repentance (tawbah). This is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah.
Thus, the apparent meaning of the hadith is qualified.
4
Apply the ruling
A pilgrim should not assume that Hajj automatically clears all dues, like missed prayers, zakat, or debts. These remain obligations unless fulfilled or forgiven.
The issue is speculative (zanni), but the safer view is the qualified one.

بشرط الإمام والإحرام ثم إلى الموقف وقف بقرب الجبل وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن لا قوله : (وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن عرنة) لحديث البخارى عرفات كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة والمزدلفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن محسر وشعاب مكة كلها منحر (۱) وفي المغرب : عرنة واد بحذاء عرفات وبتصغيرها سميت عرينة ينسب إليها العرنيون. وذكر القرطبي في تفسيره أنها بفتح الراء وضمها بغربي مسجد عرفة حتى لقد قال بعض العلماء : إن الجدار الغربي من مسجد عرفة لو سقط سقط في بطن عرنة. وحكى الباجي عن ابن حبيب أن عرفة في الحل وعرنة في الحرم قوله : (حامداً مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً) أي قف حامداً إلى آخره لحديث مالك وغيره أفضل الدعاء دعاء يوم عرفة وأفضل ما قلته أنا والنبيون من قبلي لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له له الملك وله الحمد يحيي ويميت وهو حي يموت بيده الخير وهو على كل شيء قدير وكان عليه السلام يجتهد في الدعاء في هذا الموقف حتى روي عنه أنه عليه السلام دعا عشية عرفة لأمته بالمغفرة فاستجيب له إلا في الدماء والمظالم ثم أعاد الدعاء بالمزدلفة فأجيب حتى الدماء والمظالم. خرجه ابن ماجه طرفي الجبيلات الصغار التي كأنها الروابي الصغار عند جبل الرحمة وجعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بطن ناقته إلى الصخرات وجبل المشاة بين يديه واستقبل القبلة وكان موقفه عند النابت، قال الأزرقي : الفجوة التي خلف موقف الإمام وإن موقف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان على ضرس مضرس بين أحجار هناك ناتئة من جبل الأل. قال الفارسي قال قاضي القضاة بدر الدين: وقد اجتهدت على تعيين موقفه من جهات متعددة ووافقني عليه بعض من يعتمد عليه من محدثي مكة وعلمائها حتى حصل الظن بتعيينه وأنه الفجوة المستعلية المشرفة على الموقف التي عن يمينها ووراءها صخرة متصلة بصخرات الجبل، وهذه الفجوة بين الجبل والبناء المربع عن يساره وهي إلى الجبل أقرب بقليل بحيث يكون الجبل قبالتك بيمين إذا استقبلت القبلة والبناء المربع عن يسارك بقليل وراء، فإن ظفرت بموقف النبي الله فهو الغاية القصوى فلازمه ولا تفارقه، وإن خفي عليك فقف ما بين الجبل والبناء المذكور على جميع الصخرات والأماكن التي بينهما وعلى سهلها تارة وعلى جبلها تارة لعلك أن تصادف الموقف النبوي. كذا في المرشدي على الكنز. وقال القاضي محمد عيد والبناء المربع هو المعروف بمطبخ آدم عليه السلام وقد وقفت بموقفه عليه السلام مراراً كثيرة وحصل لي منه خشوع عظيم، ويعرف بحذائه صخرة محروقة تتبع هي وما حولها من الصخرات المفروشة وما وراءها من الصخار السود المتصلة بالجبل هنا المطلوب ا هـ. كذا في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار قول المصنف : (وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن عرنة) ظاهر هذا والنابت هم (۱) رواه مسلم في كتاب الحج حديث ١٤٩ أبو داود في كتاب المناسك باب ٥٦. الترمذي في كتاب الحج باب ٥٤. النسائي في كتاب المناسك باب ٢٠٢ الموطأ في كتاب الحج حديث ١٦٦. أحمد في مسنده (١/ ٧٢، ٧٥، ٧٦). وهكذا إلى آخر الحديث المذكور. ثم قال: وهو ضعيف بالعباس بن مرادس فإنه منكر الحديث ساقط الاحتجاج كما ذكره الحفاظ لكن له شواهد كثيرة، فمنها ما رواه أحمد بإسناد صحيح عن ابن عباس قال: كان فلان ردف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم عرفة فجعل الفتى يلاحظ النساء وينظر إليهن فقال له النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : ابن أخي إن هذا يوم من ملك فيه سمعه وبصره غفر له ومنها ما رواه البخاري مرفوعاً من حج فلم يرفث ولم يفسق خرج من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته أمه ومنها ما رواه مسلم في صحيحه مرفوعاً «إن الإسلام يهدم ما كان قبله وإن الهجرة تهدم ما كان قبلها، وإن الحج يهدم ما كان قبله (١) ومنها ما رواه مالك في الموطأ مرفوعاً «ما رؤي الشيطان يوماً هو أصغير ولا أدخر ولا أغيظ منه في يوم عرفة وما ذاك إلا لما يرى من تنزل الرحمة وتجاوز الله تعالى عن الذنوب العظام إلا ما رؤي يوم بدر فإنه رأى جبريل يزع الملائكة» (٢) فإنها تقتضي تكفير الصغائر والكبائر ولو كانت من حقوق العباد لكن ذكر الأكمل في شرح المشارق أن الإسلام يهدم ما كان قبله أن المقصود أن الذنوب السالفة تحبط بالإسلام والهجرة والحج صغيره كانت أو كبيرة وتتناول حقوق الله وحقوق العباد بالنسبة إلى الحربي حتى لو أسلم لا يطالب بشيء منها حتى لو كان قتل وأخذ المال وأحرزه بدار الحرب ثم أسلم لا يؤاخذ بشيء من ذلك، وعلى هذا كان الإسلام كافياً في تحصيل مراده ولكن ذكر صلى الله عليه وسلم الهجرة والحج تأكيداً في بشارته وترغيباً في مبايعته فإن الهجرة والحج لا يكفران المظالم ولا يقطع فيهما بمحو الكبائر وإنما يكفران الصغائر. ويجوز أن يقال والكبائر التي ليست من حقوق العباد أيضاً كالإسلام من أهل الذمة وحينئذ لا يشك أن ذكرهما كان للتأكيد ا هـ . وهكذا ذكر الإمام الطيبي في شرح هذا الحديث وقال : إن الشارحين اتفقوا عليه. وهكذا ذكر الإمام النووي والقرطبي في شرح مسلم. وذكر القاضي عياض أن أهل السنة أجمعوا على أن الكبائر لا يكفرها إلا التوبة. فالحاصل أن المسألة ظنية وأن الحج لا يقطع فيه بتكفير الكبائر من حقوق الله تعالى فضلاً عن حقوق العباد وإن قلنا بالتكفير للكل فليس معناه كما يتوهمه كثير من الناس أن الدين يسقط عنه وكذا قضاء الصلوات والصيامات والزكاة إذ لم يقل أحد بذلك، وإنما المراد وكذا قوله في مزدلفة وهي موقف إلا بطن محسر أن المكانين ليسا بمكان وقوف فلا يجزئ فيهما كما سيأتي . قوله : (تحبط بالإسلام والهجرة والحج أي بمجموع الثلاثة لا بكل واحد على انفراده قوله : (١) رواه مسلم في كتاب الإيمان حديث ١٩٢. (٢) رواه في الموطأ في كتاب الحج حديث ٢٤٥.
With the condition of the imam and ihram, then proceed to the standing place, stand near the mountain, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batin (Arana). His statement: (And all of Arafat is a standing place except Batin 'Arana) due to the hadith of Bukhari: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and avoid the valley of 'Arana, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir, and all the mountain passes of Mecca are places of sacrifice.' (1) And in al-Mughrib: 'Arana is a valley adjacent to Arafat, and its diminutive is 'Uraynah, attributed to the 'Uraniyyun. Al-Qurtubi mentioned in his Tafsir that it is with fathah and dammah to the west of the mosque of Arafat, to the extent that some scholars said: If the western wall of the mosque of Arafat fell, it would fall into the valley of 'Arana. Al-Baji reported from Ibn Habib that Arafat is in al-Hill and 'Arana is in al-Haram. His statement: (praising, declaring greatness, declaring unity, declaring talbiyah, praying, supplicating) i.e., stand praising etc., due to the hadith of Malik and others: 'The best supplication is the supplication of the day of Arafah, and the best thing I and the prophets before me have said is: La ilaha illa Allah, alone without partner, to Him belongs the dominion and to Him belongs praise, He gives life and causes death, and He is living and does not die, in His hand is good, and He is over all things capable.' And he (peace be upon him) used to strive in supplication in this standing place until it is narrated that he supplicated on the evening of Arafah for his ummah for forgiveness, and it was answered except for bloods and injustices, then he repeated the supplication at Muzdalifah and it was answered even for bloods and injustices. Ibn Majah narrated it. The small hills at the foot of the Mount of Mercy, which look like small mounds, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) placed the belly of his she-camel towards the rocks, and the mountain of the walkers in front of him, and he faced the Qibla, and his standing place was at al-Nabit. Al-Azraqi said: The gap behind the imam's standing place, and the Prophet's standing place was on a rugged tooth between stones protruding from Jabal al-Al. Al-Farisi said that Qadi al-Qudat Badr al-Din said: I have endeavored to determine his standing place from multiple directions, and some reliable scholars of Mecca agreed with me until I obtained a probable determination: it is the elevated gap overlooking the standing place, to its right and behind it a rock connected to the mountain rocks, and this gap is between the mountain and the square building to its left, and it is slightly closer to the mountain, such that the mountain is to your right when facing the Qibla and the square building is slightly to your left and behind. If you find the Prophet's standing place, that is the ultimate goal, so adhere to it and do not leave it. And if it is hidden from you, stand between the mountain and the mentioned building on all the rocks and the places between them, sometimes on its plain and sometimes on its mountain, hoping that you may coincide with the prophetic standing place. Thus in al-Murshidi 'ala al-Kanz. And al-Qadi Muhammad 'Aid said: The square building is known as the Kitchen of Adam (peace be upon him), and I have stood at his (the Prophet's) standing place many times and experienced great humility. It is known by a burned rock that follows it and its surrounding scattered rocks and the black rocks beyond connected to the mountain; here is the sought goal. End quote. Thus in Hashiyat al-Madani 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The author's statement: (And all of Arafat is a standing place except Batin 'Arana) apparently this... and al-Nabit... (1) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Hajj, hadith 149; Abu Dawud in the Book of Rituals, chapter 56; al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Hajj, chapter 54; al-Nasa'i in the Book of Rituals, chapter 202; al-Muwatta in the Book of Hajj, hadith 166; Ahmad in his Musnad (1/72, 75, 76). And so on to the end of the mentioned hadith. Then he said: It is weak due to al-Abbas ibn Mirdas, for he is a munkar hadith, rejected in evidence as the memorizers mentioned, but it has many supporting evidences, including what Ahmad narrated with a sound chain from Ibn 'Abbas: A young man was riding behind the Messenger of Allah on the day of Arafah, and he kept looking at women, so the Prophet said: 'O son of my brother, this is a day whoever controls his hearing and sight will be forgiven.' And including what al-Bukhari narrated marfu': 'Whoever performs Hajj and does not engage in obscenity or immorality will return from his sins like the day his mother bore him.' And including what Muslim narrated in his Sahih marfu': 'Islam destroys what was before it, and hijrah destroys what was before it, and Hajj destroys what was before it.' (1) And including what Malik narrated in al-Muwatta marfu': 'The devil is not seen on any day smaller, more humiliated, or angrier than on the day of Arafah, and that is only due to the descent of mercy and Allah's overlooking of great sins, except on the day of Badr, for he saw Jibril arranging the angels.' (2) These imply expiation of minor and major sins, even if they are rights of the servants. However, al-Akmal mentioned in Sharh al-Mashariq that 'Islam destroys what was before it' means that previous sins are nullified by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj, whether minor or major, and they include rights of Allah and rights of servants with respect to a harbi, such that if he embraces Islam, he is not held accountable for anything, even if he killed, took wealth, and stored it in dar al-harb, then embraced Islam, he is not taken to task for any of that. Based on this, Islam alone would suffice to achieve this, but the Prophet mentioned hijrah and Hajj as an emphasis in his good tidings and encouragement to embrace his message, for hijrah and Hajj do not expiate injustices nor are they decisively established to erase major sins; rather, they expiate minor sins. It is possible to say that major sins that are not rights of servants are also included, like the Islam of a dhimmi, and then there is no doubt that their mention was for emphasis. End quote. Thus Imam al-Tibi mentioned in his commentary on this hadith and said that the commentators agreed upon it. Thus Imam al-Nawawi and al-Qurtubi mentioned in Sharh Muslim. And Qadi 'Iyad mentioned that Ahl al-Sunnah are unanimously agreed that major sins are only expiated by repentance. The conclusion is that the issue is speculative, and Hajj is not decisively established to expiate major sins from the rights of Allah, let alone rights of the servants. And if we accept expiation for all, it does not mean, as many people assume, that debts are dropped from him, nor the making up of prayers, fasts, and zakat, for no one has said that. Rather, the meaning is... and likewise his statement about Muzdalifah that it is a standing place except Batin Muhassir, that the two places are not places of standing, so they are not sufficient as will come. His statement: (It destroys by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj) i.e., by the three together, not by each one individually. (1) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Faith, hadith 192. (2) Narrated in al-Muwatta in the Book of Hajj, hadith 245.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a portion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering two main rulings: (1) the valid place for wuquf (standing) at Arafat, and (2) the recommended actions during the standing, including a detailed discussion on the expiation of sins through Hajj. The commentator follows the order of the matn, first explaining that all of Arafat is a valid standing place for Hajj except the valley of Batin 'Arana. The proof is the famous hadith from Bukhari, which is also narrated by several other hadith collections. The commentary then provides geographical clarifications: 'Arana is a valley adjacent to Arafat, and some scholars place it within the Haram boundary, while Arafat itself is in the Hill. The second part addresses the actions recommended during wuquf: praising Allah (hamd), magnifying Him (takbir), declaring His oneness (tahlil), reciting the talbiyah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and making supplication (dua). The best dua on this day is 'La ilaha illa Allah...' as narrated by Malik. The commentary then recounts a story about the Prophet's intense supplication on the day of Arafah, emphasizing that he supplicated for his ummah and was answered, except for matters of blood and injustices; he repeated the dua at Muzdalifah and was answered fully. This leads into a lengthy discussion about the hadiths that mention Hajj expiating sins. The commentator clarifies that the apparent meaning of these hadiths might suggest that Haj wipes out all sins, major and minor, even rights of others. However, the reliable Hanafi position, supported by scholars like al-Akmal, al-Tibi, al-Nawawi, al-Qurtubi, and Qadi 'Iyad, is that this applies fully only to a former harbi (enemy combatant) who embraces Islam, for whom previous crimes are waived. For Muslims, Hajj expiates minor sins but not major sins (kaba'ir) nor rights of the servants (mazalim). Major sins require sincere repentance (tawbah), and debts, missed prayers, fasts, and zakat remain obligations that are not automatically forgiven by Hajj. The commentator concludes that the issue is speculative (zanni), not definitive, and that one should not assume Hajj absolves one of all responsibilities. The passage ends by returning to the matn reference to Muzdalifah as a standing place, excluding Batin Muhassir, and emphasizing that the expiation mentioned in the hadith is achieved collectively by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj, not by any one act alone.

Key Terms
التحط (al-taḥaṭṭu): The act of destruction or annulment of previous sins through Islam, hijrah, or Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of Hajj on major sins (kaba'ir)?
A) They are automatically expiated
B) They require separate repentance (tawbah) for expiation
C) They are expiated only if accompanied by charity
D) They are not expiated at all

Key Takeaway
Hajj expiates minor sins, but major sins require repentance and rights of others must be settled separately.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Hajj Expiation: Sins Forgiven, Obligations Remain
Clarifying that Hajj expiates sins but not outstanding obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on what Hajj does and does not expiate, and distinguish between expiation of sin (ithm) and removal of obligation (wajib).

Core Idea
Hajj expiates the sin of delaying obligations; the duties themselves remain.

Many Muslims believe that performing Hajj wipes clean all financial debts and missed prayers. This lesson, drawn from Ibn Nujaym's al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, clarifies the correct Hanafi position: Hajj forgives the sin of neglecting obligations, but the obligations themselves—like qada prayers, zakat, and debts—must still be fulfilled. The author relies on the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah that major sins require repentance, not just Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing Hajj; the ruling discussed is its effect on previous sins and obligations.
The text discusses a ruling about expiation (takfir).
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites multiple hadiths: 'Whoever performs Hajj and does not commit obscenity or wickedness comes out of his sins like the day his mother bore him' (Bukhari); 'Islam destroys what was before it, hijrah destroys what was before it, and Hajj destroys what was before it' (Muslim).
These hadiths are ahad, so they provide zanni proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key word 'yahdimu' (destroys) suggests removal. Scholars ask: does it remove sin, obligation, or both? The Hanafi position distinguishes: the sin (ithm) is removed, but the obligation (wajib) remains.
This distinction is critical and based on other texts and consensus.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some people (and even some scholars) mistakenly think Hajj removes all liabilities. The text explicitly refutes this, saying 'no one said that'.
The ikhtilaf is between the correct scholarly view and a popular misconception.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that Hajj expiates sins but obligations remain. This is supported by consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah as reported by Qadi Iyad.
The author uses the example of a harbi convert to show that only in that specific case are rights of people also forgiven.

فالحاصل أن المسألة ظنية وأن الحج لا يقطع فيه بتكفير الكبائر من حقوق الله تعالى فضلاً عن حقوق العباد وإن قلنا بالتكفير للكل فليس معناه كما يتوهمه كثير من الناس أن الدين يسقط عنه وكذا قضاء الصلوات والصيامات والزكاة إذ لم يقل أحد بذلك، وإنما المراد وكذا قوله في مزدلفة وهي موقف إلا بطن محسر أن المكانين ليسا بمكان وقوف فلا يجزئ فيهما كما سيأتي . قوله : (تحبط بالإسلام والهجرة والحج أي بمجموع الثلاثة لا بكل واحد على انفراده قوله : (رواه مسلم في كتاب الإيمان حديث ١٩٢. رواه في الموطأ في كتاب الحج حديث ٢٤٥). بمقتضى عموم أن إثم مطل الدين وتأخيره يسقط ثم بعد الوقوف بعرفة إذا مطل صار آثماً الآن، وكذا إثم تأخير الصلاة عن أوقاتها يرتفع بالحج القضاء ثم بعد الوقوف بعرفة يطالب بالقضاء فإن لم يفعل كان آثماً على القول بفوريته، وكذا في البقية على هذا القياس. وبالجملة فلم يقل أحد الأحاديث الواردة في الحج كما لا يخفى. وأشار بقوله «ملبياً» إلى الرد على من قال يقطعها إذا وقف.
The Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. 'Aranah (a place) praising, magnifying, saying la ilaha illallah, saying labbayk, praying, supplicating, then to Muzdalifah after sunset, and descend near...' And it is weak because of al-Abbas ibn Muradas, for he is munkar al-hadith, not acceptable according to the memorizers, but it has many supporting evidences. Among them is what Ahmad narrated with a sound chain from Ibn Abbas: 'A young man was riding behind the Messenger of Allah on the day of Arafah, and he started looking at women and glancing at them. The Prophet said: O son of my brother, this is a day on which whoever controls his hearing and sight will be forgiven.' Among them is what Bukhari narrated marfu'an: 'Whoever performs Hajj and does not commit obscenity or wickedness comes out of his sins like the day his mother bore him.' Among them is what Muslim narrated in his Sahih marfu'an: 'Islam destroys what was before it, hijrah destroys what was before it, and Hajj destroys what was before it.' Among them is what Malik narrated in al-Muwatta marfu'an: 'Shaytan is never seen smaller, more disgraced, or more angry than on the day of Arafah, and that is only because he sees the descent of mercy and Allah's overlooking of great sins, except what he saw on the day of Badr, for he saw Jibril arranging the angels.' These imply the expiation of minor and major sins, even if they involve the rights of people. But al-Akmal mentioned in Sharh al-Mashariq that the meaning of 'Islam destroys what was before it' is that past sins are nullified by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj, whether minor or major, and include the rights of Allah and the rights of people with respect to a harbi, so that if he becomes Muslim, he is not asked for anything of them, even if he killed, took wealth, and stored it in dar al-harb, then became Muslim, he is not held accountable for any of that. On this, Islam alone is sufficient to achieve his purpose, but he mentioned hijrah and Hajj as emphasis in his glad tidings and encouragement in his pledge, for hijrah and Hajj do not expiate injustices, nor is it decisively said that they erase major sins; they only expiate minor sins. And it may be said that major sins that do not involve the rights of people are also like the Islam of dhimmis, and then there is no doubt that their mention was for emphasis. End. Thus mentioned Imam al-Tibi in his commentary on this hadith, and he said: The commentators agreed upon it. Thus mentioned Imam al-Nawawi and al-Qurtubi in their commentaries on Muslim. And Qadi Iyad mentioned that Ahl al-Sunnah have consensus that major sins are not expiated except by repentance. So the conclusion is that the matter is speculative, and it is not decisively said that Hajj expiates major sins from the rights of Allah, let alone the rights of people. And if we do say it expiates everything, its meaning is not as many people mistakenly think that the debt falls from him, nor the making up of prayers, fasts, and zakat, for no one said that. Rather, the intent is... and likewise his statement about Muzdalifah: 'It is a place of standing except for Muhassir valley' that the two places are not places for standing, so it is not acceptable there as will come. His statement: 'They are nullified by Islam, hijrah, and Hajj' meaning by all three together, not by each one individually. By virtue of the general meaning that the sin of delaying debt and postponing it falls, then after standing at Arafah, if one delays, he becomes sinful now. Likewise, the sin of delaying prayer from its times is elevated by Hajj to qada, then after standing at Arafah, he is required to make it up; if he does not do it, he is sinful based on the view of its immediacy. And so on for the rest on this analogy. In summary, no one said the hadiths reported about Hajj, as is not hidden. And he indicated by his statement 'saying labbayk' the refutation of those who say he cuts it off when he stands.
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This is a commentary from the sharh (expansive explanation) of the matn, clarifying the effect of Hajj on sins and obligations. The passage begins with a weak hadith but supports it with multiple sound narrations showing the virtue of Arafah and the expiatory power of Hajj. The author then addresses a key misunderstanding: does Hajj remove all sins including major ones and even obligations like debts and missed prayers? He reports the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah that major sins require repentance, not just Hajj. However, Hajj does expiate the sin (ithm) of delaying obligations, but the obligation itself (e.g., qada, repayment) remains. This is analogous to the case of a harbi who converts: his past sins are forgiven, but if he killed and took property, he is not pursued, but this is specific to the condition of harbi. For Muslims, the obligations remain. The author stresses that the hadiths about Hajj destroying previous sins mean the sin itself, not the liability. He also clarifies a point about the talbiyah: one should continue reciting it until standing at Arafah, refuting a view that it is cut off earlier.

Key Terms
تكفير (takfir): Expiating or covering sins, removing their punishment in the afterlife.
الكبائر (al-kaba'ir): Major sins that are specifically warned against in the Quran or Sunnah, e.g., murder, zina, neglecting salah.
حقوق العباد (huquq al-ibad): Rights of people, such as debts, property, and bodily integrity, that must be fulfilled even after repentance or Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, does Hajj expiate the obligation to make up missed prayers?
A) Yes, it expiates both sin and obligation.
B) No, it only expiates the sin of delaying, not the qada obligation.
C) It depends on the type of sin.
D) The text does not discuss this.

Key Takeaway
Hajj expiates the sin of neglecting obligations, but the obligations themselves remain binding.

Conditions and Sunan of Wukuf at Arafat
Outlining the ruling, conditions, wajibat, and sunan of wukuf at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions, wajibat, and sunan of wukuf at Arafat and explain why continuity is wajib but not a rukn.

Core Idea
Wukuf at Arafat is the greatest pillar of Hajj; being present suffices, but continuity until sunset is wajib.

Wukuf at Arafat is the central act of Hajj. This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies exactly what constitutes wukuf, its necessary conditions, and the recommended practices. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for the validity of one's pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
Locate the author's statement that wukuf is a rukn and the hadith cited. Note that the hadith 'al-Hajju Arafah' is the primary evidence.
2
List the conditions (shurut)
Extract the two explicit conditions: being within the boundaries of Arafat and being within the designated time. Confirm that standing upright and intention are not conditions.
3
Distinguish between rukn and wajib
Note that wukuf itself is a rukn (pillar), but its continuity (imtidad) until sunset is wajib. Understand the consequence: missing the rukn invalidates Hajj; missing the wajib requires a dam.
4
Identify the sunan
List the recommended acts: ghusl, two khutbahs, combining Zuhr and Asr, performing wukuf immediately after, being not fasting, and being in wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن الوقوف ركن من أركان الحج كما قدمناه وهو أعظم أركانه للحديث الصحيح الحج عرفة وشرطه شيئان: أحدهما كونه في أرض عرفات. الثاني أن يكون في وقته كما سيأتي بيانه وليس القيام من شرطه ولا من واجباته حتى لو كان جالساً جاز لأن الوقوف المفروض هو الكينونة فيه، وكذا النية ليس من شرطه، وواجبه الامتداد إلى الغروب. وأما سننه فالاغتسال للوقوف والخطبتان والجمع بين الصلاتين وتعجيل الوقوف عقيبهما وأن يكون مفطراً لكونه أعون على الدعاء، وأن يكون متوضئاً لكونه أكمل،
Then know that standing (wuquf) is a pillar (rukn) of Hajj, as we have mentioned, and it is the greatest of its pillars due to the authentic hadith: 'Hajj is Arafah.' Its conditions are two: one: being in the land of Arafat; two: being within its time, as will be explained. Standing upright is not a condition nor a wajib, so if one is sitting, it is permissible, because the required standing is simply being present. Similarly, intention is not a condition. Its wajib is continuity until sunset. As for its sunan: performing ghusl for the standing, the two khutbahs, combining the two prayers (Zuhr and Asr), performing the standing immediately after them, being in a state of not fasting (because it helps in supplication), and being in a state of wudu (because it is more complete).
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage is a clear ruling on the rukn of wukuf (standing at Arafah). The author first establishes that wukuf is a rukn, citing the famous hadith 'al-Hajju Arafah'. It is the greatest rukn because missing it invalidates Hajj. Two conditions are listed: being within the geographical boundaries of Arafat, and being within the designated time (from zawal on 9th Dhul Hijjah until dawn of 10th). Importantly, the author clarifies that standing upright (qiyam) is neither a condition nor a wajib; sitting, lying down, or even passing through while staying for the required duration suffices. The intention (niyyah) for wukuf is also not a condition; the mere presence with the intention of Hajj is enough. However, there is a wajib: staying continuously from after the combined prayer until sunset. The sunan (recommended acts) include ghusl, delivering two khutbahs, combining Zuhr and Asr (jama' taqdim), performing wukuf immediately after the prayer, being in a state of not fasting (so as to have more energy for dua), and being in wudu.

Key Terms
الوقوف (al-wuquf): Present at Arafah, whether standing, sitting, or lying down, for the specified time.
الركن (al-rukn): An integral part of Hajj; its omission invalidates the entire act.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation; continuity until sunset is wajib, not rukn, so compensation is required if omitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is a condition of wukuf (standing) at Arafat?
A) Standing upright.
B) Having a specific intention for wukuf.
C) Being in the land of Arafat.
D) Fasting on the day of Arafah.

Key Takeaway
The rukn of wukuf is simply being present in Arafat at the right time; continuity until sunset is a wajib requiring compensation if missed, and many acts commonly thought necessary are only sunan.

Hajj Expiation and the Obligations that Remain
Detailed analogy between Hajj and tawba in expiating sins while obligations remain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that Hajj expiates sins but does not remove obligations arising from those sins, using the qiyas with tawba.

Core Idea
Hajj forgives the sin, not the duty; obligations like qada, debt, and qisas remain.

Many Muslims hope that performing Haj wipes away all past sins and obligations. But does Hajj cancel the need to make up missed prayers or repay debts? This passage clarifies using the established principle of tawba: just as repentance expiates the sin but leaves the obligation intact, so too does Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed claim
Recognize the misconception that Hajj expiates both sins and obligations arising from them.
2
Recognize the asl (original case): Tawba
Acknowledge that tawba, by consensus, expiates sins but does not cancel obligations (e.g., making up prayers, returning stolen property).
This is the foundation for the analogy.
3
Confirm the hukm of the asl
Establish that according to ijma, tawba does not remove obligations; they must still be fulfilled.
4
Establish the illa (effective cause)
Both tawba and Hajj are acts of worship that expiate sins based on textual evidence (hadith). This common attribute justifies the analogy.
The 'illa is takfir al-dhunub (expiation of sins).
5
Apply the qiyas to the far' (Hajj)
Since Hajj shares the illa of expiating sins, it also shares the ruling: sins are forgiven, but obligations remain.
Examples: delaying prayer, postponing debt, murder – sin expiated, obligation stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وإنما المراد أن اثم مطل الدين وتأخيره يسقط الخ) أقول : بيان ذلك أن من أخر صلاة عن وقتها فقد ارتكب معصية وهي التأخير ووجب عليه شيء آخر وهو القضاء، وكذا إذا مطل الذين، وكذا إذا قتل أحداً ارتكب معصية وهي الجناية على العبد مخالفاً نهي الرب تعالى ووجب عليه شيء آخر وهو تسليم نفسه للقصاص إن كان عمداً أو تسليم الدية، وكذا نظائر ذلك مما يكون معصية يترتب عليها واجب، سواء كان ذلك الواجب من حقوق الله تعالى أو حقوق العبد فما ورد من تكفير الحج للكبائر فالمراد تكفيره للمعاصي الكبائر كتأخير الصلاة ومطل الدين والجناية على العبد. وأما الواجبات المترتبة على تلك المعاصي من لزوم قضاء الصلاة وأداء الدين وتسليم نفسه للقصاص أو تسليم الدية فإنها لا تسقط لأن التكفير إنما يكون للذنب وهذه واجبات لا ذنوب حتى تسقط، ألا ترى أن التوبة تكفر الذنوب بالاتفاق ولا يلزم من ذلك سقوط الواجبات المترتبة على تلك الذنوب على أن التوبة من ذنب يترتب عليه واجب لا تتم إلا بفعل ذلك الواجب فمن غصب شيئاً ثم تاب لا تتم توبته إلا بضمان ما غصب فما بالك بالحج الذي فيه النزاع؟ والمراد من قولنا «لا تتم توبته إلا بفعل الواجب أنه لا يخرج عن عهدة الغصب في الآخرة إلا بذلك وإلا فلو غصب وتاب عن فعل الغصب المذكور وحبس الشيء المغضوب عنده ومنع صاحبه عنه وقد عزم على رده إلى صاحبه تصح توبته وإن بقيت ذمته مشغولة به إلى أن يرده إلى صاحبه فحينئذ تتم توبته بمعنى أنه يخرج عن عهدته من كل جهة. وكذا يقال في مطل الدين وتأخير الصلاة، فقد ظهر بما قررناه أن الحج كالتوبة في تكفير الكبائر، سواء تعلقت بحقوق الله تعالى أو بحقوق العبد أو لم تتعلق بحق أحد أي لم يترتب عليها واجب آخر كشرب الخمر ونحوه، فيكفر الحج الذنب ويبقى حق الله تعالى وحق العبد في ذمته إن كان ذنباً يترتب عليه حق أحدهما كما قررنا وإلا فلا يبقى عليه شيء، فاغتنم هذا التحرير الفريد فإن به يتضح المرام وتندفع الشبهة والأوهام وقد أشار إليه العلامة إبراهيم اللقاني في شرحه الكبير على منظومته في التوحيد فقال إن قوله لا من حج البيت فلم يرفث ولم يفسق خرج
(And the intent is that the sin of delaying debt and postponing it falls, etc.) I say: The clarification of that is that whoever delays a prayer from its time has committed a sin, which is the delay, and something else becomes obligatory upon him, which is the make-up (qada). Similarly, if one delays a debt, and if one kills someone, he commits a sin which is the transgression against the servant, violating the command of Allah Almighty, and something else becomes obligatory upon him, which is surrendering himself for retribution if intentional, or paying blood money. Likewise, similar cases where a sin entails an obligation, whether that obligation is from the rights of Allah or the rights of the servant. Thus, what has been reported regarding Hajj expiating major sins means expiation for the major sins themselves, like delaying prayer, postponing debt, and transgression against a servant. As for the obligations arising from those sins, such as the necessity of making up prayer, paying the debt, and surrendering oneself for retribution or paying blood money, these are not dropped because expiation is only for the sin, and these are obligations, not sins, so they are not dropped. Do you not see that repentance expiates sins by consensus, and yet it does not necessitate dropping the obligations arising from those sins? Indeed, repentance from a sin that entails an obligation is not complete except by fulfilling that obligation. So if someone wrongfully seizes something and then repents, his repentance is not complete except by returning what he seized. What then of Hajj which is subject to dispute? The meaning of our statement 'his repentance is not complete except by fulfilling the obligation' is that he does not discharge himself from the liability of the usurpation in the Hereafter except by that. Otherwise, if he usurps and repents from the act of usurpation, but keeps the usurped item with him and prevents the owner from it, while having resolved to return it to its owner, his repentance is valid, although his liability remains occupied with it until he returns it to its owner. Then at that point his repentance is complete in the sense that he discharges himself from all aspects. The same is said regarding delaying debt and postponement of prayer. Thus, it has become clear from what we have established that Hajj is like repentance in expiating major sins, whether they relate to the rights of Allah or the rights of the servant, or do not relate to anyone's right, i.e., no other obligation arises from them, like drinking wine and the like. So Hajj expiates the sin, while the right of Allah and the right of the servant remain in his liability if it is a sin that entails a right of either, as we have explained. Otherwise, nothing remains upon him. So seize this unique analysis, for by it the goal becomes clear and doubts and illusions are dispelled. And the scholar Ibrahim al-Laqani indicated it in his large commentary on his poem on tawhid, saying: 'His statement: Whoever performs Hajj to the House and does not commit obscenity or sin, comes out...'
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage is a detailed continuation and refinement of the earlier discussion on Hajj expiation. The author explicitly draws an analogy (qiyas) between Hajj and tawba (repentance). He states that just as tawba expiates the sin of an act but does not remove the obligation that arises from it (e.g., qada prayer, repayment of debt, qisas/diya for murder), similarly Hajj expiates the sin (ithm) but the obligation remains. To illustrate, he uses the example of ghasp (usurpation): if someone usurps property and repents, the repentance is valid, but he remains liable to return the property until he actually does so. Thus, Hajj removes the sin of delaying prayer, but the qada prayer is still obligatory; Hajj removes the sin of delaying debt, but the debt must still be paid; Hajj removes the sin of murder, but the qisas or diya remains. However, if the sin does not entail an obligation (e.g., drinking wine), then Hajj expiates it fully and nothing remains. The author emphasizes that this is a unique and important clarification that resolves misconceptions. He concludes by citing Ibrahim al-Laqani, who referenced the same understanding from the hadith 'Whoever performs Hajj and does not commit obscenity or sin comes out [from his sins]' — implying that the hadith's 'coming out' refers to sins, not obligations.

Key Terms
التوبة (al-tawba): Repentance from sin, which according to consensus expiates sins but does not remove obligations that arise from those sins.
الذنب (al-dhanb): Sin, an act of disobedience that incurs punishment but may be expiated through worship like Hajj or tawba.
الغصب (al-ghasp): Usurpation or wrongful possession of another's property, which is a sin that entails the obligation of returning the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qiyas presented in the lesson, what is the relationship between Hajj and tawba regarding expiation?
A) Hajj expiates more than tawba.
B) Both expiate sins but not obligations.
C) Only tawba expiates sins, Hajj does not.
D) Both expiate sins and obligations.

Key Takeaway
Hajj expiates the sin of an act but does not cancel the obligation to fulfill consequential duties (e.g., qada, debt, qisas); this is established by analogy with tawba.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Hajj Expiation of Sins without Removing Obligations
Clarifying that Hajj expiates sins but not obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what Hajj expiates (sin only) and identify that obligations arising from the sin remain due, applying this to cases of missed prayers, debts, and homicide.

Core Idea
Hajj expiates the sin, but obligations like qada and debt repayment remain.

This passage addresses a frequent question: does Hajj wipe away all past mistakes, including duties we owe to Allah and others? The author clarifies that Hajj removes the sin (ithm) of delaying or committing prohibited acts, but the obligatory duties that result from those acts—such as making up missed prayers, repaying debts, or submitting to retribution—are not cancelled. The argument hinges on the distinction between sin and obligation, supported by analogy with repentance, which also expiates sin but requires fulfillment of consequent duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
Read the passage to understand the difference between 'ithm' (sin) and 'wajib' (obligation). The author uses examples: delaying prayer (sin) vs. making up the prayer (wajib); delaying debt (sin) vs. paying debt (wajib); murder (sin) vs. retribution/diyah (wajib).
Note that the sin is of the act of delay/aggression, while the wajib is the remedial duty.
2
Examine the analogy with repentance
The author compares Hajj to tawbah: both expiate sins, but do not automatically fulfill obligations. The example of usurpation (ghasb) illustrates that even after repentance, the usurped property must be returned or guaranteed.
This strengthens the argument that Hajj, like repentance, cannot drop owed duties.
3
Understand the scope of expiation
Passage states that for sins that entail no further wajib (e.g., drinking wine), Hajj fully expiates and nothing remains. For sins that do entail a wajib (e.g., delayed prayer), the sin is expiated but the wajib stays.
Thus the effect of Hajj depends on the type of sin.
4
Note the refutation of opposing views
The author criticizes those who misinterpret hadiths about Hajj expiating all past sins, implying they mistakenly include duties. The correct understanding limits expiation to the sin itself.
This highlights a methodological principle: hadiths must be interpreted in light of other texts and reason (here, analogy with repentance).
5
Apply to real scenarios
Given a case (e.g., missed prayers, unpaid debt), determine what is expiated (the sin of neglecting/delaying) and what remains (the duty to fulfill).
Practice with the examples from the passage: prayer qada, debt repayment, retribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بمقتضى عموم أن إثم مطل الدين وتأخيره يسقط ثم بعد الوقوف بعرفة إذا مطل صار آثماً الآن، وكذا إثم تأخير الصلاة عن أوقاتها يرتفع بالحج القضاء ثم بعد الوقوف بعرفة يطالب بالقضاء فإن لم يفعل كان آثماً على القول بفوريته، وكذا في البقية على هذا القياس. وبالجملة فلم يقل أحد الأحاديث الواردة في الحج كما لا يخفى. وأشار بقوله «ملبياً» إلى الرد على من قال يقطعها إذا وقف. (وإنما المراد أن اثم مطل الدين وتأخيره يسقط الخ) أقول : بيان ذلك أن من أخر صلاة عن وقتها فقد ارتكب معصية وهي التأخير ووجب عليه شيء آخر وهو القضاء، وكذا إذا مطل الذين، وكذا إذا قتل أحداً ارتكب معصية وهي الجناية على العبد مخالفاً نهي الرب تعالى ووجب عليه شيء آخر وهو تسليم نفسه للقصاص إن كان عمداً أو تسليم الدية، وكذا نظائر ذلك مما يكون معصية يترتب عليها واجب، سواء كان ذلك الواجب من حقوق الله تعالى أو حقوق العبد فما ورد من تكفير الحج للكبائر فالمراد تكفيره للمعاصي الكبائر كتأخير الصلاة ومطل الدين والجناية على العبد. وأما الواجبات المترتبة على تلك المعاصي من لزوم قضاء الصلاة وأداء الدين وتسليم نفسه للقصاص أو تسليم الدية فإنها لا تسقط لأن التكفير إنما يكون للذنب وهذه واجبات لا ذنوب حتى تسقط، ألا ترى أن التوبة تكفر الذنوب بالاتفاق ولا يلزم من ذلك سقوط الواجبات المترتبة على تلك الذنوب على أن التوبة من ذنب يترتب عليه واجب لا تتم إلا بفعل ذلك الواجب فمن غصب شيئاً ثم تاب لا تتم توبته إلا بضمان ما غصب فما بالك بالحج الذي فيه النزاع؟ والمراد من قولنا «لا تتم توبته إلا بفعل الواجب أنه لا يخرج عن عهدة الغصب في الآخرة إلا بذلك وإلا فلو غصب وتاب عن فعل الغصب المذكور وحبس الشيء المغضوب عنده ومنع صاحبه عنه وقد عزم على رده إلى صاحبه تصح توبته وإن بقيت ذمته مشغولة به إلى أن يرده إلى صاحبه فحينئذ تتم توبته بمعنى أنه يخرج عن عهدته من كل جهة. وكذا يقال في مطل الدين وتأخير الصلاة، فقد ظهر بما قررناه أن الحج كالتوبة في تكفير الكبائر، سواء تعلقت بحقوق الله تعالى أو بحقوق العبد أو لم تتعلق بحق أحد أي لم يترتب عليها واجب آخر كشرب الخمر ونحوه، فيكفر الحج الذنب ويبقى حق الله تعالى وحق العبد في ذمته إن كان ذنباً يترتب عليه حق أحدهما كما قررنا وإلا فلا يبقى عليه شيء، فاغتنم هذا التحرير الفريد فإن به يتضح المرام وتندفع الشبهة والأوهام وقد أشار إليه العلامة إبراهيم اللقاني في شرحه الكبير على منظومته في التوحيد فقال إن قوله لا من حج البيت فلم يرفث ولم يفسق خرج
By the general meaning that the sin of delaying debt and its postponement is removed, then after standing at Arafa, if he delays, he becomes sinful now. Likewise, the sin of delaying prayer beyond its time is removed by the performance of Hajj and then after standing at Arafa he is required to make it up; if he does not, he becomes sinful according to the view of its immediacy. And similarly for the rest on this analogy. In summary, no one said the hadiths about Hajj as is not hidden. And he indicated by his saying 'making talbiyah' a refutation of those who said he cuts it off when he stands. (And the intended meaning is that the sin of delaying debt and its postponement is removed, etc.) I say: The explanation of that is that whoever delays a prayer beyond its time has committed a sin, which is the delay, and something else becomes obligatory upon him, which is making it up. Likewise, if he delays a debt, and likewise if he kills someone, he commits a sin, which is the aggression against the servant contrary to the prohibition of the Lord Most High, and something else becomes obligatory upon him, which is surrendering himself for retribution if intentional or surrendering the blood money. And similar cases where there is a sin upon which an obligation is consequent, whether that obligation is from the rights of Allah Most High or the rights of the servant. So what has come regarding the expiation of major sins by Hajj means its expiation of major sins like delaying prayer, delaying debt, and aggression against a servant. As for the obligations consequent upon those sins, such as the necessity of making up prayer, paying the debt, surrendering himself for retribution or paying blood money, they are not dropped because expiation is only for the sin, and these are obligations, not sins, that they be dropped. Do you not see that repentance expiates sins by agreement, and it does not follow from that the dropping of obligations consequent upon those sins? Moreover, repentance from a sin that entails an obligation is not complete except by performing that obligation. So whoever usurps something, then repents, his repentance is not complete except by guaranteeing what he usurped. So what about Hajj, which is disputed? And the meaning of our saying 'his repentance is not complete except by performing the obligation' is that he does not acquit himself of the liability of usurpation in the Hereafter except by that. Otherwise, if he usurps and repents from the mentioned act of usurpation, keeps the usurped thing with him and prevents its owner from it, but resolves to return it to its owner, his repentance is valid even though his liability remains occupied with it until he returns it to its owner; then at that point his repentance becomes complete in the sense that he acquits himself of liability from every angle. And the same is said regarding delaying debt and delaying prayer. So it has become clear from what we have established that Hajj is like repentance in expiating major sins, whether they pertain to the rights of Allah Most High or the rights of the servant, or do not pertain to anyone's right, i.e., no other obligation is consequent upon them, like drinking wine and the like. So Hajj expiates the sin, and the rights of Allah Most High and the rights of the servant remain in his liability if it is a sin that entails a right of either of them as we have established; otherwise, nothing remains upon him. So seize this unique exposition, for by it the intent becomes clear and doubts and illusions are repelled. Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the scope of Hajj's expiation. The author begins by stating that the sin of delaying a debt or prayer is removed by Hajj, but the obligation (qada, repayment) remains. After Arafah, if one delays again, he becomes sinful. The same applies to murder: the sin is expiated, but retribution or diyah is still obligatory. The author emphasizes that expiation is for the sin (ithm), not for the obligations (wajibat) that follow from the sin. He supports this with the analogy of repentance: repentance expiates the sin by consensus, but does not drop the obligation to make amends—e.g., one who usurps property must still return it. Thus, Hajj is like repentance: it expiates the sin but does not remove the duty to fulfill rights of Allah or people. The author criticizes those who misunderstand the hadith 'Hajj expiates what came before.' He then praises his own unique exposition and cites al-Laqqani's support.

Key Terms
تكفير (takfir): Expiation or removal of sin (ithm) through Hajj or repentance.
الذنب (al-dhanb): Sin or disobedience; the act itself that is expiated by Hajj.
الواجب (al-wajib): The obligatory act that remains due despite expiation of sin, e.g., qada, debt, retribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does Hajj expiate for a person who has delayed a prayer?
A) The prayer itself becomes valid without making it up.
B) The sin of delaying the prayer, but the obligation to make it up remains.
C) Both the sin and the obligation to make it up are removed.
D) Only the obligation to make it up, not the sin.

Key Takeaway
Hajj expiates the sin of disobedience, but any wajib consequent to that sin remains binding until fulfilled.

The Pillar of Wuquf: Conditions, Obligations, and Recommended Acts
Defining the standing at Arafat as a rukn with conditions and sunan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions and the wajib of wuquf, and distinguish between its rukn, wajib, and sunan.

Core Idea
Wuquf is the greatest pillar of Hajj; its essence is presence, not standing; its wajib is staying until sunset.

The standing at Arafat (wuquf) is the central act of Hajj, without which the Hajj is invalid. In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author defines wuquf as a rukn, clarifies its minimal conditions, and enumerates its obligatory and recommended elements. Understanding this hierarchy—rukun, wajib, sunnah—is crucial for correct practice and for knowing what requires compensation if missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
Recognize that wuquf is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, based on the hadith 'Hajj is Arafah'. This establishes its fundamental status.
The hadith proves that the very essence of Hajj is the standing; without it, there is no Hajj.
2
Extract the conditions
List the two conditions: being within the land of Arafat and being at the correct time (from noon of 9th to dawn of 10th). Note that standing up and intention are not conditions.
Conditions are prerequisites for validity; missing a condition invalidates the act.
3
Distinguish rukn, wajib, and sunan
Classify the elements: rukn = presence (just being there); wajib = remaining until sunset; sunan = all other recommended acts (ghusl, dua, etc.). Understand the consequences of omission for each.
Hanafi usul: rukn omission → invalidity; wajib omission → compensation (dam); sunnah omission → no penalty.
4
Analyze the refutation of Mount of Mercy
Understand that the Prophet's standing place is the most virtuous spot; the Mount of Mercy has no special merit. This corrects a common misconception.
The author cites al-Nawawi to dismiss the baseless claim about Jabal al-Du'a.
5
Evaluate rulings on fasting and mount
Fasting on the day of Arafah is not absolutely disliked; it depends on whether it weakens the pilgrim. Standing on a mount is recommended for all, not just the Imam, as it aids focus.
These rulings demonstrate the Hanafi method of balancing textual evidence and practical benefit.

الصحابة كانوا يقتدون بفعه ، ولأنه متى وقف راكباً يكون قلبه فارغاً عن جانب الدابة فيكون قلبه في الدعاء أسكن وفي المناجاة أخلص. قاله الشيخ عبد الله العفيف. ثم قال: وفي السراج الوهاج نقلاً عن منسك ابن العجمي : يكره الوقوف على ظهر الدابة إلا في حال الوقوف بعرفة بل هو الأفضل للإمام وغيره. وقال ابن الحاج في المدخل : وهذا الموضع مستثنى عما نهى عنه من اتخاذ ظهور الدواب مساطب يجلس عليها ا هـ . وفي منسك ابن العجمى ومن لم يكن له مركب فالأفضل أن يقف قائماً فإذا أعيا جلس ولو وقف جالساً جاز ا هـ . ومفهوم عبارة الكرماني أن من قدر على الركوب ولم
Then know that the standing is a pillar of the pillars of Hajj as we have presented, and it is the greatest of its pillars due to the authentic hadith 'Hajj is Arafah.' Its conditions are two: one is that it be in the land of Arafat. The second is that it be in its time as will be explained. Standing up is not a condition nor a requirement, so even if he sits, it is permissible, because the obligatory standing is simply being there. Likewise, intention is not a condition. Its obligatory (wajib) is extension until sunset. As for its sunan: performing ghusl for the standing, the two sermons, combining the two prayers, hastening the standing after them, being in a state of breaking fast (not fasting) because it helps in supplication, being in a state of wudu because it is more complete, standing on his mount, facing the qibla, being behind the Imam close to him, being present-hearted and free from distracting matters, so he should avoid the path of caravans and others lest he be disturbed by them. And he should stand at the [stone] markers of the Prophet's standing place, and if difficult, he should stand near it as much as possible. As for what is famous among the common people of paying attention to standing on the Mount of Mercy, which is in the middle of Arafat, and preferring it over others, it is a clear error and contrary to the Sunnah. No one who is counted has mentioned any special virtue for climbing this mountain; rather, it has the same ruling as other lands of Arafat except the Prophet's standing place, which is best. Except for al-Tabari and al-Mawardi in al-Hawi, who said it is recommended to seek this mountain called Jabal al-Du'a. He said: It is the standing place of the prophets. But what they said has no basis, and no sound or weak hadith has been reported about it. This was mentioned by al-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. And it is from the Sunnah to abundantly make supplication, takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, istighfar, recitation of Quran, and salawat upon the Prophet. And he should be very careful not to fall short in any of this, for this day cannot be made up. And he should frequently utter repentance from all violations with remorse of the heart, and should cry much while remembering his sins as if he were born from his mother that day. This does not include the rights of Allah and the rights of His servants, because they are in the liability and are not sins; rather, the sin is the delay involved, so it depends on the dropping by the owner. So what drops is only the sin of violating Allah Most High. End. And Allah knows best. His saying: (one of them being in the land of Arafat) apparently this is its pillar because it is inconceivable without it, as in Sharh al-Lubab. His saying: (and that he be not fasting) counted in al-Lubab among the recommended acts of standing: fasting for the strong and breaking fast for the weak. He said: and it is said it is disapproved. Its commentator said: it is a tanzih disapproval lest his character become bad and cause him to fall into something forbidden. Likewise, fasting on the day of Tarwiyah because it weakens him from performing the actions of Hajj. It is established that the Prophet broke his fast on the day of Arafah despite complete strength, but he did not forbid anyone from fasting, so there is no face for absolute disapproval. As for what is in al-Khaniyya: it is disliked to fast on the day of Arafah in Arafat, and likewise the day of Tarwiyah because it weakens him from performing the actions of Hajj, it is based on the ruling of the majority, so it does not contradict what is in al-Kirmani that it is not disliked for the pilgrim to fast on the day of Arafah according to us unless it weakens him from performing the rites; then it is better to leave it. And in al-Fath: if it weakens him from standing and supplications, then it is recommended to leave it. End. His saying: (and that he stands on his mount) is the wording of the text of al-Tanwir: 'and the Imam stands on his she-camel.' al-Madani said in his gloss: there is no specificity for the Imam here; rather, riding is recommended for every person standing in Arafah. The Imam is mentioned only because he is followed in all rites, as the Companions followed his action. And because when he stands riding, his heart is free from the side of the animal, so his heart is more calm in supplication and more sincere in intimate prayer. This was said by Shaykh Abdullah al-Afif. Then he said: In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj quoting from Mansak Ibn al-Ajmi: it is disliked to stand on the back of an animal except in the case of standing at Arafah; rather, it is best for the Imam and others. And Ibn al-Haj said in al-Madkhal: this place is exempt from the prohibition of taking the backs of animals as platforms to sit on. End. And in Mansak Ibn al-Ajmi: he who has no mount, it is better to stand standing; if he tires, he sits; and if he stands sitting, it is permissible. End. And the meaning of al-Kirmani's statement is that one who is able to ride and did not...
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling passage covering the standing at Arafat (wuquf). It first establishes that wuquf is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, indeed the greatest, based on the hadith 'Hajj is Arafah.' The conditions are: being within the land of Arafat, and being at the correct time (from midday of the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah until dawn of the 10th). Standing up is not required; sitting suffices because the essence is presence. Intention is also not a condition. The wajib (obligatory) element is that the standing must extend until sunset. The sunan include: ghusl, delivering two khutbahs, combining zuhr and asr, hastening to the standing after prayer, being in a state of not fasting (since fasting may weaken the person for supplication), having wudu, being on a mount, facing qibla, being near the Imam, being focused, avoiding disturbances, and standing at the Prophet's specific spot (near the rocks). The author then refutes the common practice of preferring the Mount of Mercy (Jabal al-Rahma), stating it has no special virtue except the Prophet's standing place. He quotes al-Tabari and al-Mawardi but dismisses their view as baseless. The sunan also include abundant dhikr, supplication, recitation, and repentance. The author then comments on the ruling of fasting on the day of Arafah: it is not absolutely disliked; rather, it depends on whether it weakens the pilgrim. If it does, leaving it is better. The passage concludes with a discussion on standing on a mount: it is recommended for all, not just the Imam, as it helps focus. If one does not have a mount, standing is better, but sitting is permissible.

Key Terms
الوقوف (al-wuquf): The act of being present in Arafat at the specified time; the greatest pillar of Hajj.
الركن (al-rukn): A fundamental component of Hajj without which the act is invalid.
الواجب (al-wajib): In the context of wuquf, the obligatory extension until sunset; omission requires dam.
السنة (al-sunnah): Recommended acts that enhance the standing; omitted without sin but merit lost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the wajib (obligatory element) of the standing at Arafat?
A) Performing ghusl before the standing
B) Facing the qibla throughout the standing
C) Remaining in Arafat until sunset
D) Standing on a mount

Key Takeaway
Wuquf is the rukn of Hajj; its essence is presence, its wajib is duration until sunset, and its sunan enhance the act without affecting validity.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Mustahabbat of Wuquf at Arafat
Lists recommended acts during wuquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended acts of wuquf and distinguish the Sunnah of standing at the Prophet's place from the innovation of climbing Jabal ar-Rahma.

Core Idea
Stand where the Prophet stood; do not climb Jabal ar-Rahma — the Sunnah is clear.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq enumerates the mustahabbat (recommended acts) during the wuquf at Arafat. It emphasizes facing qibla, being behind the imam, and especially standing at the Prophet's own standing place (as-Su'). The author strongly warns against the common practice of climbing Jabal ar-Rahma, declaring it a clear error. The passage concludes with a call to increase dhikr and repentance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
List the actions described as mustahabb: standing on mount, facing qibla, being behind imam, avoiding disturbances, standing at the Prophet's place, increasing dhikr, etc.
These are not obligatory but rewarded.
2
Locate the best place for wuquf
Learn about the Prophet's standing place at the rocks (as-Su') and understand its superiority over other spots in Arafat.
The author explicitly states this is the best place.
3
Analyze the critique of Jabal ar-Rahma
Understand why the author rejects climbing Jabal ar-Rahma: it is contrary to Sunnah, has no basis in hadith, and only a minority opinion supports it.
At-Tabari and al-Mawardi are mentioned as dissenting.
4
Examine the dhikr and tawba recommendations
Note the specified forms of remembrance (takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, etc.) and the conditions for repentance: sins against Allah can be forgiven through tawba, but sins against people require their forgiveness.
This distinguishes between huquq Allah and huquq al-ibad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن يقف على راحلته وأن يكون مستقبل القبلة، وأن يكون وراء الإمام بالقرب منه، وأن يكون حاضر القلب فارغاً من الأمور الشاغلة عن الدعاء فينبغي أن يجتنب في موقفه طريق القوافل وغيرهم لئلا ينزعج بهم ، وأن يقف عند الصخرات السوء موقف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وإن تعذر عليه يقف بقرب منه بحسب الإمكان، وأما ما اشتهر عن العوام من الاعتناء بالوقوف على جبل الرحمة الذي هو بوسط عرفات وترجيحهم له على غيره فخطأ ظاهر ومخالف للسنة ولم يذكر أحد ممن يعتد به في صعود هذا الجبل فضيلة تختص به بل له حكم سائر أراضي عرفات غير موقف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنه أفضل إلا الطبري والماوردي في الحاوي فإنهما قالا باستحباب قصد هذا الجيل الذي يقال له جبل الدعاء . قال : وهو موقف الأنبياء. وما قالاه لا أصل له ولم يرد فيه حديث صحيح ولا ضعيف كذا ذكر النووي في شرح المهذب. ومن السنة أن يكثر من الدعاء والتكبير والتهليل والتلبية والاستغفار وقراءة القرآن والصلاة على النبي ، وليحذر كل الحذر من التقصير في شيء من هذا فإن هذا اليوم لا يمكن تداركه . ويكثر من التلفظ بالتوبة من جميع المخالفات مع الندم ،بالقلب، وأن يكثر البكاء مع الذكر من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته أمه لا يتناول حقوق الله تعالى وحقوق عباده لأنها في الذمة ليست ذنباً، وإنما الذنب المطل فيه فيتوقف على إسقاط صاحبه فالذي يسقط إثم مخالفة الله تعالى فقط ا هـ . والله أعلم
And that he stands on his mount and that he faces the qibla, and that he is behind the imam near him, and that he is present-hearted free from distracting matters from supplication, so he should avoid in his standing the path of caravans and others so as not to be disturbed by them, and that he stands at the rocks (as-Su') the standing place of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and if it is difficult for him, he stands near it as much as possible. As for what is famous among the commoners of paying attention to standing on the Mount of Mercy (Jabal ar-Rahma) which is in the middle of Arafat and preferring it over others, it is a clear error and contrary to the Sunnah, and no one of those whose opinion is considered has mentioned regarding climbing this mountain a virtue specific to it; rather it has the ruling of the rest of the lands of Arafat except the standing place of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for it is superior. Except at-Tabari and al-Mawardi in al-Hawi, they said it is recommended to go to this mountain, which is called Jabal ad-Du'a. He said: It is the standing place of the prophets. What they said has no basis and no authentic or weak hadith has been reported about it, as mentioned by an-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. It is from the Sunnah to increase in supplication, takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, istighfar, reciting the Quran, and sending blessings on the Prophet; and he should be very careful not to be deficient in any of this, for this day cannot be made up. And he should increase in uttering repentance from all violations with regret in the heart, and he should increase in weeping while remembering his sins as if he were born from his mother, not including the rights of Allah and the rights of His servants because they are in the dhimmah (obligation) and are not sins; rather the sin is the delay, so it depends on the dropping by the owner. So it drops the sin of violating Allah only. End. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq lists the mustahabbat (recommended acts) of wuquf at Arafat. The sharh explains that the pilgrim should stand on his mount, face the qibla, and stand behind the imam. He should avoid disturbances. The best place to stand is at the rocks (as-Su') where the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood. The author strongly criticizes the common practice of climbing Jabal ar-Rahma, stating it has no virtue in the Sunnah, except for a minority opinion from at-Tabari and al-Mawardi which he dismisses as baseless. The passage then recommends various forms of dhikr and supplication, including weeping over sins. It clarifies that only sins against Allah can be forgiven through tawba; sins against people require their forgiveness. This is a clear Hanafi position based on the Sunnah and the practice of the Salaf.

Key Terms
مستحبات الوقوف (mustahabbat al-wuquf): Recommended acts during the standing at Arafat, not obligatory but rewarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on climbing Jabal ar-Rahma (Mount of Mercy) at Arafat?
A) It is recommended because it is the place of the prophets.
B) It is a clear error and contrary to the Sunnah.
C) It is obligatory for the wuquf to be valid.
D) It is permissible but not recommended.

Key Takeaway
The mustahabbat of wuquf emphasize following the precise Sunnah of the Prophet, avoiding innovations like climbing Jabal ar-Rahma, and dedicating oneself to dhikr and sincere repentance.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Pillar of Wuquf and Ruling on Fasting on Arafah
States the rukn of wuquf and discusses the ruling on fasting at Arafah with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rukn of wuquf and apply the Hanafi ruling on fasting on Arafah for pilgrims, distinguishing between the views of al-Karmani and al-Khaniyyah.

Core Idea
The rukn of wuquf is being in Arafat; fasting is sunnah unless it weakens one from worship.

This lesson examines two key rulings from Kanz al-Daqaiq: the essential pillar of wuquf and the nuanced Hanafi position on fasting during the day of Arafah. Understanding the rukn clarifies what is indispensable for Hajj, while the fasting discussion demonstrates how Hanafi usul weighs prophetic action against potential harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rukn of wuquf
The passage explicitly states that being in the land of Arafat is the rukn because wuquf cannot be conceived without it.
Hanafis define wuquf as presence in Arafat, not a specific action like standing.
2
Understand the baseline ruling on fasting
Al-Lubab counts fasting among the mustahabbat (recommended acts) for those who are strong, while the weak should not fast. There is a reported view that it is makruh.
The commentator clarifies this is makruh tanzihi, not tahrimi.
3
Analyze the dalil: the Prophet's action
The Prophet (peace be upon him) broke his fast on Arafah despite being strong, proving it is not obligatory, but he did not forbid others, indicating permissibility.
This shows the ruling is not absolute prohibition or obligation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Khaniyyah states it is disliked absolutely, while al-Karmani restricts dislike to cases where fasting weakens the pilgrim.
The ikhtilaf hinges on whether the illa (weakness) is assumed always or only when actual.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view, supported by al-Fath and al-Bahr al-Raiq, is that fasting is not disliked unless it weakens the pilgrim from the rituals and supplications.
This balances the Prophetic example with consideration of individual capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أحدهما كونه في أرض عرفات الظاهر أن هذا ركنه لعدم تصوره بدونه، كذا في شرح اللباب قوله : (وإن يكون مفطراً) عد في اللباب من مستحبات الوقوف الصوم لمن قوي والفطر للضعيف قال : وقيل يكره. قال شارحه : وهي كراهة تنزيه لئلا يسيء خلقه فيوقعه في محذور أو محظور، وكذا صوم يوم التروية لأنه . يعجزه عن أداء أفعال الحج، وقد ثبت أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم أفطر يوم عرفة مع كمال القوة إلا أنه لم ينه أحداً عن صومه فلا وجه لكراهته على الإطلاق. وأما ما في الخانية ويكره صوم يوم عرفة بعرفات وكذا صوم يوم التروية لأنه يعجزه عن أداء أفعال الحج، فمبني على حكم الأغلب فلا ينافيه ما في الكرماني من أنه لا يكره للحاج الصوم في يوم عرفة عندنا إلا إذا كان يضعفه . عن أداء المناسك فحينئذ تركه أولى، وفي الفتح : إن كان يضعفه عن الوقوف والدعوات فالمستحب تركه ا هـ .
His saying: (One of them is being in the land of Arafat). Apparently this is its pillar (rukn) because it cannot be conceived without it. So in Sharh al-Lubab. His saying: (And that he be not fasting). Al-Lubab counted among the mustahabbat of wuquf fasting for the one who is strong and not fasting for the weak. He said: And it is said it is disliked. Its commentator said: It is a tanzihi dislike (makruh tanzihan) lest his character become bad and cause him to fall into something forbidden or prohibited. Likewise fasting on the day of Tarwiyah because it weakens him from performing the actions of Hajj. And it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) broke his fast on the day of Arafah despite complete strength, but he did not forbid anyone from fasting it, so there is no basis for it being absolutely disliked. As for what is in al-Khaniyyah: 'It is disliked to fast on the day of Arafah at Arafat, and likewise fasting on the day of Tarwiyah because it weakens him from performing the actions of Hajj', it is based on the ruling of the majority, so it does not contradict what is in al-Karmani that it is not disliked for the pilgrim to fast on the day of Arafah in our school unless it weakens him from performing the rituals, in which case leaving it is better. And in al-Fath: If it weakens him from standing and supplications, then it is recommended to leave it.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This section covers two matn phrases from Kanz al-Daqaiq. First, the pillar (rukn) of wuquf is simply being in the land of Arafat; one cannot conceive of wuquf without being there. Second, the ruling on fasting on the day of Arafah. The author notes that according to al-Lubab, fasting is mustahabb for strong pilgrims and not fasting for weak ones, but there is also a view that it is makruh. The sharh clarifies that the dislike is tanzihi (not even close to haram), based on the fear that fasting might affect one's character and devotion. The Prophet's breaking his fast on Arafah despite being able to fast is cited, but he did not prohibit fasting. The Hanafi position from al-Karmani is that fasting is not disliked unless it weakens the pilgrim; then leaving it is better. This nuanced view balances following the Prophet's action and considering individual capacity.

Key Terms
ركن الوقوف (rukn al-wuquf): The essential integral of wuquf: being present in the land of Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dominant Hanafi view, what is the ruling on fasting on the day of Arafah for a pilgrim who is strong?
A) Haram.
B) Makruh tanzihi absolutely.
C) Not disliked, but leaving it is better if it causes weakness.
D) Mustahabb and recommended.

Key Takeaway
The rukn of wuquf is being in Arafat, and fasting on Arafah for the pilgrim is not disliked unless it weakens him from the rituals.

The Ruling of Standing on a Mount at Arafat
Discusses the ruling of standing on a mount during wuquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for standing on a mount during wuquf at Arafat and explain the preferred positions for those without a mount.

Core Idea
Riding at Arafat is a confirmed sunnah; leaving it while able is blameworthy.

This lesson examines the recommendation of standing on a mount during the wuquf at Arafat. The Hanafi school considers it a sunnah muakkadah for all pilgrims, not just the imam. The passage clarifies the virtue and also addresses the etiquettes for those who cannot ride.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (wuquf on a mount) and its hukm level in the Hanafi school.
The act is standing on a riding animal during wuquf at Arafat.
2
Locate the evidence and rationale
Understand the proof: the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) and Companions, and the reasoning that riding frees the heart for devotion.
The reasoning is a form of istihsan or talil.
3
Note the exception
Recognize that this sunnah is specific to Arafat; on other days, standing on an animal is disliked.
Some scholars like Ibn al-Hajj mention this exemption.
4
Apply to those without a mount
For those who cannot ride, the best is standing, then sitting if tired. Lying down is disliked unless excused.
This gradation is from the later Hanafi manuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وأن يقف على راحلته عبارة متن التنوير ووقف الإمام على ناقته . قال المدني في حاشيته : لا خصوصية للإمام هنا بل ينبغي الركوب لكل واقف في عرفة، وإنما ذكر الإمام لأنه يقتدي به في جميع المناسك لأن الصحابة كانوا يقتدون بفعله ، ولأنه متى وقف راكباً يكون قلبه فارغاً عن جانب الدابة فيكون قلبه في الدعاء أسكن وفي المناجاة أخلص. قاله الشيخ عبد الله العفيف. ثم قال: وفي السراج الوهاج نقلاً عن منسك ابن العجمي : يكره الوقوف على ظهر الدابة إلا في حال الوقوف بعرفة بل هو الأفضل للإمام وغيره. وقال ابن الحاج في المدخل : وهذا الموضع مستثنى عما نهى عنه من اتخاذ ظهور الدواب مساطب يجلس عليها ا هـ . وفي منسك ابن العجمى ومن لم يكن له مركب فالأفضل أن يقف قائماً فإذا أعيا جلس ولو وقف جالساً جاز ا هـ . ومفهوم عبارة الكرماني أن من قدر على الركوب ولم يركب يكون مسيئاً لتركه السنة فأفهم وإلا فقاعداً وهو يلي القيام في الفضيلة، ويكره الاضطجاع إلا من عذر كما هو مذكور كور في كتب المناسك ا هـ
His saying: (And that he stands on his mount). The wording of Matn al-Tanwir: 'And the imam stands on his she-camel.' Al-Madani said in his gloss: There is no specificity for the imam here; rather riding is recommended for every person standing at Arafat. The imam is only mentioned because he is followed in all rituals, since the Companions used to follow his action, and because when he stands riding, his heart is free from the side of the animal, so his heart is more tranquil in supplication and more sincere in intimate prayer. Sheikh Abdullah al-Afif said that. Then he said: In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, quoting from Mansak Ibn al-Ajami: It is disliked to stand on the back of an animal except in the case of standing at Arafat; rather it is superior for the imam and others. Ibn al-Hajj said in al-Madkhal: This place is excepted from what is prohibited of making the backs of animals as benches to sit on. And in Mansak Ibn al-Ajami: Whoever has no mount, the best is to stand standing; if he tires, he sits, and if he sits, it is permissible. The implication of al-Karmani's statement is that whoever can ride but does not ride is sinful for leaving the Sunnah? Understand, otherwise sitting, and it is next to standing in virtue, and lying down is disliked except for an excuse, as is mentioned in the books of rituals.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommendation of standing on a mount during wuquf at Arafat. The initial matn says 'and that he stands on his mount'. The sharh clarifies that this is not specific to the imam; it is sunnah for everyone. Various authorities are cited: al-Madani says it is recommended for all because it frees the heart for devotion. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj quotes a view that standing on an animal is disliked except at Arafat, where it is superior. However, the predominant view is that riding is sunnah. For those without a mount, standing is best, then sitting if tired. Lying down is disliked unless excused. The passage uses the term 'asá' (sinful) for leaving the sunnah, indicating that the later Hanafi position considers riding at Arafat a confirmed sunnah, leaving which is blameworthy.

Key Terms
الوقوف على الراحلة (al-wuquf 'ala al-rahilah): To stand (or remain) on a riding animal during the wuquf at Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible and equally virtuous.
B) It is disliked (makruh tanzihi).
C) He is considered to have left a sunnah, which is blameworthy (isa'ah).
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Riding at Arafat is a confirmed sunnah; those able should practice it for a more focused devotion.
