Virtue of Arafah on Friday
Discusses extra virtue of Arafah on Friday

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the extra virtue of Arafah coinciding with Friday, cite the supporting hadith and Ibn Jama'ah's five reasons, and state the Hanafi position that the obligation of Hajj remains unchanged.

Core Idea
Arafah on Friday is better than seventy Hajjs, but does not affect the obligation.

This passage explores the special merit when the Day of Arafah falls on Friday. The author quotes a hadith that such a standing is better than seventy ordinary Hajjs and that forgiveness is granted to all present. Five additional reasons for the virtue are provided by Ibn Jama'ah, but the key point is that this is about extra reward, not a change in the fiqh of Hajj. The lesson also includes a warning to avoid quarreling and foul speech to preserve the reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the virtue claimed
The passage states that when Arafah coincides with Friday, forgiveness is granted to all people of the standing and it is better than seventy Hajjs on other days.
This is a fada'il (virtue) matter, not a change in the ruling of wuquf.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The author cites a hadith reported by Razin: 'The best of days is the day of Arafah, and if it coincides with Friday, it is better than seventy Hajjs on other than Friday.' Another hadith mentions forgiveness on Friday for all people of the standing.
The hadith is of zanni thubut and dalala, so it encourages but does not create a new obligation.
3
Analyze the five reasons of Ibn Jama'ah
Ibn Jama'ah lists five aspects: (1-2) the two hadiths, (3) actions are honored by honor of time (Friday is best day of week), (4) the hour of acceptance on Friday, (5) the Prophet's Farewell Pilgrimage was on Friday.
These reasons explain the basis for the extra virtue from a broader perspective.
4
Note the caution about behavior
The author warns against quarreling, abuse, hostility, foul speech, and even excessive permissible talk on this day, as they can diminish the reward.
This is adab (etiquette) to preserve the spiritual benefit.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school affirms the virtue (it is sunnah to value this day) but emphasizes that the obligation of Hajj is not altered. The mufta bihi is to seize the opportunity for extra reward while maintaining proper conduct.
The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin; there is no ikhtilaf among schools on the virtue itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قيل إذا وافق يوم عرفة يوم جمعة غفر لكل أهل الوقف وأنه أفضل من سبعين حجة في غير يوم جمعة كما ورد في الحديث. وليحذر كل الحذر من المخاصمة والمشاتمة والمنافرة والكلام القبيح بل ومن المباح أيضاً في مثل هذا اليوم. قوله : (وقد قيل إذا وافق يوم عرفة الخ) قال الرملي : قال صلى الله عليه وسلم تعالى «أفضل الأيام يوم عرفة وإذا وافق يوم جمعة فهو أفضل من سبعين حجة في غير يوم جمعة» أخرجه رزين. وعن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم إذا كان يوم جمعة غفر الله تعالى لجميع أهل الموقف قال الشيخ عز الدين بن جماعة : سئل والدي عن وقفة الجمعة هل لها موزية على غيرها؟ فأجاب أن لها مزية على غيرها من خمسة أوجه الأول والثاني ما ذكرناه من الحديثين الثالث أن العمل يشرف بشرف الأزمنة كما يشرف بشرف الأمكنة، ويوم الجمعة أفضل أيام الأسبوع فوجب أن يكون العمل فيه أفضل، الرابع في يوم الجمعة ساعة لا يوافقها عبد مسلم يسأل الله تعالى شيئاً إلا أعطاه إياه وليست في غير يوم الجمعة ، الخامس موافقة النبي إن وقفته في حجة الوداع كانت يوم الجمعة وإنما يختار له الأفضل . قال والدي : أما من حيث إسقاط الفرض فلا مزية لها على غيرها وسأله بعض الطلبة فقال : قد جاء أن الله تعالى يغفر لجميع أهل الموقف، فما وجه تخصيص ذلك . الجمعة في الحديث يعني المتقدم؟ فأجابه بأنه بيوم يحتمل أن الله تعالى يغفر في يوم الجمعة بغير واسطة وفي غير يوم الجمعة يهب قوماً لقوم ا هـ. كذا في حاشية الشيخ نور الدين الزيادى الشافعي
And it has been said: if the day of Arafah coincides with Friday, forgiveness is granted to all the people of the standing, and it is better than seventy Hajjs on a day other than Friday, as reported in the hadith. And he should be very careful to avoid quarreling, abuse, hostility, and foul speech, even permissible talk, on such a day. His saying: (And it was said if the day of Arafah coincides with Friday, etc.) Ar-Ramli said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The best of days is the day of Arafah, and if it coincides with Friday, it is better than seventy Hajjs on other than Friday.' Reported by Razin. And from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When it is Friday, Allah forgives all the people of the standing.' Shaykh Izz ad-Din ibn Jama'ah said: My father was asked: Does the standing on Friday have any virtue over other days? He answered that it has virtue in five ways: first and second are the two hadiths mentioned; third, actions are honored by the honor of times as they are honored by places, and Friday is the best day of the week, so action on it is better; fourth, on Friday there is an hour when no Muslim asks Allah for anything but He gives it, which is not on other days; fifth, the Prophet's standing in the Farewell Pilgrimage was on Friday, and he only chooses the best for himself. My father said: As for the fulfillment of the obligation, there is no extra virtue over other days. Some students asked him: It has come that Allah forgives all people of the standing, so why is that specific to Friday in the hadith? He answered: It is possible that Allah forgives on Friday directly, and on other days He makes groups forgive each other. This is in the gloss of Shaykh Nur ad-Din az-Ziyadi ash-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This section adds a spiritual dimension: the day of Arafah falling on Friday has special merit. The author quotes hadith that it is equivalent to seventy ordinary Hajjs and that forgiveness is granted to all present. Ibn Jama'ah provides five reasons for the extra virtue, including the honor of Friday and the Prophetic example. Note that this extra virtue does not affect the obligation (the Hajj itself is already accepted); it is an additional blessing. The author also warns against arguments and foul speech, which can diminish the reward. The passage includes a Shafi'i source (az-Ziyadi), showing inter-madhhab respect. The Hanafi school accepts these virtues as part of the general encouragement for the day.

Key Terms
وقفة الجمعة (waqfatu al-jumu'ah): The standing at Arafat when it coincides with Friday.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many virtues does Ibn Jama'ah mention for the standing on Friday?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Arafah on Friday brings immense reward, but the fiqh of Hajj remains unchanged.

Departure from Arafat After Sunset: Wajib Ruling and Recommended Acts in Muzdalifah
Ruling on departure from Arafat and acts in Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on departure from Arafat, identify the consequence of violating it, and describe the recommended practices upon reaching Muzdalifah.

Core Idea
Departing Arafat before sunset requires a dam; after sunset, follow the Prophet's method including standing near Mount Qazh.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains two key points in Hajj: the wajib nature of leaving Arafat only after sunset, and the recommended actions upon arriving at Muzdalifah. The commentator expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, clarifying the proof from Sahih Muslim and detailing the Sunnah practices of walking, dhikr, and standing behind the imam. Understanding this distinction between wajib and mandub helps the pilgrim fulfill the rites correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is departing from Arafat to Muzdalifah after sunset. The Hanafi school rules this as wajib (obligatory), meaning leaving before sunset is a violation that requires a dam (sacrificial offering).
Wajib in Hanafi fiqh means established by a zanni dalil; violation incurs compensation but does not invalidate Hajj.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's consistent practice (fi'l) as recorded in Sahih Muslim. The commentator states 'as established in Sahih Muslim from him (peace be upon him).' This fi'l is interpreted as indicating obligation because it was done regularly and emphatically.
Hanafi usul: al-fi'l al-mutawatir or al-fi'l al-mustamir can indicate wujub if accompanied by qarinah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet (saw) always departed after sunset and never before, and he instructed others to do so. This continuous practice (along with the fact that he criticized those who departed early in other narrations) shows that departing after sunset is a required part of the Hajj sequence.
The Hanafi jurists derive wujub from the Prophet's action when there is no indication of permissibility for earlier departure.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that departing before sunset is permissible (makruh tanzihan) and does not require a dam. They consider the Prophet's action as sunnah, not wajib.
This ikhtilaf stems from differing usul principles: Hanafis give greater weight to the Prophet's customary practice as binding.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
If a pilgrim departs before sunset and leaves Arafat's boundaries, a dam is wajib. If the imam delays departure after sunset, the people should still depart to follow the Sunnah. A short stay after departure due to crowding is excusable; a long delay is blameworthy.
The text also covers etiquette: walking calmly, speeding up when possible, and entering Muzdalifah on foot with dhikr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم إلى مزدلفة بعد الغروب أي ثم رح كما ثبت في صحيح مسلم من عليه السلام، وهذا بيان للواجب حتى لو دفع قبل الغروب وجاوز حدود عرفة لزمه دم . وأشار إلى أن الإمام لو أبطأ بالدفع بعد الغروب. فإن الناس يدفعون لأنه لا موافقة في مخالفة السنة، ولو مكث بعد الغروب وبعد دفع الإمام وإن كان قليلاً لخوف الزحام فلا بأس به، وإن كان كثيراً كان مسيئاً لمخالفة السنة، والأفضل أن يمشي على هيئته وإذا وجد فرجة أسرع، ويستحب أن يدخل مزدلفة ماشياً وأن يكبر ويهلل ويحمد ويلبي ساعة فساعة قوله : وانزل بقرب جبل قزح يعني المشعر الحرام وهو غير منصرف للعدل والعلمية كعمر من قزح الشيء ارتفع يقال إنه كانون آدم عليه السلام وهو موقف الإمام كما رواه أبو داود. ولا ينبغي النزول على الطريق ولا الانفراد عن الناس فينزل عن يمينه أو يساره، ويستحب يقف وراء الإمام كالوقوف بعرفة
His saying: (Then to Muzdalifah after sunset) i.e., then depart, as established in Sahih Muslim from him (peace be upon him). This is an explanation of the obligatory (wajib) such that if he departs before sunset and passes beyond the boundaries of Arafat, a dam (sacrifice) is required of him. And he indicated that if the imam delays departure after sunset, the people should depart, because there is no agreement in opposing the Sunnah. And if he stays after sunset and after the imam's departure, even if for a short time due to fear of crowding, there is no harm; but if it is a long time, he is sinful for opposing the Sunnah. The best is that he walks in his normal pace, and if he finds a gap, he speeds up. And it is recommended to enter Muzdalifah walking, and to say takbir, tahlil, tahmid, and talbiyah from time to time. His saying: (And descend near Mount Qazh) meaning al-Mash'ar al-Haram. It is diptote due to being proper noun and feminine? Like 'Umar from qazh meaning something elevated. It is said it was the place where Adam (peace be upon him) was, and it is the standing place of the imam as reported by Abu Dawud. And he should not descend on the road nor be alone from the people; rather he descends to the right or left of them. And it is recommended to stand behind the imam like the standing at Arafat.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage covers two matn phrases: departing to Muzdalifah after sunset, and descending near Mount Qazh. Departure after sunset is wajib (a confirmed obligation); leaving before sunset without a valid reason requires dam (sacrifice). If the imam delays, the people should still depart according to the Sunnah. Staying a short while after departure due to crowd is acceptable, but a long delay is blameworthy. Upon reaching Muzdalifah, one should walk, engage in dhikr, and stand behind the imam. The second part recommends staying near Mount Qazh (al-Mash'ar al-Haram), which is the prophetic practice. The Hanafi position emphasizes following the footsteps of the Prophet and the imam.

Key Terms
الدفع بعد الغروب (ad-daf' ba'd al-ghurub): Departing from Arafat after sunset; wajib in Hajj.
جبل قزح (jabal quzah): A mountain in Muzdalifah, also called al-Mash'ar al-Haram, where the Prophet stood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling in the Hanafi school for a pilgrim who leaves Arafat before sunset?
A) No problem; it is permissible.
B) It is makruh but no sacrifice required.
C) It is a violation requiring a dam (sacrifice).
D) The hajj is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Departing from Arafat after sunset is a wajib act; violating it requires dam, while following the Sunnah in Muzdalifah brings reward.

Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah: One Adhan, No Nafl
Rulings on combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah with one adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah and identify which voluntary prayers are prohibited between them.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, Maghrib and Isha are combined with one adhan, and no voluntary prayer is offered between them.

This lesson examines a specific sunnah of Hajj: the method of praying Maghrib and Isha together at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi school follows the explicit practice of the Prophet, which includes a prohibition on any nafl between the two prayers. Understanding this ruling helps the pilgrim perform the ritual correctly and avoid common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah with jam' ta'khir. The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah), though some scholars consider it wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Ibn Umar in Muslim: the Prophet gave adhan for Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then iqamah, then prayed Isha with the first iqamah.
The hadith shows the method: one adhan and two iqamahs.
3
Understand the prohibition of nafl
The text explicitly states that no voluntary prayer (nafl) is allowed between Maghrib and Isha, not even the confirmed sunnah of Maghrib.
This is a specific ruling for Muzdalifah; normally, the sunnah of Maghrib is prayed after Maghrib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصل بالناس العشائين بأذان وإقامة) أي المغرب جمع تأخير لرواية مسلم عن ابن عمر أنه عليه السلام أذن للمغرب بجمع فأقام ثم صلى العشاء بالإقامة الأولى. وأشار إلى أنه لا تطوع بين الصلاتين ولو سنة مؤكدة
His saying: (And pray with the people the two evening prayers with one adhan and iqamah) i.e., Maghrib and Isha, combined with delay (jam' ta'khir) according to the narration of Muslim from Ibn Umar that he (peace be upon him) gave the adhan for Maghrib at Jama' (Muzdalifah), then gave iqamah, then prayed Isha with the first iqamah. And he indicated that there is no voluntary prayer between the two prayers, even if it is a confirmed sunnah.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage addresses the specific way of combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah in the Hajj. It is a sunnah practice (some say wajib) to pray both prayers together after sunset with one adhan and two iqamahs, or one adhan and two iqamahs as per the hadith. The matn says 'with one adhan and iqamah', but the sharh clarifies that there are two iqamahs: one for each prayer. The important point: no voluntary prayer (nafl) is to be offered between Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, not even the sunnah of Maghrib or Isha. This is a specific ruling for this occasion. The Hanafi school follows this, though some Imams differ. The wisdom is to emphasize the haste and focus on the ritual.

Key Terms
جمع تأخير (jam' ta'khir): Combining two prayers by delaying the first to the time of the second.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is recommended.
B) It is permissible but makruh.
C) It is prohibited; no voluntary prayer is allowed between them.
D) It is obligatory to pray them.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of combining at Muzdalifah includes the prohibition of any nafl between Maghrib and Isha.

Departure from Arafat to Muzdalifah After Sunset
Commentary on the obligation of departing Arafat after sunset

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on departing from Arafat after sunset and identify the penalty for early departure.

Core Idea
Departing Arafat after sunset is wajib; leaving early costs a dam.

In this lesson, we examine a key wajib action during Hajj: the departure from Arafat to Muzdalifah after sunset. The commentator explains that this act is based on the Prophet's practice, and failure to perform it correctly triggers a penalty. We will also see how the imam's timing affects the pilgrims and the recommended manner of travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is departing from Arafat towards Muzdalifah after sunset. Its ruling is wajib (obligatory), not merely sunnah or mustahab.
The Hanafi school uses 'wajib' for acts proven by zanni evidence.
2
Locate the proof
The commentator cites Sahih Muslim as evidence that the Prophet departed after sunset. This is a sunnah ahad, giving zanni certainty.
The exact hadith text is not quoted, but the reference establishes the act.
3
Understand the penalty for violation
If a pilgrim departs before sunset and leaves the boundaries of Arafat, a dam (sacrifice) is required as compensation.
The penalty is for omitting a wajib, not for invalidating the Hajj.
4
Analyze the imam's role
If the imam delays after sunset, the people should still depart to avoid opposing the sunnah. A short delay due to crowding is excusable, but a long delay is blameworthy.
Obedience to the imam does not override following the sunnah in this case.
5
Note the recommended conduct
Walking at a normal pace, speeding up when finding an opening, and entering Muzdalifah on foot while making dhikr (takbir, tahlil, tahmid, talbiyah) are recommended.
These are acts of sunnah that enhance the Hajj experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم إلى مزدلفة بعد الغروب أي ثم رح كما ثبت في صحيح مسلم من عليه السلام، وهذا بيان للواجب حتى لو دفع قبل الغروب وجاوز حدود عرفة لزمه دم . وأشار إلى أن الإمام لو أبطأ بالدفع بعد الغروب. فإن الناس يدفعون لأنه لا موافقة في مخالفة السنة، ولو مكث بعد الغروب وبعد دفع الإمام وإن كان قليلاً لخوف الزحام فلا بأس به، وإن كان كثيراً كان مسيئاً لمخالفة السنة، والأفضل أن يمشي على هيئته وإذا وجد فرجة أسرع، ويستحب أن يدخل مزدلفة ماشياً وأن يكبر ويهلل ويحمد ويلبي ساعة فساعة
He said: (Then to Muzdalifah after sunset) meaning then proceed as established in Sahih Muslim from him (peace be upon him), and this is an explanation of the wajib; so if he departed before sunset and passed the boundaries of Arafah, a dam is required of him. And he indicated that if the imam delays the departure after sunset, the people should depart because there is no obedience in opposing the sunnah. And if he stayed after sunset and after the imam's departure, even if a little due to fear of crowding, there is no problem, but if it was much, he is doing wrong due to opposing the sunnah. And it is best that he walks in his normal manner, and when he finds an opening, he speeds up. And it is recommended to enter Muzdalifah walking, and to say takbir, tahlil, tahmid, and talbiyah from time to time.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This is a commentary on the matn phrase 'ثم إلى مزدلفة بعد الغروب' (Then to Muzdalifah after sunset). The commentator explains that this ruling is for departing from Arafat after sunset, and it is a wajib. If one departs before sunset and leaves the boundaries of Arafah, he must offer a dam (sacrifice). If the imam delays the departure after sunset, the people should not wait for him because following the sunnah takes precedence. If one stays after sunset and after the imam's departure, even briefly due to crowding, it is permissible, but a long delay is blameworthy. The recommended manner of walking is moderate, with occasional speed to find an opening. It is sunnah to enter Muzdalifah walking while making dhikr.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required as a penalty for omitting a wajib in Hajj.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act proven by zanni evidence; omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must return and cannot perform Hajj that year.
B) He must offer a dam (sacrifice).
C) His Hajj is invalid.
D) He must give charity.

Key Takeaway
Departing from Arafat after sunset is a wajib; leaving early and exiting boundaries requires a dam.

Recommended Stay in Muzdalifah: Near Jabal Quzah
Commentary on recommended location and manner of staying in Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended location for staying in Muzdalifah and explain the sunnah manner of standing behind the imam.

Core Idea
Stay near Jabal Quzah (al-Mash'ar al-Haram) and stand behind the imam – this is sunnah, not wajib.

In Muzdalifah, the pilgrim is encouraged to stay near a specific landmark known as Jabal Quzah, identified as al-Mash'ar al-Haram. This is the place where the imam stands for the combined prayer and supplication. The Hanafi school emphasizes following this sunnah while avoiding isolation or obstructing the road.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act
The passage instructs the pilgrim to stay (nuzul) in Muzdalifah near Jabal Quzah. Recognize that this is a specific location within Muzdalifah.
Jabal Quzah is also called al-Mash'ar al-Haram.
2
Determine the hukm level
The text uses 'يستحب' (it is recommended), indicating that this act is sunnah (mandub), not wajib. In Hanafi fiqh, omitting a sunnah does not invalidate the Hajj but one misses a reward.
Compare with the standing at Arafah, which is a rukn.
3
Note the recommended manner
The pilgrim should not stay on the road (to avoid blocking traffic) and should not isolate from the people. He should stand to the right or left of the imam, and it is recommended to stand behind the imam, similar to the standing at Arafah.
Standing behind the imam is a sunnah; one may also stand beside him if space is limited.
4
Recognize the evidence
The commentator cites a hadith from Abu Dawud that Jabal Quzah is the standing place of the imam. This is the basis for the recommendation.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim but referenced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وانزل بقرب جبل قزح يعني المشعر الحرام وهو غير منصرف للعدل والعلمية كعمر من قزح الشيء ارتفع يقال إنه كانون آدم عليه السلام وهو موقف الإمام كما رواه أبو داود. ولا ينبغي النزول على الطريق ولا الانفراد عن الناس فينزل عن يمينه أو يساره، ويستحب يقف وراء الإمام كالوقوف بعرفة
He said: (And stay near Jabal Quzah) meaning al-Mash'ar al-Haram, and it is diptote due to being both a proper noun and feminine-like, like 'Umar; from qazaha (to rise), it is said it was the oven of Adam (peace be upon him), and it is the standing place of the imam as narrated by Abu Dawud. And one should not stay on the road nor separate from the people, rather he should stay to its right or left, and it is recommended to stand behind the imam like the standing at Arafah.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This is a commentary on the matn phrase 'وانزل بقرب جبل قزح' (And stay near Jabal Quzah). The commentator identifies Jabal Quzah as al-Mash'ar al-Haram (the sacred monument). It is the place where the imam stands for the prayer and dua in Muzdalifah, as reported by Abu Dawud. One should avoid staying on the road or isolating from the people; rather, he should stand to the right or left of the imam. It is recommended to stand behind the imam, similar to the standing at Arafah.

Key Terms
المشعر الحرام (al-Mash'ar al-Haram): The sacred monument in Muzdalifah, identified as Jabal Quzah, where the imam stands.
غير منصرف (ghayr munṣarif): A noun that is diptote (does not take tanwin) due to being a proper noun and having feminine-like gender.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Combining Maghrib and Isha in Muzdalifah
Commentary on the ruling of combining Maghrib and Isha in Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining Maghrib and Isha in Muzdalifah, identify the conditions and consequences, and explain the prohibition of voluntary prayers between them.

Core Idea
In Muzdalifah, Maghrib is delayed and combined with Isha with one adhan and iqamah; no voluntary prayer is allowed between them.

The night at Muzdalifah is a unique moment in Hajj, where the Prophet ﷺ combined Maghrib and Isha with a single adhan and iqamah. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling based on the hadith, explains why no voluntary prayers are permitted between the two obligatory prayers, and clarifies practical points such as the repetition of iqamah if one prays voluntary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The matn instructs the imam to combine Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and iqamah. Understand that this is jam' ta'khir (deferring Maghrib to Isha time), and it is a wajib of Hajj.
Omission requires a dam (sacrifice).
2
Examine the dalil
The commentator cites the hadith from Ibn 'Umar in Sahih Muslim: the Prophet gave adhan for Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then iqamah, then prayed Isha with the first iqamah. This is the proof for combining with one adhan.
The hadith is ahad, so the ruling is wajib not fard.
3
Understand the prohibition of voluntary prayers
The text states there is no tatawwu' between the two prayers, not even a confirmed sunnah. If one prays voluntary, the iqamah must be repeated, just as for any other distracting action.
This is specific to Muzdalifah; normally sunnah prayers are allowed between Maghrib and Isha.
4
Note the differences from the jam' at Arafah
At Arafah, the jam' requires an imam and is considered qada' for Zuhr and ada' for Asr. At Muzdalifah, no imam is required (though congregation is better), and Isha is ada' while Maghrib is qada'.
This is because Muzdalifah's jam' is due to the ritual, not travel, so it applies to residents of Makkah and others.
5
Appreciate the virtue of the night
The night of Muzdalifah combines the honor of place and time; one should strive to revive it with prayer, recitation, dhikr, and supplication.
The commentator encourages praying before unloading the load.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصل بالناس العشائين بأذان وإقامة) أي المغرب جمع تأخير لرواية مسلم عن ابن عمر أنه عليه السلام أذن للمغرب بجمع فأقام ثم صلى العشاء بالإقامة الأولى. وأشار إلى أنه لا تطوع بين الصلاتين ولو سنة مؤكدة على الصحيح ولو تطوع بينهما أعاد الإقامة كما لو اشتغل بينهما بعمل آخر : وفي الهداية : وكان أن يعاد الأذان كما في الجمع الأول إلا أنا اكتفينا بإعادة الإقامة لما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى المغرب بمزدلفة ثم تعشى ثم أفرد الإقامة بالعشاء، وإلى أن هذا الجمع لا يختص بالمسافر لأنه جمع بسب النسك فيجوز لأهل مكة ومزدلفة ومنى ،وغيرهم، وإلى أن هذا الجمع لا يشترط فيه الإمام كما شرط في الجمع المتقدم لأن العشاء تقع أداء في وقتها والمغرب قضاء، والأفضل أن يصليهما مع الإمام بجماعة. وينبغي أن يصلي الفرض قبل حط رحله بل ينيخ جماله ويعقلها، وهذه ليلة جمعت شرف المكان والزمان فينبغي أن يجتهد في إحيائها بالصلاة والتلاوة والذكر والتضرع
He said: (And lead the people in the two evening prayers with one adhan and iqamah) meaning Maghrib deferred (jam' ta'khir) according to the narration of Muslim from Ibn 'Umar that he (peace be upon him) gave adhan for Maghrib at Jam' (Muzdalifah), then iqamah, then prayed 'Isha with the first iqamah. And he indicated that there is no voluntary prayer between the two prayers, even a confirmed sunnah, according to the correct opinion. And if one prays voluntary between them, he must repeat the iqamah, just as if he engaged in another action between them. In al-Hidayah: the adhan should be repeated as in the first jam', but we suffice with repeating the iqamah due to the report that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then had dinner, then gave a separate iqamah for 'Isha. And [he indicated] that this jam' is not specific to travelers because it is a jam' due to the ritual (nusk), so it is permissible for the people of Makkah, Muzdalifah, Mina, and others. And that this jam' does not require an imam unlike the earlier jam' (at Arafah) because 'Isha is performed in its actual time and Maghrib is qada'. And it is better to pray them with the imam in congregation. And he should pray the obligatory prayer before unloading his load, rather he should kneel his camels and hobble them. And this night combines the honor of place and time, so one should strive to revive it with prayer, recitation, dhikr, and supplication.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This commentary explains the Hajj ritual of combining Maghrib and Isha in Muzdalifah. The matn instructs the imam to lead the two prayers with one adhan and iqamah. The commentator clarifies that Maghrib is delayed and combined with Isha (jam' ta'khir) based on a hadith from Muslim that the Prophet gave adhan for Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then iqamah, then prayed Isha with the same iqamah. It is not permissible to pray any voluntary prayer between them, even a confirmed sunnah. If one does so, he must repeat the iqamah. This combination is specific to the Hajj ritual, not to travel, so it applies to residents of Makkah and others present. It does not require an imam, but praying in congregation is better. One should pray before setting up camp. The night of Muzdalifah is highly virtuous, so one should engage in worship.

Key Terms
جمع تأخير (jam' ta'khir): Delaying the first prayer (Maghrib) to be performed together with the second (Isha) in the time of the second.
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary prayer; here specifically sunnah prayers between the obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is recommended.
B) It is permissible but not recommended.
C) It is not allowed; if done, the iqamah must be repeated.
D) It is required.

Key Takeaway
Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah is a wajib act of Hajj performed with one adhan and iqamah, with no voluntary prayers allowed between them.

Maghrib Prayer Not Permissible on the Way to Muzdalifah
Commentary on the prohibition of Maghrib before Muzdalifah with proof and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on Maghrib prayer before reaching Muzdalifah, apply the exception for fear of dawn, and explain the requirement to repeat the prayer.

Core Idea
Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah is prohibited unless you fear missing the time.

During Hajj, the pilgrim must combine Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. This lesson explores the ruling that Maghrib cannot be prayed before arrival, the proof from the Prophet's practice, and the consequences if one neglects this ruling. You will also learn the exceptional circumstance that permits praying on the way.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying Maghrib (and by extension Isha) while still on the way to Muzdalifah, i.e., before reaching the destination. The ruling is that it is not permissible (makruh tahrimi).
The text uses 'لم تجز' meaning 'not permissible'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'الصلاة أمامك' (the prayer is ahead of you), narrated when the Prophet was asked to pray on the way. This indicates that the proper place is Muzdalifah.
This is a sunnah ahad, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's response implies that the prayer should be delayed until reaching Muzdalifah. By analogy (qiyas awwali), if it is not permissible in Arafah (a closer point), it is even more emphatic on the way.
The commentary applies the principle of 'first argument' (بالطريق الأولى).
4
Note exceptions
If the pilgrim fears that dawn will break before reaching Muzdalifah, it becomes permissible to pray on the way because otherwise the prayer would become qada (missed).
This exception is based on necessity (darurah).
5
Evaluate consequences of violation
If one prays on the way without necessity, the prayer is makruh tahrimi and must be repeated (i'ada) as long as it is still night (before dawn). After dawn, repetition is waived because the purpose of combining is lost.
The repetition is wajib according to the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولم تجز المغرب في الطريق أي لم تحل صلاة المغرب قبل الوصول إلى مزدلفة للحديث الصلاة أمامك قاله حين قيل له الصلاة يا رسول الله وهو في طريق مزدلفة أي وقتها فدل كلامه أنها لا تحل بعرفات بالطريق الأولى. وأشار إلى أن العشاء لا تحل بالطريق الأولى وإن كان بعد دخول وقتها لأن صاحبة الوقت وهي المغرب إذا كانت لا تحل به فغيرها أولى. ولما كان وقت هاتين الصلاتين وقت العشاء علم أنه لو خاف طلوع الفجر جاز أن يصليهما في الطريق لأنه لو لم يصلهما لصارتا قضاء وإذا لم يحل له أداؤهما بالطريق فإذا صلاهما أو إحداهما فقد ارتكب كراهة التحريم فكل صلاة أديت معها وجب إعادتها فيجب إعادتهما ما لم يطلع الفجر، فإن طلع سقطت الإعادة لأن الإعادة للجمع بينهما
He said: (And Maghrib is not permissible on the way) meaning Maghrib prayer is not permissible before reaching Muzdalifah due to the hadeeth 'The prayer is ahead of you' which he said when it was said to him 'The prayer, O Messenger of Allah' while he was on the way to Muzdalifah, meaning its time [is later], so his words indicate that it is not permissible in Arafah a fortiori. And he indicated that Isha is also not permissible on the way a fortiori, even if its time has entered, because the owner of the time - Maghrib - if it is not permissible there, then others are even more so. And since the time of these two prayers is the time of Isha, it is known that if he fears the dawn, it is permissible to pray them on the way because if he does not pray them, they become qada. And since it is not permissible for him to perform them on the way, if he prays them or one of them, he has committed a makruh tahrimi, so every prayer performed under this circumstance must be repeated; so he must repeat them as long as dawn has not risen. If dawn rises, repeating is waived because the repetition was for combining them.
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This commentary explains the matn 'ولم تجز المغرب في الطريق' (Maghrib is not permissible on the way). The pilgrim must pray Maghrib in Muzdalifah, not on the road or in Arafah. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet said 'The prayer is ahead of you' when asked to pray on the way to Muzdalifah. This shows that Maghrib cannot be prayed before reaching Muzdalifah, and by extension, Isha also cannot be prayed on the way. However, if one fears that the dawn will break before reaching Muzdalifah, it is permissible to pray on the way to avoid missing the prayer entirely. But if one prays on the way without such fear, it is makruh tahrimi and the prayer must be repeated unless dawn has risen, in which case repetition is waived because the purpose (combining) is no longer possible.

Key Terms
كراهة التحريم (karahah tahrimiyah): A prohibition close to haram; the act is sinful but not as severe as haram.
الصلاة أمامك (al-salatu amamaka): The prayer (i.e., its proper place/time) is ahead of you, meaning at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim prays Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah without fear of dawn, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer is makruh tahrimi and must be repeated if still night.
D) The prayer is haram and cannot be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Maghrib and Isha must be prayed in Muzdalifah; praying on the way is makruh tahrimi and requires repetition unless dawn rises.

Ruling on Praying Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah
Explains the rules and proofs for combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Maghrib and Isha to Muzdalifah, explain the evidence from the hadith 'al-salat amamaka', and apply the rule that praying early requires i'ada before dawn.

Core Idea
Praying Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah is valid but makruh tahrimi and must be repeated unless dawn breaks.

When performing Hajj, the Prophet's practice at Muzdalifah provides a unique ruling: Maghrib and Isha are to be delayed and combined there, even though other schools treat this as a travel concession. The Hanafi school relies on a specific hadith and its acceptance by the early community to establish this rule. In this lesson, we will trace the legal reasoning from the text of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and understand the consequences if a pilgrim prays before reaching Muzdalifah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is praying Maghrib (and similarly Isha) on the road to Muzdalifah, before arriving. The text states 'la tajuz' (it is not permissible), which in Hanafi fiqh means makruh tahrimi – the prayer is valid but sinful, and repetition is required.
This is not a ruling of invalidity (batil) but of prohibition of the timing/place.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith 'al-salat amamaka' (the prayer is ahead of you), which the Prophet ﷺ said when asked to pray on the way to Muzdalifah. This indicates that the proper place for the prayer is Muzdalifah, not the road.
The hadith is narrated in al-Bukhari from Ibn Mas'ud (as an action), and it is classified as ahad but became mashhur through acceptance by the early community.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative word 'amamaka' (ahead of you) points to a spatial directive – the time for prayer has not fully arrived until you reach Muzdalifah. The Prophet ﷺ effectively delayed the prayer to its proper location, indicating that praying earlier is not permitted.
The text also infers that Isha is even more restricted, since its time has technically entered but the 'owner of the time' (Maghrib) is not permitted yet.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
An objection is raised: this hadith is ahad, so how can it override the Quranic verse 'Inna al-salata kanat ala al-mu’minina kitaban mawquta' (al-Nisa 103) which seems to require fixed, invariable times? The Hanafi response is that the hadith is not a simple ahad but mashhur – widely accepted and acted upon by the early community, thus it can specify the general verse.
The issue is not abrogation but takhsis (specification). The verse itself does not specify the exact limits; the Sunnah provides the details.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on this ruling as mufta bihi because the evidence is strong: the hadith, supported by the practice of the Companions and the early community, outweighs the general implication of the verse. Therefore, delaying to Muzdalifah is wajib, and praying early is makruh tahrimi with required i'ada unless dawn breaks.
If dawn breaks, the i'ada is dropped because the time for the correct combination has passed.

عبارة العناية الشيخ بعد خمساً . في وقت العشاء وقد خرج. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : ثم ههنا مسألة لا بد من معرفتها وهو أنه لو قدم العشاء على المغرب بمزدلفة يصلي المغرب ثم يعيد العشاء، فإن لم يعد العشاء حتى انفجر الصبح عاد العشاء إلى الجواز، وهذا كما قال أبو حنيفة فيمن ترك صلاة الظهر ثم صلى وهو ذاكر للمتروكة لم يجز، فإن صلى السادسة عاد إلى الجواز. واعلم أن المشايخ صرحوا في كتبهم بعدم الجواز وهو يوهم عدم الصحة وليس بمراد بل المراد عدم الحل ولهذا صرحوا بالإعادة. ولو كانت باطلة لكان أداء إن كان في الوقت وقضاء إن كان خارجه، ولو صرحوا بعدم الحل لزال الاشتباه وحاصل دليلهم المقتضي لعدم الحل أنه ظني مفيد تأخير وقت المغرب في خصوص هذه الليلة ليتوصل إلى الجمع بمزدلفة، فعملنا بمقتضاه ما لم يلزم ، الرحمن المرشدي في شرحه وأقرها . كذا في حاشيته المدني على الدرر قوله : (ثم ههنا مسألة الخ) قال الرملي : فيه وصلى الوتر جاز لسقوط الترتيب به، وهذا عند أ أبي حنيفة لأنه فرض عنده فصار كفرضين اجتمعا في وقت واحد كالقضائين أو القضاء والأداء فينبغي أن يكون في تقديم صلاة العشاء على المغرب هنا كذلك إذ لا موجب لسقوط الترتيب وبانفجار الصبح لم تدخل الفوائت في حد الكثرة ا هـ . قلت : وهذا خلاف الظاهر بل المتبادر سقوط الترتيب هنا أيضاً ولذا قال في حواشي مسكين : تزاد هذه على ما يسقط به الترتيب قوله : (وهو يوهم عدم الصحة) قال في النهر : أنى يتوهم عدم الصحة للصلاة بعد دخول وقتها ا هـ . ونأمله مع ما مر عن السراج. وقوله في حديث «الصلاة أمامك» أي وقتها أفلا يتوهم معه ذلك؟ وقال الرملي : كيف لا يتوهم والجواز مشترك بين الصحة والحل، وإذا قلنا أنى يتوهم عدم ا الصحة بعد دخول الوقت قلنا : أنى يتوهم عدم الحل بعد دخوله كما هو ظاهر فالتوهم هنا لا ينكر قوله : (لكان أداء أي لكان فعلها ثانياً أداء إن كان في الوقت الخ قوله : (وحاصل دليلهم الخ) خطر لي هنا إشكال وهو أن الحديث المفيد تأخير المغرب إذا كان ظنياً وكان الدليل والموجب للمحافظة على الوقت قطعياً لم يجز تأخير المغرب عن وقتها الثابت بالقطعي والإلزام تقديم الظني عليه مع أنه لا قائل بعدم جواز تأخیره بل بوجوبه ، ولا محيص حينئذ إلا بدعوى عدم ظنية الحديث أو عدم قطعية دلالة الآية . وإذا كان كذلك لا يتم قوله «فعملنا بمقتضاه الخ وبه يتأيد بحث المحقق. ثم رأيت في العناية قال ما نصه : واعترض بأن هذا الحديث من الآحاد فكيف يجوز أن يبطل به قوله تعالى إن الصلاة كانت على المؤمنين كتاباً موقوتاً [النساء : ۱۰۳] وأجاب شيخ شيخي العلامة بأنه من المشاهير تلقته الأمة بالقبول في Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: At Mount Quzah, he led the people in the two night prayers with adhan and iqamah, and it is not permissible to pray Maghrib on the way. Then it is correct to pray the obligatory prayer before unloading his load, rather he should make his camel kneel and tie it. If he performs a supererogatory prayer between them, he repeats the iqamah, just as if he engaged in another action between them. In Al-Hidayah: It would be to repeat the adhan as in the first combination, except that we suffice with repeating the iqamah due to the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then ate dinner, then gave the iqamah alone for Isha. And this combination is not specific to the traveler because it is a combination due to the ritual, so it is permissible for the people of Makkah, Muzdalifah, Mina, and others. And this combination does not require the imam, as is required in the preceding combination, because Isha is performed as an actual prayer in its time and Maghrib is a makeup. It is better to pray them with the imam in congregation. He should pray the obligatory prayer before unloading his load, rather he should make his camel kneel and tie it. This night combines the honor of place and time, so he should strive to revive it with prayer, recitation, remembrance, and supplication. His statement: (And Maghrib is not permissible on the way) means it is not permissible to pray Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah due to the hadith: 'The prayer is ahead of you' he said when it was said to him: 'Prayer, O Messenger of God' while he was on the road to Muzdalifah, meaning its time. So his speech indicates that it is even less permissible at Arafat. And he indicated that Isha is even less permissible on the way, even if its time has entered, because the owner of the time, Maghrib, when it is not permissible there, then others are even more so. Since the time of these two prayers is the time of Isha, it is known that if he fears the break of dawn, it is permissible to pray them on the road because if he does not pray them, they would become makeup. And since it is not permissible for him to perform them on the road, if he prays them or one of them, he has committed a disliked act of prohibition (karahah tahrimiyyah). So every prayer performed with that requires repetition, so he must repeat both, unless the dawn breaks. If it breaks, the repetition is dropped because the repetition is for combining them. From him, Maghrib, Maghrib, Isha, and Witr after it, as stated by our master Abd al-Rahman al-Jami (may God sanctify his secret) in his Manasik. Likewise in Sharh al-Lubab by al-Qari. His statement: (Due to the narration that the Prophet etc.) There is no basis for this from the Messenger of God (may God bless him and grant him peace), rather it is in al-Bukhari from Ibn Mas'ud that he did it, and similarly Ibn Abi Shaybah recorded it, and its completion is in al-Fath. His statement: (And Maghrib is a makeup) was refuted in al-Nahr by what is in al-Siraj, that he intends performance (ada') not makeup. I say: It is indicated by the author's later statement: 'Since the time of these two prayers is the time of Isha' etc., and also what comes later that the speculative evidence indicates the delay of the time of Maghrib, i.e., that it does not exit with the entry of Isha's time specifically on this night. His statement: (And this night combines the honor of place and time) said in al-Nahr: The question has arisen about its honor over Friday night, and I was one who inclined to that, then I saw in al-Jawhara that it is the best night of the year. The author's statement: (And Maghrib is not permissible on the way) said al-Allamah al-Shihawi in his Manasik: This ruling we mentioned regarding Maghrib prayer on the road is only when one goes to Muzdalifah via its path. But if one goes to Mecca via a path other than the Muzdalifah path, it is permissible for him to pray Maghrib on the road without hesitation. I have not found anyone explicitly stating that except the author of al-Nihayah and al-Inayah in the chapter on making up missed prayers, and the statement of the commentator of al-Kanz indicates it - a beneficial point. Similarly, it is explicitly stated in al-Binayah in that chapter. I found it in the margin of my copy of al-Kanz in the handwriting of the scholar Sheikh Ibrahim Abu Salamah. And the Sheikh later quoted the phrase from al-Inayah after five. [Note: Text becomes unclear] In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: Then here is an issue that must be known: that if one prays Isha before Maghrib at Muzdalifah, he prays Maghrib and then repeats Isha. If he does not repeat Isha until dawn breaks, Isha returns to permissibility. This is like Abu Hanifah's position on one who misses Zuhr and then prays while remembering the missed prayer, it does not suffice. If he prays the sixth, it returns to permissibility. Know that the scholars explicitly state in their books that it is not permissible, and this may give the impression of invalidity, but that is not intended; rather the intended meaning is non-permissibility (lack of allowance). That is why they explicitly stated the repetition. If it were invalid, it would be considered performance (ada') if within the time and makeup if outside. If they had stated non-permissibility explicitly, the confusion would be removed. The essence of their evidence for non-permissibility is that it is speculative evidence indicating the delay of Maghrib's time specifically on this night to achieve the combination at Muzdalifah. So we act on its implication as long as it does not necessitate something else. Al-Rahman al-Murshidi in his commentary and confirmed it. Likewise in his hashiah al-Madani on al-Durar. His statement: (Then here is an issue etc.) said al-Ramli: There is a problem in it, which is that it involves loss of order (tartib), which is an obligatory element whose loss invalidates permissibility, like the order of Witr after Isha. If it is taken at face value, it is problematic, unless it is taken as an omission of order or that it returns to permissibility if one prays five after it. That is because Maghrib and Isha have their time as the time of Isha, so they are two prayers that coincide in one time. It has been mentioned earlier regarding Witr and Isha that order is obligatory between them. They said: There, one should not pray Witr before Isha due to order, not because the time of Witr has not entered, so that if one forgets Isha and prays Witr, it is permissible because order lapses. This is according to Abu Hanifah because it is an obligatory (fard) in his view, so it becomes like two obligatory prayers that coincide in one time, like two makeups or a makeup and an actual prayer. Accordingly, it should be the same in the case of praying Isha before Maghrib here, since there is no reason for the lapse of order, and with the break of dawn, the missed prayers have not entered the category of many. I say: This contradicts the apparent; rather, the obvious is that order also lapses here. Therefore, it is said in the marginal notes of Miskin: This case is added to those in which order lapses. His statement: (And it may give the impression of invalidity) said in al-Nahr: How can one imagine invalidity for a prayer after its time has entered? I say: We consider this with what has been mentioned from al-Siraj. And his statement in the hadith: 'The prayer is ahead of you' means its time. Does that not lead one to imagine that? Al-Ramli said: How can one not imagine it, when permissibility (jawaz) is common between validity (sihha) and permissibility (hill)? And if we say: How can one imagine invalidity after the time has entered, we say: How can one imagine non-permissibility after the time has entered, as is apparent. So the imagination here is not denied. His statement: (It would be performance (ada') i.e., his second act would be performance if within the time etc. His statement: (The essence of their evidence etc.) Here an issue occurred to me: that if the hadith indicating the delay of Maghrib is speculative (zanni), and the evidence requiring preservation of the time is definitive (qat'i), then it is not permissible to delay Maghrib from its time established by definitive evidence, and it would be an obligation to give precedence to the speculative over it, while no one says it is not permissible to delay; rather, they say it is obligatory. There is no escape except by claiming that the hadith is not speculative or that the indication of the verse is not definitive. If so, his statement 'we act on its implication' is not valid, and this strengthens the investigation of the verifier. Then I saw in al-Inayah where he says: It was objected that this hadith is ahad, so how can it abrogate the statement of Allah: 'Indeed, prayer has been upon the believers a book of prescribed times' (al-Nisa 103)? And the teacher of my teacher, al-Allamah, answered that it is among the well-known (mashhur) hadiths that the early community accepted and acted upon, so it is permissible to use it to add to the Book of Allah. And I say: The verse 'Indeed, prayer has been upon the believers a book of prescribed times' and similar verses do not contain a definitive indication of the specific times; rather, their indication is that prayers have times.
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the rules of combining Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah during Hajj. The author begins by stating the ruling: the imam leads the people in both the Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah with adhan and iqamah, and it is not permissible (la tajuz) to pray Maghrib on the way before reaching Muzdalifah. He explains that if one performs a supererogatory prayer between the two, he must repeat the iqamah, citing the authority of al-Hidayah. The proof for the iqamah only (not adhan) is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who prayed Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then ate, then gave iqamah for Isha only. The author then clarifies that this combination is not specific to travelers but is due to the ritual (nasak), so residents of Makkah, Muzdalifah, and Mina may also combine. Unlike the combination at Arafah (where the imam is required), this combination does not require an imam because Isha is performed in its actual time while Maghrib is considered qada' (makeup). The better practice is to pray in congregation with the imam. The author stresses the virtue of praying before unloading and settling down. The key proof cited is the hadith 'al-salat amamaka' (the prayer is ahead of you) which the Prophet said when asked to pray on the way to Muzdalifah, indicating that one should not pray until reaching Muzdalifah. This implies that praying at Arafat is even more forbidden. The author clarifies that if one fears missing the time due to dawn approaching, it becomes permissible to pray on the way to avoid qada'. However, if one prays without necessity, it is makruh tahrimi and requires repetition (i'ada) unless dawn breaks. The passage then enters into detailed discussions: the refutation of the notion that Maghrib is qada' (it is ada' with the niyyah of ada'), the issue of tartib (order) between Maghrib and Isha when one mistakenly prays Isha first, and the crucial usul al-fiqh objection that the hadith (being ahad) cannot overrule the Quranic verse about fixed prayer times. The author responds by noting that the hadith is mashhur and widely accepted by the early community, thus it can specify (not abrogate) the general verse. He further argues that the verse does not definitively prescribe specific timings, so the hadith provides the details. Overall, this passage is a dense legal analysis typical of Hanafi fiqh, balancing textual evidence, rational reasoning (qiyas, istihsan), and the authority of early practice.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two prayers (Maghrib and Isha) at Muzdalifah, not in the sense of shortening but delaying until the same time.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Order between prayers; here, the order between Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah; if one prays Isha first, the order is lost and may affect validity.
أداء (ada'): Performing a prayer within its prescribed time; Maghrib at Muzdalifah is considered ada' with the intention of ada', not qada'.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a prayer after its time; sometimes thought that Maghrib at Muzdalifah is qada', but the author clarifies it is not.
إعادة (i'ada): Repetition of a prayer due to a flaw in its performance; here, if Maghrib is prayed early without necessity, it must be repeated at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pilgrim prays Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah (without necessity), what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil) and must be repeated with the intention of qada'
B) The prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi, and must be repeated unless dawn breaks
C) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed because it was performed in its time
D) The prayer is valid only if prayed with the imam

Key Takeaway
Delaying Maghrib and Isha to Muzdalifah is a confirmed sunnah; praying early is valid but makruh tahrimi and requires repetition before dawn.

The Suspended Invalidity: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Praying Before Muzdalifah
Intra-Hanafi dispute with talil (reasoning)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of mawquf (suspended ruling) as applied to the Hajj prayer dispute and state the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A prayer before Muzdalifah is invalid, but its invalidity is suspended until the proper time passes.

The Hajj combines many unique legal rulings, including the obligation to perform Maghrib and Isha together at Muzdalifah. But what if a pilgrim prays them on the road before arriving? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute where the majority, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, hold the prayer invalid and require a repeat, while Abu Yusuf considers it valid albeit blameworthy. At the heart of the disagreement is a subtle concept: suspended invalidity (al-fasad al-mawquf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine exactly what action is being ruled upon: praying Maghrib (or Isha) before reaching Muzdalifah during Hajj. Understand the Hanafi position that this act is not valid (lam yujzih).
Ruling relates to validity (sihhah), not mere permissibility (jawaz).
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues that if the prayer were valid, no repetition is needed; if invalid, it must be repeated immediately. His logic is binary: an act cannot change from invalid to valid over time.
Common-sense critique: what is invalid remains invalid.
3
Understand the Hanafi response: suspended invalidity
The majority respond that the invalidity is suspended (mawquf) — its effect appears only later. Similar to the issue of tarteeb (order) where a later act can 'validate' an earlier one under certain conditions.
The prayer is not definitively invalid at the moment of performance; its status depends on whether the pilgrim later reaches Muzdalifah in time.
4
Trace the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the prayer is invalid and must be repeated before Fajr. For Abu Yusuf: it is valid, but the pilgrim has done wrong (asa'a) and no repetition is needed.
The difference is not merely theoretical but affects whether the pilgrim must pray again.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text indicates that the majority view (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, Hasan) is the relied-upon position. Abu Yusuf's view is considered weak in this regard.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the analogy with the tarteeb case and the authority of the majority.

وشكك عن أبي يوسف أي أورد إشكالاً من جانبه على صاحبيه بأن صلاة المغرب التي صلاها في الطريق إما أن وقعت صحيحة أو لا، فإن كان الأول فلا تجب الإعادة لا في الوقت ولا بعده، وإن كان الثاني وجبت فيه وبعده لأن ما وقع فاسداً لا ينقلب صحيحاً بمضي الوقت . وأجيب بأن الفساد موقوف يظهر أثره في ثاني الحال كما مر في مسألة الترتيب ا هـ. هذا ويؤخذ من هذا الجواب أن مرادهم من عدم الجواز عدم الصحة لأنه لا فرق بين الفساد والبطلان في العبادات وهو ظاهر ما في الهداية حيث قال : ومن صلى المغرب في الطريق لم يجزه عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمه الله وعليه إعادتها ما لم يطلع الفجر . وقال أبو يوسف : يجزئه وقد أساء ا اه. لأن قوله «لم يجزه» من الإجزاء لا من الجواز، والذي يطلق على الحل الثاني لا الأول. و قول المؤلف ولو كانت باطلة الخ» جوابه ما علمت من أن البطلان غير باتٍ بل هو موقوف، ويدل عليه ما نقله عن الظهيرية وتنظيره بمن ترك الظهر الخ فإن البطلان في المقيس عليه غير بات نعم ظاهر ما في النهاية يوافق ما ذكره المؤلف حيث نظر وجوب الإعادة هنا بما إذا صلى الظهر في منزله يوم الجمعة قوله : ( وفي المحيط لو صلاهما بعد ما جاوز المزدلفة جاز) نقله في شرح اللباب عن المنتفى ثم قال : وهو خلاف ما عليه الجمهور. وقال أيضاً : وإذا ثبت وجوب هذا الجمع بمزدلفة في وقت العشاء، فلو صلى المغرب في وقتها أو العشاء
He doubted on behalf of Abu Yusuf, i.e., he raised an objection from his side against his two companions that the Maghrib prayer that he prayed on the road is either valid or not. If the first, then repetition is not obligatory neither in the time nor after it; if the second, then it is obligatory in it and after it because what occurred as invalid cannot become valid by the passing of time. And it was answered that invalidity is suspended, its effect appears in the second state as passed in the issue of order. End. This, and it is taken from this answer that their meaning of non-permissibility is invalidity because there is no difference between corruption and nullity in acts of worship. And that is apparent in Al-Hidayah where it said: Whoever prays Maghrib on the road, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and he must repeat it before Fajr. And Abu Yusuf said: It is valid and he has done wrong. End. Because his statement 'it is not valid' is from validity, not from permissibility, which is applied to the second meaning, not the first. And the author's statement 'even if it were invalid etc.' its answer is what you learned that invalidity is not conclusive but is suspended, and it is indicated by what he transmitted from Al-Zahiriyyah and his analogy with the one who left Dhuhr etc., for invalidity in the analogized case is not conclusive. Yes, apparent in Al-Nihayah agrees with what the author mentioned where he considered the obligation of repetition here similar to if one prayed Dhuhr in his house on Friday. His statement: (In Al-Muhit: If he prayed both after having passed Muzdalifah, it is permissible) He transmitted it in Sharh al-Lubab from Al-Muntafa then said: It is contrary to what the majority are upon. And he also said: When the obligation of this combination at Muzdalifah in the time of Isha is established, then if he prayed Maghrib in its time or Isha
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling for a pilgrim who prays Maghrib and Isha before reaching Muzdalifah during Hajj. The text begins by relating a doubt (shakk) raised on behalf of Abu Yusuf against Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf argues logically: if the prayer was valid, no repetition is needed; if invalid, it must be repeated in its time or later. The response is that the invalidity is suspended (mawquf) and only becomes apparent later, similar to the issue of order (tarteeb). The commentator explains that the term 'la yujzihi' in Al-Hidayah refers to non-validity (adam al-sihhah), not mere permissibility. The settled position of the school is that such a prayer is invalid and must be repeated before Fajr, while Abu Yusuf holds it valid but disliked. The text then mentions a minority view from Al-Muhit that if one prays after passing Muzdalifah, it is permissible, but this is against the majority. The passage concludes with a conditional statement about the obligation of combining at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
الفساد (al-fasad): Invalidity of an act of worship; in this context, the prayer is considered fasid due to being performed before its proper place.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a ruling whose effect is not immediately conclusive but appears later upon the occurrence of a condition or the passage of time.
إجزاء (ijza'): Validity or sufficiency; the act of fulfilling the obligation such that no repetition is needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what must a pilgrim do if he prayed Maghrib on the road before reaching Muzdalifah?
A) Nothing; the prayer is valid because he intended to combine.
B) He must repeat it before Fajr.
C) He must repeat it at Muzdalifah after Isha.
D) He must repeat it only if he passed Muzdalifah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority holds that praying Maghrib (and Isha) before reaching Muzdalifah is invalid, but the invalidity is suspended; the pilgrim must repeat it before Fajr to avoid the conclusive invalidity.

Standing at Muzdalifah: Wuquf, Time, Excuses, and Boundaries
Detailed explanation of wuquf at Muzdalifah, its sunnahs, time, and boundaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time, sunnahs, and conditions of wuquf at Muzdalifah and identify when the obligation is waived due to a valid excuse.

Core Idea
Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib from dawn to sunrise; the obligation is excused for the weak, ill, or those fearing crowds.

The wuquf at Muzdalifah after Fajr on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah is one of the wajibat of Hajj. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains its time, recommended acts, the excusing conditions, and the precise boundaries of the standing area, including the exclusion of Wadi Muhassir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that wuquf at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn, based on the text's statement 'قدمنا أنه واجب' (we have already explained that it is wajib).
This classification affects the consequence of omission: dam (sacrifice) required if left without excuse, not invalidation of Hajj.
2
Determine the time and sunnahs
Note that the time is from dawn (fajr) to sunrise. The sunnahs include facing qiblah, glorifying Allah, sending blessings, and supplicating at Jabal Qazah if possible.
The sunnahs are commendable but not obligatory; missing them incurs no penalty.
3
Recognize the excuse for dropping the wajib
The text states that the obligation falls due to an excuse: weakness, illness, or fear of crowd (including both men and women). The ruling is derived from Al-Hidayah and Al-Muhit.
This is a general principle: any wajib left due to a valid excuse incurs no penalty.
4
Note the excluded area
Batn Muhassir (Wadi Muhassir) is not part of Muzdalifah for standing; it is a valley between Mina and Muzdalifah. Standing there does not fulfill the wajib.
Analogous to Batn 'Arnah at Arafat, which is excluded from the standing area of Arafah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج/ باب الإحرام وقف على جبل قزح إن أمكنك وإلا فبقرب منه وهي موقف إلا بطن محسر ثم إلى منى قوله : (ثم قف مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً على النبي داعياً ربك بحاجتك وقف على جبل قزح إن أمكنك وإلا فبقرب منه بيان للسنة، فلو وقف قبل الصلاة أجزأه، ووقته من طلوع الفجر إلى طلوع الشمس وقدمنا أنه واجب. وصرح في الهداية بسقوطه للعذر بأن يكون به ضعف أو علة أو كانت امرأة تخاف الزحام لا شيء عليه، وسيأتي في الجنايات أن هذا لا يخص هذا الواجب بل كل واجب إذا تركه للعذر لا شيء عليه. ولم يقيد في المحيط خوف الزحام بالمرأة بل أطلقه فشمل الرجل لو مر قبل الوقت لخوفه لا شيء عليه، ولو مر بها من غير أن يقف جاز كالوقوف بعرفة، ولو مر في جزء من أجزاء المزدلفة جاز. كذا في المعراج واختلف في جبل قزح فقيل هو المشعر الحرام وقيل المشعر جميع المزدلفة. ولم يذكر البيتوتة بمزدلفة سنة لا شيء عليه لو تركها كما لو وقف بعد ما أفاض الإمام قبل وهي الشمس لأن البيتوتة شرعت للتأهب للوقوف ولم تشرع نسكاً قوله : (وهي موقف إلا بطن محسر) أي المزدلفة كلها موقف إلا وادي مُحسّر، وهو بضم الميم وفتح الحاء المهملة وكسر السين المهملة المشددة وبالراء، سمي بذلك لأن فيل أصحاب الفيل فيه أي عيي وكل. ووادي محسر موضع فاصل بين منى ومزدلفة ليس من واحدة منهما قال الأزرقي : إن وادي محسر خمسمائة ذراع وخمسة وأربعون ذراعاً، وأما مزدلفة فإنها كلها من الحرم سميت بذلك من التزلف والازدلاف وهو التقرب لأن الحجاج يتقربون منها وحدها ما بين وادي محسر ومأزمي عرفة ويدخل فيها جميع تلك الشعاب والجبال الداخلة في الحد المذكور. وظاهر كلام المصنف كغيره أن بطن محسر ليس مكان الوقوف كبطن عرنة في عرفات فلو وقف حسر
Book of Hajj / Chapter of Ihram: Stop at Jabal Qazah if you can, otherwise near it, and it is a standing place except Batn Muhassir, then to Mina. His statement: (Then stop magnifying, uttering tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings on the Prophet, supplicating your Lord with your need. Stop at Jabal Qazah if you can, otherwise near it.) This is an explanation of the sunnah. If he stopped before prayer, it suffices him. Its time is from dawn to sunrise, and we have already explained that it is wajib. It is clearly stated in Al-Hidayah that it falls due to an excuse: if he has weakness or illness, or if a woman fears the crowd, nothing is upon him. It will come in the chapter of violations that this is not specific to this obligation; rather every obligation that he leaves due to an excuse, nothing is upon him. In Al-Muhit, fear of the crowd was not restricted to women; rather it was absolute, so it includes a man. If he passed before the time due to fear, nothing is upon him. If he passed through it without stopping, it is valid like standing at Arafah. If he passed through a part of Muzdalifah, it is valid. This is in Al-Mi‘raj. There is a difference of opinion about Jabal Qazah: it is said that it is the Mash‘ar al-Haram, and it is said that the Mash‘ar is all of Muzdalifah. He did not mention staying overnight (baytutah) at Muzdalifah as sunnah; nothing is upon him if he leaves it, just as if he stopped after the imam departed before sunrise, because staying overnight is legislated for preparation for standing, not legislated as a ritual (nusk). His statement: (And it is a standing place except Batn Muhassir) meaning Muzdalifah is all a standing place except Wadi Muhassir, which is with dammah on the meem, fatha on the ha, kasra on the seen with shaddah, and ra. It was so named because the elephant of the Companions of the Elephant became exhausted and weak there. Wadi Muhassir is a separating place between Mina and Muzdalifah, not belonging to either. Al-Azraqi said: Wadi Muhassir is 545 cubits. As for Muzdalifah, it is all from the Haram; it was so named from tazalluf and izdilaf, which is drawing near, because the pilgrims draw near from it. It is the area between Wadi Muhassir and the two passes of Arafah, and it includes all those valleys and mountains within the mentioned boundary. The apparent statement of the author, like others, is that Batn Muhassir is not a place of standing, like Batn ‘Arnah at Arafat. So if he stands in Muhassir...
Source pages p. 600

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of standing at Muzdalifah (wuquf), which is a wajib act of Hajj. The sunnah actions include facing the qiblah, glorifying Allah, making talbiyah, sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him), and supplicating. The recommended place is Jabal Qazah (the Mount of Mercy), but if unable, anywhere in Muzdalifah suffices. The time for standing is from dawn (fajr) to sunrise. The obligation is waived for those with a valid excuse such as illness, weakness, or fear of the crowd. The text clarifies that the entire area of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Wadi Muhassir, which is a valley between Mina and Muzdalifah. This is analogous to Batn ‘Arnah at Arafat, which is not part of Arafah. Staying overnight (baytutah) at Muzdalifah is considered sunnah, not wajib; one who leaves it incurs no penalty. The commentator notes differing views on whether Jabal Qazah is the entire Mash‘ar al-Haram or just the mountain.

Key Terms
الواقوف (al-wuquf): Standing at a specified place during Hajj; at Muzdalifah, it is wajib after Fajr.
بيتوتة (baytutah): Spending the night at Muzdalifah, considered sunnah in Hanafi, not wajib.
بطن محسر (batn muhassir): A valley between Mina and Muzdalifah that is excluded from the standing area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the time for standing at Muzdalifah according to the Hanafi school?
A) From Maghrib to Isha
B) From Fajr to sunrise
C) From sunrise to noon
D) From noon to sunset

Key Takeaway
Wuquf at Muzdalifah is a wajib act of Hajj performed between dawn and sunrise, excused for those with valid obstacles, and the entire area except Wadi Muhassir is valid for standing.
