Standing at Muzdalifah (Wuquf) and Its Exceptions
Expansion on the obligatory standing at Muzdalifah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on standing at Muzdalifah, identify the valid standing place, and apply the exception of Batn Muhassir.

Core Idea
All of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir; standing is wajib but dropped for excuses.

The standing at Muzdalifah is a distinct wajib act in Hajj, separate from the rukn of Arafat. This lesson clarifies where exactly to stand, the time, and when the obligation lifts. We'll also explore the debated identity of Jabal Qazah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Determine from the text that standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, its time from dawn to sunrise, and that it is dropped for excuses like illness or fear of crowds.
The text references al-Hidayah for the excuse ruling.
2
Analyze the standing place
Understand that all of Muzdalifah is a valid standing place except Batn Muhassir. Note that this exclusion is like Batn Uranah in Arafat.
Batn Muhassir is the valley between Mina and Muzdalifah.
3
Examine the Jabal Qazah dispute
There are two views: some say Jabal Qazah is al-Mash'ar al-Haram, others say the entire Muzdalifah is al-Mash'ar. This does not affect the obligation.
The sunnah is to stand at the mountain if possible.
4
Understand consequences of omission
If one omits the standing without excuse, a dam (sacrifice) is owed. With excuse, no penalty. Merely passing through without stopping is permissible if one intends the standing at another spot.
The text compares to Arafat: passing through suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج/ باب الإحرام
وقف على جبل قزح إن أمكنك وإلا فبقرب منه وهي موقف إلا بطن محسر ثم إلى منى
قوله : (ثم قف مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً على النبي داعياً ربك بحاجتك وقف على جبل قزح إن أمكنك وإلا فبقرب منه بيان للسنة، فلو وقف قبل الصلاة أجزأه، ووقته من طلوع الفجر إلى طلوع الشمس وقدمنا أنه واجب. وصرح في الهداية بسقوطه للعذر بأن يكون به ضعف أو علة أو كانت امرأة تخاف الزحام لا شيء عليه، وسيأتي في الجنايات أن هذا لا يخص هذا الواجب بل كل واجب إذا تركه للعذر لا شيء عليه. ولم يقيد في المحيط خوف الزحام بالمرأة بل أطلقه فشمل الرجل لو مر قبل الوقت لخوفه لا شيء عليه، ولو مر بها من غير أن يقف جاز كالوقوف بعرفة، ولو مر في جزء من أجزاء المزدلفة جاز. كذا في المعراج واختلف في جبل قزح فقيل هو المشعر الحرام وقيل المشعر جميع المزدلفة. ولم يذكر البيتوتة بمزدلفة سنة لا شيء عليه لو تركها كما لو وقف بعد ما أفاض الإمام قبل وهي الشمس لأن البيتوتة شرعت للتأهب للوقوف ولم تشرع نسكاً قوله : (وهي موقف إلا بطن محسر) أي المزدلفة كلها موقف إلا وادي مُحسّر، وهو بضم الميم وفتح الحاء المهملة وكسر السين المهملة المشددة وبالراء، سمي بذلك لأن فيل أصحاب الفيل فيه أي عيي وكل. ووادي محسر موضع فاصل بين منى ومزدلفة ليس من واحدة منهما قال الأزرقي : إن وادي محسر خمسمائة ذراع وخمسة وأربعون ذراعاً، وأما مزدلفة فإنها كلها من الحرم سميت بذلك من التزلف والازدلاف وهو التقرب لأن الحجاج يتقربون منها وحدها ما بين وادي محسر ومأزمي عرفة ويدخل فيها جميع تلك الشعاب والجبال الداخلة في الحد المذكور. وظاهر كلام المصنف كغيره أن بطن محسر ليس مكان الوقوف كبطن عرنة في عرفات فلو وقف [في؟] حسر [؟] 
والمغرب في وقت العشاء قبل أن يأتي مزدلفة أو بعد ما جاوزها لم يجزه وعليه إعادتهما ما لم يطلع الفجر في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وزفر والحسن وقال أبو يوسف : يجزئه ولا يعيد وقد أساء لترك السنة، ولو لم يعد حتى طلع الفجر عادت إلى الجواز وسقط القضاء اتفاقاً إلا أنه يأثم لتركه الواجب . وعن أبي حنيفة : إذا ذهب نصف الليل سقطت الإعادة لذهاب وقت الاستحباب ا هـ . قوله : (وقف على جبل قزح الخ) كذا في الزيلعي والظاهر أنه يوجد في بعض النسخ المتن وإلا فالذي رأيته في بعضها وعليه كتب في النهر بدون هذه الزيادة قوله : (وهي سنة الخ) وللشافعي قولان: قول بالوجوب وقول بالنية حكاهما النووي في مناسكه ثم قال : ويتأكد الاعتناء بهذا المبيت سواء قلنا إنه واجب أو سنة فقد فعله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقد ذهب إمامان جليلان من أصحابنا إلى أن هذا المبيت ركن يصح الحج إلا به قاله أبو عبد الرحمن ابن بنت الشافعي وأبو بكر محمد بن اسحق بن خزيمة، أن يحرص على المبيت للخروج من الخلاف ا هـ . قوله : ( ومازمي عرفة) قال في شرح النوازل : المأزم المضيق بين جبلين والمراد عند الفقهاء الطريق بين الجبلين وهما جبلان بين عرفات ينبغي ومزدلفة .

ثم إلى منى بعد ما أسفر جداً فارم جمرة العقبة من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات كحصى الخذف وكبر فيهما فقط لا يجوز كما لوقف في منى، سواء قلنا إن عرنة ومحسراً من عرفة ومزدلفة أو لا. ووقع في البدائع : وأما مكانه يعني الوقوف بمزدلفة فجزء من أجزاء مزدلفة إلا أنه لا له أن ينزل في وادي محسر، ولو وقف به أجزأه مع الكراهة وذكر مثله في بطن عرنة. قال في فتح القدير: وما ذكره في البدائع غير مشهور من كلام الأصحاب بل الذي يقتضيه كلامهم عدم الإجزاء وهو الذي يقتضيه النظر لأنهما ليسا من مسمى المكانين والاستثناء منقطع قوله : (ثم إلى منى بعد ما أسفر جداً) أي ثم رح وفسر الإسفار بأن تدفع بحيث لم يبق إلى طلوع الشمس إلا مقدار ما يصلي ركعتين كما في المحيط. وفي الظهيرية : وينبغي أن يكثر من الذكر والصلاة عليه السلام والدعاء وهو ذاهب فإذا بلغ بطن محسر أسرع إن كان ماشياً وحرك دابته إن كان راكباً قدر رمية حجر لأنه عليه السلام فعل ذلك .
قوله: (فارم جمرة العقبة من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات كحصى الخذف) أي المكان المسمى بذلك. والجمار هي الصغار من الحجارة جمع جمرة وبها سموا المواضع التي ترمي جماراً وجمرات لما بينهما من الملابسة، وقيل لتجمع ما هنالك من الحصى من تجمر القوم إذا تجمعوا، وجمر شعره إذا جمعه على قفاه والخذف بالخاء والذال المعجمتين أن ترمي بحصاة أو نواة أو نحوها تأخذه بين سبابتيك، وقيل أن تضع طرف الإبهام على طرف السبابة وفعله من باب ضرب. كذا في المغرب وصحح الولوالجي القول الثاني لأنه أكثر إهانة للشيطان وهذا بيان للسنة، فلو رمي كيف أراد ،جاز، ولو رمى من فوق العقبة أجزأه وكان مخالفاً للسنة . قيد لأنه لو وضعها وضعاً لم يجز لترك الواجب والطرح رمي إلى قدميه فيكون مجزئاً إلا أنه مخالف للسنة ومقدار الرمي أن يكون بين الرامي وموضع السقوط خمسة أذرع. كذا في بالرمي
قوله : (أي المكان المسمى بذلك تفسير الجمرة العقبة قوله : (وقيل أن تضع طرف الإبهام الخ) قال في الشرنبلالية عليه مشى في الهداية فقال : وكيفية الرمي أن يضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه اليمنى ويستعين بالمسبحة أ.هـ. قال الكمال : وهذا التفسير يحتمل كلاً من تفسيرين قيل بهما : أحدهما يضع طرف إبهامه اليمنى على وسط السبابة ويضع الحصاة على ظهر الإبهام كأنه عاقد سبعين فيرميها، وعرف منه أن المسنون في كون الرمي باليد اليمنى والآخر أن يحلق سبابته ويضعها على مفصل إبهامه كأنه عاقد عشرة، وهذا في التمكن من الرمي به مع الزحمة والوهجة عسر، وقيل يأخذها بطرفي إبهامه وسبابته وهذا هو الأصح لأنه الأيسر المعتاد ا.هـ. وكذا نقل تصحيحه في السراج عن النهاية وهو الذي صححه الولوالجي أيضاً، وظاهر كلام المؤلف أن الثاني مما في المغرب هو هذا فما مشى تقدير عليه في الهداية غيره كما يدل عليه كلام الكمال وهو الظاهر خلافاً لما مر عن الشرنبلالية قوله : (ومقدار الرمي الخ) هذا تقدير أقل ما يكون بينه وبين المكان في المسنون. كذا
Book of Hajj / Chapter of Ihram. Stand at Jabal Qazah if possible, otherwise near it; it is a standing place except Batn Muhassir, then to Mina. His statement: (Then stand, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings upon the Prophet, supplicating to your Lord for your need; stand at Jabal Qazah if possible, otherwise near it) is an explanation of the sunnah. So if he stands before the prayer, it suffices him. Its time is from dawn until sunrise, and we have stated that it is obligatory. It is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah that it is dropped due to an excuse: if the person has weakness, illness, or if the woman fears crowding, nothing is upon him. And it will come in the chapter of violations that this is not specific to this obligation, rather every obligation if he leaves it due to an excuse, nothing is upon him. In al-Muhit, fear of crowding was not restricted to women, but rather made absolute, so it includes a man if he passes before the time due to fear, nothing is upon him. And if he passes through it without standing, it is permissible like the standing at Arafat. And if he passes through any part of Muzdalifah, it is permissible. Likewise in al-Mi'raj. And there is a difference of opinion about Jabal Qazah: it is said that it is al-Mash'ar al-Haram, and it is said that al-Mash'ar is all of Muzdalifah. He did not mention spending the night at Muzdalifah as a sunnah; nothing is upon him if he leaves it, just as if he stands after the imam has departed before sunrise, because spending the night is legislated for readiness for standing and is not legislated as a ritual. His statement: (And it is a standing place except Batn Muhassir) i.e. all of Muzdalifah is a standing place except the valley of Muhassir. It is with dammah on the meem, fathah on the haa, kasrah on the seen, and shaddah, and with raa. It is named so because the elephant of the people of the elephant became tired and exhausted there. And Wadi Muhassir is a separating place between Mina and Muzdalifah, not belonging to either. Al-Azraqi said: Wadi Muhassir is five hundred and forty-five cubits. As for Muzdalifah, it is all from the Haram; it is named from tazalluf and izdilaf, which is drawing near, because the pilgrims draw near from it. Its boundaries are between Wadi Muhassir and the two passes of Arafat, and it includes all those ravines and mountains within the mentioned boundary. The apparent meaning of the author's words, like others, is that Batn Muhassir is not a place for standing, like Batn Uranah in Arafat. So if he stands in [؟] Muhassir [؟] and Maghrib at the time of Isha before he comes to Muzdalifah or after he passes it, it does not suffice him, and he must repeat both unless dawn breaks, according to Abu Hanifah, Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Hasan. Abu Yusuf said: It suffices him, and he does not repeat, but he has done wrong by leaving the sunnah. If he does not repeat until dawn breaks, it returns to permissibility and the make-up is dropped by agreement, except that he sins for leaving the wajib. And from Abu Hanifah: if half the night passes, the make-up is dropped because the time of desirability has passed. End quote. His statement: (Stand at Jabal Qazah etc.) Likewise in al-Zayla'i, and apparently it is found in some copies of the text, otherwise what I saw in some of them and upon it is written in al-Nahr without this addition. His statement: (And it is sunnah etc.) For al-Shafi'i there are two opinions: one for obligation and one for desirability, narrated by al-Nawawi in his Manasik. Then he said: And attention to this night stay is emphasized, whether we say it is obligatory or sunnah, for the Messenger of Allah ﷺ did it, and two eminent imams from our companions held that this night stay is a pillar such that Hajj is not valid without it, as stated by Abu Abd al-Rahman Ibn Bint al-Shafi'i and Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Khuzaymah. So one should be keen on the night stay to exit from difference. End quote. His statement: (And the two passes of Arafat) He said in Sharh al-Nawazil: Al-Ma'zam is the narrow pass between two mountains, and what is meant by the jurists is the road between two mountains, and they are two mountains between Arafat and Muzdalifah. Then to Mina after it is very bright, then stone Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like the pebbles of khadhf, and say takbir with each, not permissible otherwise like standing at Mina. Whether we say that Uranah and Muhassir are part of Arafat and Muzdalifah or not. And it occurs in al-Bada'i: As for its place, meaning the standing at Muzdalifah, it is a part of the parts of Muzdalifah, except that he should not alight in Wadi Muhassir, and if he stands there, it suffices him with dislike. And the like is mentioned for Batn Uranah. He said in Fath al-Qadir: What al-Bada'i mentioned is not well-known from the statements of the companions; rather what is required by their statements is non-sufficiency, and that is what is required by consideration because they are not from the named places, and the exception is disjunctive. His statement: (Then to Mina after it is very bright) i.e. then depart, and he explained brightness as departing such that there remains only enough time to pray two rak'ahs before sunrise, as in al-Muhit. In al-Zahiriyyah: He should increase in remembrance, blessings upon the Prophet, and supplication while going. When he reaches Batn Muhassir, he should hurry if walking, and spur his mount if riding, for the distance of a stone's throw because he ﷺ did that. His statement: (Stone Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like the pebbles of khadhf) i.e. the place so named. Al-Jimar are small stones, plural of jamrah, and by them the places stoned are called jimar and jamarat due to the connection between them. And it is said that it is because of the gathering of the pebbles there from tajammur of the people when they gather. And jamar his hair if he gathered it at the nape. Al-Khadhf (with khaa and dhaal) is that you throw a pebble, date pit, or the like, taking it between your two index fingers. And it is said that you place the tip of the thumb on the tip of the index finger; its verb is from the pattern daraba. Likewise in al-Mughrib, and al-Walwaliji confirmed the second opinion because it is more humiliating for the devil. This is an explanation of the sunnah. So if he stones however he wishes, it is permissible. And if he stones from above the Aqabah, it suffices him but he is contradicting the sunnah. It is restricted because if he places it as a placement, it is not permissible due to leaving the wajib. Al-Tarh (throwing) is throwing to his feet, so it is sufficient but contrary to sunnah. The distance of stoning is that there should be five cubits between the thrower and the landing place. Likewise in... His statement: (i.e. the place so named) explanation of Jamrat al-Aqaba. His statement: (And it is said that you place the tip of the thumb etc.) He said in al-Sharnablaliyyah: Al-Hidayah proceeded upon it, saying: The manner of stoning is that he places the pebble on the back of his right thumb and assists with the index finger. End quote. Al-Kamal said: This interpretation bears both of the two interpretations that have been said: one is that he places the tip of his right thumb on the middle of the index finger and places the pebble on the back of the thumb as if he is making a knot of seventy, then throws it. And from it, it is understood that the sunnah is that the stoning is with the right hand. The other is that he loops his index finger and places it on the joint of his thumb as if he is making a knot of ten. And to be able to stone with this in crowded conditions and heat is difficult. And it is said that he takes it with the tips of his thumb and index finger, and this is the most correct because it is the easiest and customary. End quote. Likewise, its correction was transmitted in al-Siraj from al-Nihayah, and it is what al-Walwaliji also confirmed. And the apparent meaning of the author's words is that the second from al-Mughrib is this, and what al-Hidayah proceeded upon is different, as indicated by al-Kamal's words, and it is apparent contrary to what was mentioned from al-Sharnablaliyyah. His statement: (And the distance of stoning etc.) This is an estimation of the minimum between him and the place in the sunnah. End quote.
Source pages p. 600

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings related to the rites at Muzdalifah and the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the sunnah acts and the obligations, including the stance of the Hanafi school and differences with other imams. The commentary begins by explaining that standing at Jabal Qazah is a sunnah, and its time is from dawn to sunrise. If one has an excuse such as illness or fear of crowding, the obligation to stand is dropped. The place of standing is all of Muzdalifah except Batn Muhassir, which is a valley separating Muzdalifah from Mina. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the prayer of Maghrib and Isha: Abu Hanifah and Muhammad require repetition if not performed at Muzdalifah, while Abu Yusuf deems it sufficient. The night stay (baytutah) at Muzdalifah is considered a sunnah, not an obligation, and there is a Shafi'i opinion making it obligatory. The stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba is performed with seven small pebbles, thrown from the bottom of the valley. The sunnah method of throwing is explained in detail, with the preferred method being to hold the pebble with the tips of the thumb and index finger. The distance between the thrower and the landing place should be at least five cubits. The commentary emphasizes the importance of following the sunnah and the permissibility of doing otherwise while noting the departure from the ideal.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims stand after coming from Arafat; all of it is a standing place except Batn Muhassir.
بطن محسر (Batn Muhassir): A valley between Mina and Muzdalifah, not part of either; it is not a place for the standing (wuquf).
المشعر الحرام (al-Mash'ar al-Haram): A sacred site at Muzdalifah; some say it is Jabal Qazah, others say all of Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid excuse for omitting the standing at Muzdalifah according to the text?
A) Weakness or illness
B) Fear of crowding for a man
C) Fear of crowding for a woman
D) Forgetting the time

Key Takeaway
Standing at Muzdalifah is a wajib act performed between dawn and sunrise anywhere in the area except Batn Muhassir; valid excuses drop the obligation without penalty.

Timing of Departure from Muzdalifah to Mina
Explains the prescribed time to leave Muzdalifah for Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended time to leave Muzdalifah for Mina and identify the sunnah of hastening in the valley of Muhassir.

Core Idea
The sunnah is to depart after isfar (brightening) before sunrise, and to hasten in Muhassir in imitation of the Prophet.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the timing of the departure from Muzdalifah to Mina on the Day of Sacrifice. It clarifies that the recommended (sunnah) time is after the sky becomes very bright (isfar), defined as the period during which one could still pray two rak'ahs before sunrise. Additionally, when reaching the valley of Muhassir, one should hasten, following the Prophet's action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prescribed time
Find the phrase 'after it has become very bright' (asfar jiddan). The text defines isfar as the time when only two rak'ahs remain until sunrise.
2
Understand the legal ruling
This timing is a sunnah, not wajib, based on the Prophet's action. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's fi'l indicates sunnah.
3
Recognize recommended practices
Upon departing, increase dhikr, salawat, and supplication.
4
Identify the hastening in Muhassir
When reaching the valley of Muhassir, hasten (walk quickly or spur mount) for a stone's throw.
This is also sunnah based on the Prophet's action.
5
Note the proof
The text cites 'because he (peace be upon him) did that.' The dalil is the Prophetic practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إلى منى بعد ما أسفر جداً أي ثم رح وفسر الإسفار بأن تدفع بحيث لم يبق إلى طلوع الشمس إلا مقدار ما يصلي ركعتين كما في المحيط. وفي الظهيرية: وينبغي أن يكثر من الذكر والصلاة عليه السلام والدعاء وهو ذاهب فإذا بلغ بطن محسر أسرع إن كان ماشياً وحرك دابته إن كان راكباً قدر رمية حجر لأنه عليه السلام فعل ذلك.
Then to Mina after it has become very bright, that is, then depart. And the explanation of 'isfar' is that you depart such that there remains before sunrise only the amount to pray two rak'ahs, as in al-Muhit. And in al-Zahiriyyah: It is recommended to increase dhikr, salawat upon him (peace be upon him), and supplication while going. When he reaches the middle of Muhassir, he should hasten if walking, and spur his mount if riding, the distance of a stone's throw, because he (peace be upon him) did that.
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on when to depart from Muzdalifah to Mina on the Day of Sacrifice. It is a recommended act (sunnah) to leave after the sky becomes very bright, i.e., before sunrise but with enough time to pray two rak'ahs of the Fajr sunnah? Actually the text says 'asfar jiddan' meaning after dawn but not yet sunrise. The commentator defines 'isfar' as the time when only the duration of two rak'ahs remains until sunrise. Upon departing, one should engage in dhikr and salawat. When reaching the valley of Muhassir, one should hasten (walk quickly or spur the mount) for the length of a stone's throw, following the Prophet's action. This is a sunnah act; if one does not hasten, no compensation is required.

Key Terms
أسفر (asfara): The time when the sky becomes very bright after dawn but before sunrise; specifically, leaving enough time to pray two rak'ahs before sunrise.
محسر (Muhassir): A valley between Muzdalifah and Mina where one should hasten while passing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the prescribed time to leave Muzdalifah for Mina on the Day of Sacrifice according to the Hanafi school?
A) After midnight
B) After the sky becomes very bright (isfar)
C) Exactly at sunrise
D) After sunset

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is to depart Muzdalifah for Mina after isfar (brightening) before sunrise, and to hasten in the valley of Muhassir.

Stoning Jamarat al-Aqaba: Place, Pebbles, and Method
Ruling on the place, pebbles, and method of stoning Jamarat al-Aqaba with digression on valley boundaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunna method of stoning Jamarat al-Aqaba and identify which variations are valid but against the sunna.

Core Idea
Stoning Jamarat al-Aqaba is wajib; the sunna is from the valley with seven small pebbles, but any throw that hits the pillar suffices.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the fiqh of stoning the largest jamrah. It clarifies that the sunna method includes throwing from the valley bottom, using seven pebbles the size of chickpeas, with takbir each time, but valid alternatives exist. The text also resolves a dispute about standing in adjacent valleys.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its wajib nature
Recognise that stoning Jamarat al-Aqaba is a wajib act in Hajj; its omission requires a dam. The text describes the sunna method.
Wajib here means obligatory, not a pillar (rukn).
2
Distinguish the sunna from the validity conditions
Separate what is sunna (location, size, method of holding) from what is minimally required for validity (throwing an object that hits the pillar area, using seven pebbles).
The text explicitly says 'if he throws however he wishes, it is permissible'.
3
Analyse the valley dispute
Examine the discussion about Muhassir and 'Arana valleys. The Hanafi relied-upon position is that standing there does not suffice for Muzdalifah.
This is an intra-madhhab tarjih against al-Bada'i.
4
Understand the method of khadhf
Learn the preferred sunna of holding the pebble: between thumb and index finger, throwing with force to humiliate Satan.
Al-Walwaliji declared this method better.
5
Apply the ruling to common scenarios
Consider cases like throwing from above, using larger stones, or failing to say takbir. Determine validity and degree of compliance with sunna.
The fatwa is that such actions are valid but khilaf al-awla.

فارم جمرة العقبة من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات كحصى الخذف وكبر فيهما فقط لا يجوز كما لوقف في منى، سواء قلنا إن عرنة ومحسراً من عرفة ومزدلفة أو لا. ووقع في البدائع : وأما مكانه يعني الوقوف بمزدلفة فجزء من أجزاء مزدلفة إلا أنه لا له أن ينزل في وادي محسر، ولو وقف به أجزأه مع الكراهة وذكر مثله في بطن عرنة. قال في فتح القدير: وما ذكره في البدائع غير مشهور من كلام الأصحاب بل الذي يقتضيه كلامهم عدم الإجزاء وهو الذي يقتضيه النظر لأنهما ليسا من مسمى المكانين والاستثناء منقطع. قوله : (فارم جمرة العقبة من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات كحصى الخذف) أي المكان المسمى بذلك. والجمار هي الصغار من الحجارة جمع جمرة وبها سموا المواضع التي ترمي جماراً وجمرات لما بينهما من الملابسة، وقيل لتجمع ما هنالك من الحصى من تجمر القوم إذا تجمعوا، وجمر شعره إذا جمعه على قفاه والخذف بالخاء والذال المعجمتين أن ترمي بحصاة أو نواة أو نحوها تأخذه بين سبابتيك، وقيل أن تضع طرف الإبهام على طرف السبابة وفعله من باب ضرب. كذا في المغرب وصحح الولوالجي القول الثاني لأنه أكثر إهانة للشيطان وهذا بيان للسنة، فلو رمي كيف أراد جاز، ولو رمى من فوق العقبة أجزأه وكان مخالفاً للسنة . قيد لأنه لو وضعها وضعاً لم يجز لترك الواجب والطرح رمي إلى قدميه فيكون مجزئاً إلا أنه مخالف للسنة.
Then stone Jamarat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf, and say takbir with each throw. It is not permissible to stand in Mina? Whether we say that 'Arana and Muhassir are part of 'Arafah and Muzdalifah or not. And it occurs in al-Bada'i': 'As for its place, meaning the standing at Muzdalifah, it is a part of Muzdalifah except that he may not descend into the valley of Muhassir; if he stands there, it suffices with dislike.' Similar is mentioned for the valley of 'Arana. Al-Fath al-Qadir said: What al-Bada'i' mentioned is not well-known from the statements of the companions; rather, their statements indicate non-sufficiency, and that is what consideration requires, because these valleys are not part of the named places, and the exception is disjoined. His statement: 'Stone Jamarat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf' means the place called by that name. Al-jimar are small stones, plural of jumrah; by them the places where one throws are named jimar and jumarat because of the connection. It is also said [they are named] because of the gathering of pebbles there, from tajammara 'the people gathered', and jamara 'he gathered his hair on his nape'. Khadhf (with khā' and dhāl) is to throw a pebble or a pit or the like, taking it between your two index fingers. It is also said to place the tip of the thumb on the tip of the index finger, its verb from bābi ḍaraba. Thus in al-Mughrib, and al-Walwaliji declared the second saying correct because it is more humiliating for Satan, and this is an explanation of the sunna. If he throws however he wishes, it is permissible. If he throws from above the 'Aqaba, it suffices but is against the sunna. Restriction because if he places it (places the pebble) without throwing, it is not valid due to leaving the obligatory; but 'throwing' includes dropping to his feet, so it would be sufficient but against the sunna.
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage details the ruling of stoning Jamarat al-Aqaba. The sunna is to throw from the bottom of the valley (batin al-wadi) facing the jamrah, using seven small pebbles the size of a chickpea (khas al-khadhf). One should say takbir with each throw. The commentator quotes a discussion from al-Bada'i' about whether one can descend into Muhassir ('Arana is a similar valley near 'Arafah). The relied-upon Hanafi position is that stoning in those valleys does not suffice because they are outside the designated area. The pebbles should be small stones. The method of holding the pebble: the preferred sunna is to place the thumb tip on the tip of the index finger (like counting one) and throw with the right hand, but any throwing method is valid (throws from above or with other hand suffices, but is against sunna). If one simply places the pebble on the pillar, it does not count because throwing is required.

Key Terms
الخذف (al-khadhf): Throwing a small pebble between the index fingers or with thumb and index; also the size of pebbles like chickpeas.
جمرة العقبة (Jamarat al-Aqaba): The large pillar nearest to Mina, stoned on the Day of Sacrifice and the following days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Valid, because the pebble is on the pillar
B) Invalid, because throwing (ramy) is required
C) Valid but disliked
D) Requires repeating after throwing

Key Takeaway
Stoning Jamarat al-Aqaba is a wajib act; the sunna method is from the valley with seven small pebbles, but any throw that hits the pillar suffices.

Minimum Distance and When a Pebble Hits an Object during Stoning
Ruling on distance and object-hitting scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunna distance for throwing and apply the ruling when a pebble hits a person or object before reaching the jamrah.

Core Idea
A pebble that sticks to a person requires repetition; one that falls off and reaches the target suffices.

Stoning the jamarat is a wajib rite of Hajj with specific technical details. This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the recommended throwing distance and the critical distinction between a pebble that becomes stuck on an object and one that continues into the basin after contact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunna distance
The text states the measure is 5 cubits between thrower and fall place. This is a sunna, not a wajib condition. If the pebble lands 'near' (customarily up to 3 cubits), it still suffices.
Some scholars define near as a cubit; others leave it to custom.
2
Understand the target condition
The pebble must reach the area around the jamrah (the basin). Falling directly on the pillar is not required; landing near it excusably is sufficient.
3
Distinguish two hit-object scenarios
If the pebble hits a person or object and sticks there, the throw is invalid and must be repeated. If it hits and then falls off in its trajectory to the target, it suffices.
The key is whether the pebble 'falls off' and continues naturally.
4
Apply the rule to the marker pole
If the pebble hits the marker pole (shakhs) which is part of the structure, it suffices because it is like reaching the target. But if it lands on the dome and does not fall off, it does not suffice due to not reaching the ground.
The pole indicates the location; hitting it counts as reaching the area.
5
Note the precaution for doubt
If unsure whether the pebble fell in the target by itself or due to movement of what it hit, or if doubting it fell in the proper place, the precaution is to repeat.
This is based on the principle: in acts of worship, doubt is resolved by precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومقدار الرمي أن يكون بين الرامي وموضع السقوط خمسة أذرع. كذا في الهداية. وفي الظهيرية: يجب أن يكون بينهما هذا القدر فلو رماها فوقعت قريباً من الجمرة يكفيه، ولو وقعت بعيداً لم يجزه لأنه لم يعرف قربة إلا في مكان مخصوص والقريب عفو . ولو وقعت الحصاة على ظهر رجل أو على محمل وثبتت عليه كان عليه إعادتها، وإذا سقطت عن المحمل أو عن ظهر الرجل في سننها ذلك أجزأه . وأشار بقوله «كحصى الخذف» إلى أنه لو رمي بسبع حصيات جملة واحدة فإنه يكون عن واحدة لأن المنصوص عليه تفرق الأفعال والتقييد بالسبع لمنع النقص لا لمنع الزيادة فإنه لو رماها بأكثر من السبع لم يضره. والتقييد في الفتح قوله : (فلو رماها فوقعت قريباً من الجمرة الخ) أي قدر ذراع ونحوه، ومنهم من لم يقدره اعتباراً للقرب عرفاً وضده البعد وتمامه في الفتح. وقال في اللباب: وقدر القريب بثلاثة أذرع والبعيد بما فوقها وقيل القريب ما دون الثلاثة قوله : ولو وقعت الحصاة على ظهر رجل الخ) فلو وقعت على الشاخص أي أطراف الميل الذي هو علامة للجمرة أجزأه ولو على قبة الشاخص ولم تنزل عنه فالظاهر أنه لا يجزئه للعبد (لباب) وفيه : وإن لم يدر أنها وقعت في المرمى بنفسها أو بنفض من وقعت عليه وتحريكه ففيه اختلاف والاحتياط يعيده وكذا لو رمى وشك في وقوعها موقعها فالأحوط أن يعيد.
The measure of throwing is that between the thrower and the place of fall be five cubits. Thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Zahiriyyah: This amount must be between them. If he throws and it falls near the jamrah, it suffices; if it falls far, it does not suffice because he did not achieve proximity except in a specific place, and nearness is excusable. If the pebble falls on the back of a man or on a camel litter and sticks there, he must repeat it; but if it falls off the litter or off the man's back in its trajectory, it suffices. And his saying 'like pebbles of khadhf' indicates that if he throws seven pebbles all at once, it counts as one, because the prescribed requirement is separation of actions, and the restriction to seven is to prevent deficiency, not to prevent increase; if he throws more than seven, it does not harm him. And the restriction in al-Fath: his saying: 'If he throws and it falls near the jamrah' means about a cubit or so. Some do not specify an amount, considering 'near' according to custom and its opposite is distant; its completion is in al-Fath. And in al-Lubab: He estimated 'near' as three cubits and 'far' as beyond that; and it is said 'near' is less than three. His saying: 'If the pebble falls on the back of a man, etc.' So if it falls on the marker, i.e., the ends of the pole that is the sign of the jamrah, it suffices; if on the dome of the marker and does not fall off, apparently it does not suffice due to distance. (al-Lubab) And in it: If he does not know if it fell in the target by itself or by the shaking of the one upon whom it fell, there is difference of opinion, and the precaution is to repeat it. Similarly, if he throws and doubts whether it fell in its place, the precaution is to repeat.
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage covers two separate but connected rulings: (1) the minimum distance between the thrower and the pillar, and (2) what happens if the pebble hits a person or object before reaching the target. The minimum sunna distance is five cubits (about 2.3 meters); if the pebble lands closer than that, it is still valid if it falls 'near' the jamrah. Nearness is customarily defined as about one cubit, or three cubits according to some. If the pebble sticks to a person or animal, the throw must be repeated. If it falls off and continues to the target, it suffices. Similarly, if it hits the marker pole (shakhs) it suffices, but if it lands on top of the dome and does not fall, it does not suffice because it did not reach the ground near the pillar. If there is doubt, the precaution is to repeat the throw.

Key Terms
قريب (qarib): Near the pillar; customarily up to three cubits away.
الشاخص (al-shakhs): The marker pole or column that indicates the jamrah's location.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Give dam (expiation)
D) Repeat all throws for that jamrah

Key Takeaway
The pebble must reach the jamrah area; if it sticks to an object en route, the throw is invalid and must be repeated.

Throwing Multiple Pebbles at Once in Stoning
Ruling on combining throws and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why throwing all seven pebbles at once only counts as one throw in the Hanafi school, and evaluate the minority view that distinguishes based on where the pebbles land.

Core Idea
Seven pebbles at once = only one valid throw — separation of actions is required.

When performing the stoning ritual (ramy) during Hajj, the pilgrim must throw seven pebbles sequentially. But what if a pilgrim throws all seven in a single handful? This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position, contrasting it with a minority Hanafi view and the positions of other schools. Understanding this ruling helps you grasp the principle of tafarruq al-af'al (separation of actions) that governs the validity of the stoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
Recognise that the ruling concerns throwing multiple pebbles at the jamarat in one go, and that the text specifies 'seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf' as the baseline for separation.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that it counts only as one throw because the required separation of actions is violated. The phrase 'like pebbles of khadhf' implies sequential throwing.
The restriction to seven is to prevent deficiency, not to permit accumulation.
3
Examine the minority Hanafi view
According to al-Karmani, if the pebbles scatter and land on different jamarat, it may be valid. But the famous position rejects this distinction.
This is a minority view not adopted for fatwa.
4
Compare with other schools
Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad agree that it counts only as one throw, because the command is seven separate throws.
Thus Hanafi position aligns with the majority of schools.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a pilgrim at Mina throws all seven at once, he must re-throw six pebbles. If he does not, his stoning is incomplete and he may owe a dam.
This is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And his saying 'like pebbles of khadhf' indicates that if he throws seven pebbles all at once, it counts as only one, because the prescribed requirement is separation of actions, and the restriction to seven is to prevent deficiency, not to prevent increase; if he throws more than seven, it does not harm him. And the restriction in al-Fath: his saying: 'If he throws and it falls near the jamrah, etc.' meaning about a cubit or so. Some do not specify an amount, considering 'near' according to custom and its opposite is distant; its completion is in al-Fath. And in al-Lubab: He estimated 'near' as three cubits and 'far' as beyond that; and it is said 'near' is less than three. His saying: 'If the pebble falls on the back of a man, etc.' So if it falls on the marker, i.e., the ends of the pole that is the sign of the jamrah, it suffices; if on the dome of the marker and does not fall off, apparently it does not suffice due to distance. Similarly, if he throws and doubts whether it fell in its place, the precaution is to repeat. His saying: (If he throws seven pebbles all at once, etc.) And in al-Karmani: If they fall separately on the places of the jamarat, it is permissible, just as if one combines the strokes of hadd with a single blow? but if they fall on one place, it is not permissible. Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad said: It does not suffice except for one pebble, however it occurs, because he is commanded to throw seven times. Commentary
This passage addresses the rule when a pilgrim throws all seven pebbles in one go. The Hanafi position, based on the phrase 'kahas al-khadhf' (like pebbles of khadhf) which implies separate throws, is that it counts as only one throw, and the other six are invalid. The text mentions an alternative view from al-Karmani: if the pebbles scatter and fall on different jamarat (the three pillars?), it may be valid. But the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school (as stated in al-Lubab al-Kabir) is that it does not suffice for all seven, only one. The three other imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) also hold that it only counts as one throw because the command is to throw seven separate times. Thus the Hanafi position aligns with the majority. The text also notes a dispute among Hanafis: some later scholars allowed it if the pebbles fall in different places, but the famous position is absolute non-permissibility. The commentator advises the reader to examine the full discussion.

Key Terms
تفرق الأفعال (tafarruq al-af'al): The requirement that each throw be a separate action; not combining them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Throwing all seven pebbles at once only counts as one throw; the pilgrim must re-throw the remaining six separately, as the principle of tafarruq al-af'al (separation of actions) is binding.

Valid and Invalid Methods of Stoning (Ramy) in Hajj
Rulings on the method of stoning and proxy stoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid stoning and identify which methods are invalid and which are acceptable for the sick and proxies.

Core Idea
Stoning must be done by hand; using a bow or foot invalidates the throw, but proxy stoning is allowed when necessary.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rulings of stoning the jamarat. It clarifies the essential method: the pebble must be thrown by hand. Alternative methods like using a bow or kicking are invalid. For those unable to throw due to illness, the pebble is placed in their hand, or they can appoint a proxy. The text also addresses the case of throwing two pebbles simultaneously for oneself and another, which is permissible but disliked. Understanding these rulings ensures that the pilgrim performs this wajib act correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its essential method
Stoning is an act of worship; the prescribed method is throwing with the hand. The passage explicitly states that using a bow or foot is not valid.
The Arabic term 'ramy' inherently implies hand-throwing.
2
Recognize invalid methods
Using a bow, slingshot, or the foot does not constitute valid ramy. The text mentions 'al-ramy bi al-qaws' and 'al-ramy bi al-rijl' as invalid.
3
Understand concessions for the sick and proxy
For a sick or unconscious person, the pebble is placed in their hand to throw. If that is not possible, a proxy may throw on their behalf by command, but the sick person throwing directly is better.
Proxy stoning is valid but the first choice is direct.
4
Note the ruling on simultaneous throws
Throwing two pebbles at once, one for oneself and one for another, is permissible but disliked. It is better to throw separately, starting with oneself.
This shows the importance of sequence and avoiding confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي حاشية المدني عن المرشدي: ولا يجزئ الرمي بالقوس ونحوه ولا الرمي بالرجل، ومن كان مريضاً أو مغمى عليه توضع الحصاة في يده ويرمي بها، وإن رمى عنه غيره بأمره أجزأه والأول أفضل. وفي اللباب ولو رمى بحصاتين إحداهما عن نفسه والأخرى عن غيره جاز ويكره، والأولى أن يرمي أولاً عن نفسه ثم عن غيره قوله : ( فإنه لو رماها بأكثر من السبع لم يضره) قال في اللباب : ولو رمى أكثر من سبع يكره. وقال شارحه : أي إذا رماه عن قصد، وأما إذا شك في السابع ورماه وتبين أنه الثامن فإنه لا يضره ذلك. هذا وقد ناقضه في الكبير بقوله : ولو رمى بأكثر من السبع لا يضره ا هـ . أقول : ما ذكره في المنسك الكبير هو ما ذكره المؤلف هنا ولعله محمول على غير القصد فلا تناقض إذ لا شك أن السبع هو المسنون فالزيادة عليها مخالفة للسنة فتكره لو كانت مقصودة وإلا فلا. وفي حاشية المدني قال الشيخ عز الدين بن جماعة في مناسكه الكبرى قالوا : لو زاد الرمي على السبع هل يندب أو يكره ؟ فقال بعضهم : إنه لا تكره الزيادة لأن رمیه طاعة، وقال بعضهم بل تكره لأنه خلاف السنة. هكذا نقل الخلاف ا هـ . وقال شمس الأئمة: لو زاد على سبع حصيات لا أجر له وينبغي أن يكره. قال القاضي عيد: وينبغي أن يكون هذا هو المذهب، ويكره رمي الجمرتين كذلك في هذا اليوم بالطريق الأولى لأنه بدعة ولم يفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام وربما اتخذها الجهال نسكاً ا هـ قوله : (وإلا فيجوز الرمي
And in the marginalia of al-Madani from al-Murshidi: Stoning with a bow and the like is not valid, nor is stoning with the foot. If someone is sick or unconscious, the pebble is placed in his hand and he throws with it. If someone else throws on his behalf by his command, it suffices, but the first is better. And in al-Lubab: If he throws two pebbles, one for himself and the other for someone else, it is permissible but disliked; it is better to throw first for himself then for the other. His saying: 'If he throws more than seven, it does not harm him.' Al-Lubab said: If he throws more than seven, it is disliked. Its commentator said: i.e., if he throws intentionally. But if he doubted about the seventh and threw again and it turned out to be the eighth, it does not harm him. This has been contradicted in al-Kabir by his saying: 'If he throws more than seven, it does not harm him.' I say: What al-Mansak al-Kabir mentioned is what the author mentioned here, and perhaps it is interpreted as unintentional, so there is no contradiction. For indeed, seven is the sunna, so increasing upon it is against the sunna and is disliked if intentional, otherwise not. And in the marginalia of al-Madani: Shaykh 'Izz al-Din ibn Jama'ah said in his Manasik al-Kubra: They said: If one increases stoning beyond seven, is it recommended or disliked? Some said it is not disliked because his throwing is obedience; some said it is disliked because it contradicts the sunna. Thus the difference is transmitted. And Shams al-A'imma said: If he increases beyond seven pebbles, he has no reward, and it ought to be disliked. Al-Qadi 'Id said: This should be the madhhab, and it is disliked to stone the two jamarat likewise on this day by primary analogy, because it is an innovation and the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not do it, and perhaps the ignorant take it as a ritual. His saying: (Otherwise, stoning is permissible...
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage collects several rulings related to the manner of stoning. First, stoning using a bow or catapult, or with the foot, is not valid because it does not constitute 'ramy' (throwing by hand) as prescribed. For a sick or unconscious person, his hand can be used to throw; proxy stoning upon instruction is valid but the person himself throwing is better. Throwing two pebbles at once (one for oneself, one for another) is permissible but disliked; it is better to separate them. Regarding throwing more than seven pebbles: the sunna is exactly seven. Adding more intentionally is disliked (makruh tanzihi). If one unintentionally throws an extra pebble (e.g., due to doubt), it does not harm. Shams al-A'imma and Qadi 'Id confirm that extra pebbles are disliked and have no reward. Some earlier scholars considered it not disliked, but the relied-upon position is karaha (dislike). The passage ends mid-sentence indicating a continuation of the ruling on permissibility of stoning in certain circumstances.

Key Terms
الرمي بالقوس (al-ramy bi al-qaws): Throwing a pebble using a bow or slingshot; not valid because it is not the prescribed method of throwing by hand.
الرمي بالرجل (al-ramy bi al-rijl): Kicking the pebble with the foot; invalid as it is not throwing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred method for a sick person who can throw with assistance?
A) Appoint a proxy immediately
B) Have the pebble placed in his hand and throw
C) Throw with a bow
D) Skip stoning

Key Takeaway
Stoning must be performed by hand-throwing; proxy stoning is allowed only when the pilgrim cannot throw directly, and simultaneous throws for self and other are valid but disliked.

Ruling on Throwing More Than Seven Pebbles
Ruling on throwing more than seven pebbles: intentional vs. unintentional, and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on throwing more than seven pebbles intentionally and explain the reasons for the dislike.

Core Idea
Throwing more than seven pebbles intentionally is disliked (makruh tanzihi) because it violates the sunna, even though the act of throwing is obedience.

The second part of the passage deals with the number of pebbles. The sunna is exactly seven for each jamarat. Adding more intentionally is contrary to the sunna and is disliked. The text records a difference of opinion: some earlier scholars considered it not disliked, but the relied-upon position (endorsed by Shams al-A'imma and Qadi 'Id) is that it is makruh. Unintentional additions due to doubt are excused. This lesson explores the reasoning and the intra-Hanafi debate.

Guided Path
1
Recognize that the sunna is seven pebbles
The passage assumes that the prescribed number is seven. The text states 'السبع هو المسنون' (seven is the sunna).
This is the baseline.
2
Distinguish intentional vs. unintentional increase
If the pilgrim intentionally adds more, it is disliked. If unintentional (e.g., due to doubt), it does not harm. The commentator clarifies: 'إذا رماه عن قصد' (if he throws intentionally) then disliked.
3
Follow the intra-Hanafi debate
The text mentions that al-Mansak al-Kabir seemed to say 'does not harm', but this is interpreted as referring to unintentional increase. Some earlier scholars considered increase not disliked, but the later relied-upon view is karaha.
The contradiction is resolved by intention.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
Shams al-A'imma and Qadi 'Id affirm that increasing beyond seven intentionally is disliked and has no reward. This is the operative position for fatwa.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي حاشية المدني عن المرشدي: ولا يجزئ الرمي بالقوس ونحوه ولا الرمي بالرجل، ومن كان مريضاً أو مغمى عليه توضع الحصاة في يده ويرمي بها، وإن رمى عنه غيره بأمره أجزأه والأول أفضل. وفي اللباب ولو رمى بحصاتين إحداهما عن نفسه والأخرى عن غيره جاز ويكره، والأولى أن يرمي أولاً عن نفسه ثم عن غيره قوله : ( فإنه لو رماها بأكثر من السبع لم يضره) قال في اللباب : ولو رمى أكثر من سبع يكره. وقال شارحه : أي إذا رماه عن قصد، وأما إذا شك في السابع ورماه وتبين أنه الثامن فإنه لا يضره ذلك. هذا وقد ناقضه في الكبير بقوله : ولو رمى بأكثر من السبع لا يضره ا هـ . أقول : ما ذكره في المنسك الكبير هو ما ذكره المؤلف هنا ولعله محمول على غير القصد فلا تناقض إذ لا شك أن السبع هو المسنون فالزيادة عليها مخالفة للسنة فتكره لو كانت مقصودة وإلا فلا. وفي حاشية المدني قال الشيخ عز الدين بن جماعة في مناسكه الكبرى قالوا : لو زاد الرمي على السبع هل يندب أو يكره ؟ فقال بعضهم : إنه لا تكره الزيادة لأن رمیه طاعة، وقال بعضهم بل تكره لأنه خلاف السنة. هكذا نقل الخلاف ا هـ . وقال شمس الأئمة: لو زاد على سبع حصيات لا أجر له وينبغي أن يكره. قال القاضي عيد: وينبغي أن يكون هذا هو المذهب، ويكره رمي الجمرتين كذلك في هذا اليوم بالطريق الأولى لأنه بدعة ولم يفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام وربما اتخذها الجهال نسكاً ا هـ قوله : (وإلا فيجوز الرمي

The Stone Must Land Close to the Jamrah: Conditions and Invalidators
Ruling on proximity and obstacles in stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a valid stoning throw and apply them to scenarios where the stone hits an obstacle.

Core Idea
A stoning throw is valid only if the stone lands close to the jamrah; if it sticks to a person or saddle, the throw must be repeated.

This passage from al-Hidayah and its commentaries clarifies the requirements for the stoning ritual at the jamrah. You will learn the distance criterion (close vs. far) and the effect of an obstacle (person or saddle) on the stone's landing. The discussion includes the Hanafi reliance on custom (urf) for defining closeness and the recommended caution in cases of doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The stone must land close to the jamrah. If it lands far away, the throw does not suffice because closeness is only known at the designated place.
The principle: the act of worship has a specific location.
2
Define 'close' in Hanafi fiqh
Closeness is defined by custom (urf). Some Hanafi scholars suggest one cubit or three cubits, but the relied-upon position is custom.
Intra-Hanafi difference: the exact measurement is not fixed.
3
Analyze the obstacle case
If the stone falls on the back of a man or on a camel saddle and sticks there, the throw must be repeated because the stone has not reached the target. If it falls off into the stoning area, it suffices.
Key distinction: the stone must actually land at the jamrah location.
4
Consider the marker (shakhis)
Hitting the marker (the mile) that indicates the jamrah suffices. However, if the stone lands on the dome of the marker and stays there, it does not suffice.
The marker is considered part of the jamrah area.
5
Handle doubt
If unsure whether the stone reached the target due to external factors (e.g., the person shaking), the cautious approach is to repeat the throw. Similarly, if doubts about the stone hitting the spot, repeating is recommended.
The principle of ihtiyat (caution) in acts of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الهداية. وفي الظهيرية: يجب أن يكون بينهما هذا القدر فلو رماها فوقعت قريباً من الجمرة يكفيه، ولو وقعت بعيداً لم يجزه لأنه لم يعرف قربة إلا في مكان مخصوص والقريب عفو . ولو وقعت الحصاة على ظهر رجل أو على محمل وثبتت عليه كان عليه إعادتها، وإذا سقطت عن المحمل أو عن ظهر الرجل في سننها ذلك أجزأه . في الفتح قوله : (فلو رماها فوقعت قريباً من الجمرة الخ) أي قدر ذراع ونحوه، ومنهم من لم يقدره اعتباراً للقرب عرفاً وضده البعد وتمامه في الفتح. وقال في اللباب: وقدر القريب بثلاثة أذرع والبعيد بما فوقها وقيل القريب ما دون الثلاثة قوله : ولو وقعت الحصاة على ظهر رجل الخ) فلو وقعت على الشاخص أي أطراف الميل الذي هو علامة للجمرة أجزأه ولو على قبة الشاخص ولم تنزل عنه فالظاهر أنه لا يجزئه للعبد (لباب) وفيه : وإن لم يدر أنها وقعت في المرمى بنفسها أو بنفض من وقعت عليه وتحريكه ففيه اختلاف والاحتياط يعيده وكذا لو رمى وشك في وقوعها موقعها فالأحوط أن يعيد
Al-Hidaya: And in al-Zahiriyya: There must be this distance between them. If he throws and it lands close to the jamrah, it suffices; if it lands far away, it does not suffice because closeness is not known except in a specific place, and nearness is pardoned. If the stone falls on the back of a man or on a camel saddle and sticks, he must repeat it; if it falls off the saddle or the man's back into its direction, it suffices. In al-Fath: His saying: 'If he throws and it falls close to the jamrah' etc., meaning about a cubit or so; some did not specify it, considering closeness by custom and its opposite distance. And it is complete in al-Fath. And it is said in al-Lubab: The close is estimated at three cubits, and the far as more than that; it is said the close is less than three. His saying: 'And if the stone falls on the back of a man' etc.: if it falls on the marker, i.e., the ends of the mile that is a sign of the jamrah, it suffices; if on the dome of the marker and has not fallen off, apparently it does not suffice due to the [؟]. In al-Lubab: If he does not know whether it fell in the stoning area by itself or by shaking of the one it fell on, there is disagreement; caution is to repeat it. Likewise, if he throws and doubts its hitting the spot, the best precaution is to repeat.
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with accompanying proof and commentary on the conditions of the stone's landing. The initial ruling from al-Hidaya states that the stone must land close to the jamrah; if it lands far away, it does not suffice because the act of worship is only fulfilled in the designated area. 'Close' is pardoned (عفو) by custom. The commentary from al-Fath and al-Lubab specifies distances: one cubit or three cubits, with some relying on custom. The second issue concerns a stone landing on a person or saddle: if it sticks there, the throw must be repeated because the stone has not reached the target; if it falls off into the stoning area, it suffices. The discussion extends to markers and domes, with the ruling that hitting a marker suffices, but landing on a dome without falling requires repetition. The passage concludes with a note on doubt: if unsure whether the stone reached the target due to external shaking, the cautious approach is to repeat the throw. This ruling is based on the principle that the act of stoning is a specific ritual whose validity depends on the stone hitting the designated place.

Key Terms
قريب (qarib): Close to the jamrah, defined by custom or estimated as a cubit or three cubits.
الشاخص (al-shakhis): The marker (mile) indicating the jamrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim throws a stone and it hits a person's back and sticks there, what is the ruling?
A) The throw is valid because the stone reached the jamrah area.
B) The throw is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The throw is valid if the person is in the stoning area.
D) It depends on whether the stone fell off.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a stoning throw depends on the stone landing close to the jamrah (by custom) and not being stuck on an obstacle; in doubt, repeat to be safe.
